401 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Savchuk v. Rush


No. 45556


Supreme Court of Minnesota


311 Minn. 480; 245 N.W.2d 624; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1841



September 10, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Vacated and Remanded, 433 U.S. 902, 97 S. Ct. 2964, 53 L. ed. 2d 1086 (1977).


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the Hennepin County District Court for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff as a passenger in an automobile driven by defendant. A garnishment summons was served upon State Farm Mutual Automobile Insurance Company, defendant's insurer. The court, Douglas K. Amdahl, Judge, granted plaintiff's motion to file a supplemental complaint and denied a motion by defendant to dismiss the action, and defendant and the garnishee appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee passenger sued appellant driver for personal injuries allegedly sustained in a single-car accident. A garnishment summons was served upon appellant garnishee, the driver's insurer. The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), granted the passenger's motion to file a supplemental complaint and denied appellants' motion to dismiss the action. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the driver and the garnishee argued that the trial court erred in granting the passenger's motion to file a supplemental complaint and denying their motion to dismiss the action. Upon review, the court found appellants' arguments without merit. Minn. St. 571.41, subd. 2, was enacted by the legislature to permit garnishment of an insurer's obligation to an insured, even though not due absolutely and without contingency. Minn. R. Civ. P. 4.04(2), which provided that when quasi in rem jurisdiction was obtained, a party defending such action thereby submitted personally to the jurisdiction of the court, applied in cases where jurisdiction was obtained pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 571.41, subd. 2, only to the extent of the driver's policy limits. Possible injustice to the driver in situations where jurisdiction was obtained pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 571.41, subd. 2, could have been controlled by application of the doctrine of forum non conveniens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting the passenger's motion to file a supplemental complaint and denying appellants' motion to dismiss the action.

 

402 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Unborn Child v. Evans


No. 46312


Supreme Court of Minnesota


310 Minn. 197; 245 N.W.2d 600; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1822



September 3, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Crow Wing County District Court brought by Brenda Wilcox on behalf of her unborn child to recover the proceeds of a life insurance policy issued to decedent Mark Evans, allegedly the father of said child, by defendants Minnesota Mutual Life Insurance Company, Inc., and Northwestern National Life Insurance Company, Inc., which proceeds had been paid to defendants George A. and Della Evans, decedent's parents. The court, Ben Grussendorf, Judge, granted defendants' motions for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff decedent's unborn child, by his mother, sought review of the decision of the Crow Wing County District Court (Minnesota), which granted defendant decedent's parents and insurers' motion for summary judgment in the unborn child's action that prayed for an injunction against the dissipation of the proceeds by the parents and for an order requiring the distribution of the insurance proceeds to the unborn child.


OVERVIEW: At the time of his conception, the unborn child's parents were not married. Before he was born, the unborn child's father, the decedent, was killed in an automobile accident. The insurers paid the decedent's parents the policy proceeds. Three months before the birth of the unborn child, his mother claimed the insurance proceeds on his behalf. The court noted that the denial to the unborn child of the insurance proceeds was made solely according to his legitimacy or illegitimacy. The main issue on appeal was whether a denial of the insurance proceeds to the unborn child violated his right to equal protection of the laws under the Fourteenth Amendment. The court held that the facts, when fully developed, would presumably have shown that the denial to the unborn child of participation in the distribution of the proceeds resulted from state action. The court also concluded that the classification of children of an insured according to whether they were legitimate or illegitimate was not reasonably related to a legitimate state interest. If all the genuinely disputed factual issues were resolved in the unborn child's favor then it appeared that he would have been entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment that had been granted in favor of the decedent's parents and the insurers and remanded the matter.

 

403 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Application of Northwestern Bell Tel. Co.


No. 46054


Supreme Court of Minnesota


310 Minn. 146; 246 N.W.2d 28; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1686



August 27, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] This court granted discretionary review of an order of the Ramsey County District Court, Ronald E. Hachey, Judge, remanding to the Public Service Commission proceedings initiated by Northwestern Bell Telephone Company for an order sanctioning certain increases in rates and charges for telephone service, in which proceedings the state intervened.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court directed a discretionary opinion toward its decision affirming an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which remanded a telephone rate case to the Minnesota Public Service Commission on review by appellant telephone company and intervenor State in an action by the company brought when the Commission granted a rate increase substantially less than had been requested by the company.


OVERVIEW: The company sought a rate increase and an increase substantially less than that requested was granted. Both the company and the State appealed and the district court remanded to the Commission. The court affirmed the decision and then granted discretionary review. The court determined that resolution of the issue required reconciliation of Minn. Stat. §§ 237.25 and 15.0425. The court held that § 15.0425 applied to judicial review of telephone rate cases so that the powers conferred in Minn. Stat. § 237.25 were cumulative rather than exclusive. Deference to the expertise of the Commission made remand a necessary option for the district court reviewing telephone rate proceedings, notwithstanding the possibility of delay. Minn. Stat. § 237.25 conferred upon the district court a power that it would not have otherwise had under Minn. Stat. § 15.0425, to avoid remand and draft its own order if the record permitted, but the district court was not compelled to do so if it determined that a just result required further exercise of the Commission's expertise. Whether in a particular rate case remand was appropriate was within the discretion of the district court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed its decision, deciding only the issue of whether the district court had authority to order the remand.

 

404 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


McKee v. County of Ramsey


No. 46380


Supreme Court of Minnesota


310 Minn. 192; 245 N.W.2d 460; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1821



August 27, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Michael McKee and Joyce McKee to recover medical expenses allegedly incurred for maternity care. The court, Edward D. Mulally, Judge, granted defendant county's motion for judgment on the pleadings, and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimants appealed the order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted judgment on the pleadings to defendant county in an action to recover medical expenses allegedly incurred for maternity care. The trial court held that the failure of the claimants to file a timely appeal from the decision of the commissioner of public welfare barred the claims under the doctrines of exhaustion of remedies and res judicata.


OVERVIEW: The county denied the claimants' request for reimbursement of maternity expenses after the claimants went to an unauthorized hospital in order to avoid lectures on family planning. The claimants filed suit and alleged negligence and violations of equal protection. On appeal, the court noted that the doctrine of exhaustion of administrative remedies did not apply if nothing could be accomplished by resort to administrative remedies, and that res judicata did not operate as to claims that were not raised and over which the administrative agency did not have jurisdiction. The court held that although both the negligence and administrative claims contemplated the same relief, the recovery of maternity costs, Minn. Stat. ch. 261 did not, under any reading, comprehend the presentation of tort claims in the administrative proceedings, so that the trial court should hear the negligence claim. The court found that the equal protection claim was based on the county's application of a statute, not the constitutionality of the statute itself, and was subject to administrative review, but held that it made little sense to sever the claim from the negligence claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the county and remanded the case for trial on both the issue of negligence and the claim of unconstitutionality in the denial of reimbursement of maternity expenses.

 

405 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Collis v. Bloomington


No. 45523


Supreme Court of Minnesota


310 Minn. 5; 246 N.W.2d 19; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1685



August 13, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought by George C. Collis and Laurel Collis, residents and taxpayers of defendant city, for a declaratory judgment invalidating a park donation ordinance of said city and a statute authorizing such ordinance, and for other relief. After findings for defendant, Dana Nicholson, Judge, plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff land developers challenged the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which found in favor of defendant city and upheld the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 462.358 and Bloomington, Minn., City Code § 20.09 II B, which authorized and mandated dedication of subdivision land to the city for park and recreational purposes or, in lieu of such dedication, payment of fees for those purposes.


OVERVIEW: In order to secure approval of their application to subdivide, the developers had to make a cash park donation to the city. The developers challenged the facial constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 462.358, subd. 2 (1971), and Bloomington, Minn., City Code § 20.09 II B, which authorized park dedications. The district court upheld the constitutionality of both the statute and the ordinance, and the court affirmed. The court held that even though the possibility of arbitrariness and unfairness in its application was substantial, the enabling statute prevented this application by authorizing dedication of only a "reasonable portion" of the land. Therefore, the statute was upheld as constitutional. A "reasonable portion" was construed to mean that portion of land which the evidence reasonably established that the municipality would need to acquire for the purposes stated as a result of approval of the subdivision. The court held that a provision in the ordinance that stated that, as a general rule, 10 percent of the land was "reasonable," was constitutional because it allowed for rebuttal of this presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and upheld the enabling statute and the city ordinance as constitutional.

 

406 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Klaus v. Minnesota State Ethics Com.


No. 45475


Supreme Court of Minnesota


309 Minn. 430; 244 N.W.2d 672; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1561



July 30, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court for a declaratory judgment invalidating legislation requiring certain disclosures by candidates for office and for injunctive relief. Defendants State Ethics Commission and the attorney general moved for summary judgment. The court, John W. Graff, retired judge, granted that motion and defendant commission's motion for a mandatory injunction requiring plaintiff as a public official and as candidate for the legislature to file a statement of economic interest. Plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered and from an order denying suspension of the injunction pending the appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate challenged an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted the motion for summary judgment that appellees, the Minnesota State Ethics Commission and the attorney general, filed in the candidate's declaratory judgment action regarding the requirement under Minn. Stat. § 10A.09 (1974) as to filing a statement of economic interest and that also requested an injunction against enforcing § 104.90.


OVERVIEW: The candidate, who was the incumbent, alleged that § 104.90 unconstitutionally invaded his right to privacy and imposed an unconstitutional property qualification in violation of Minn. Const. art. 1, § 17. The court affirmed the district court's judgment, concluding that § 104.90 did not unduly infringe any of the candidate's protected rights. The court reasoned that precedent showed that the public's right to know of matters possible conflicts of interest between the public employment and the private financial interests of public office holders was a proper legislative concern. The court also held that, by willingly entering the public arena and accepting publicly conferred benefits after being elected to public office, the candidate was legitimately much more subject to reasonable scrutiny and exposure than a purely private person. The court further determined that § 104.90 did not require the candidate to disclose his net worth or the amount of his income, that it did not require owning realty in order to seek or to hold office, and did not make non-compliance with § 104.90 a bar on running for office because only penalties was imposed for non-compliance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of appellees' summary judgment motion in the candidate's declaratory judgment action that sought a ruling that an economic disclosure statute was unconstitutional and that sought an injunction against its enforcement.

 

407 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Ebel v. South International Falls


No. 45400


Supreme Court of Minnesota


309 Minn. 580; 244 N.W.2d 496; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1598



July 23, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Koochiching County District Court for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff as the result of the negligence of defendant village. The court, Gordon L. McRae, Judge, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the judgment of the Koochiching District Court (Minnesota), which granted defendant municipality's motion for summary judgment and dismissed plaintiff's personal injury action for failure to comply with Minn. Stat. § 466.05, subd. 1.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff commenced a personal injury action against the municipality alleging that plaintiff was seriously injured when a snowmobile that he was operating collided with a bale of barbed wire that had been negligently left at the accident site by the municipality's employees and subsequently concealed by snow. Plaintiff's summons and complaint were served more than one year after the date of the accident and at no time prior to commencement of the action did plaintiff give formal written notice to the municipality of the tort claim. The trial court granted the municipality's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the action for failure to comply with Minn. Stat. § 466.05, subd. 1. The court remanded. No formal notice from the injured plaintiff was required if the municipal defendant had actual notice from another source. Thus, the trial court had to determine whether the municipality had actual notice within the 30-day period. The court noted that the cause was not commenced until more than one year after the date of the injury and the action could be barred in the absence of circumstances to toll the one-year statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the trial court's judgment.

 

408 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hill


No. 46592


Supreme Court of Minnesota


309 Minn. 206; 244 N.W.2d 728; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1521



June 25, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied, 429 U.S. 1065, 97 S. Ct. 794, 50 L. ed. 2d 782 (1977).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Stanley Curtis Hill from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, David E. Marsden, Judge, whereby he was convicted of aggravated rape.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) for aggravated rape. Defendant was sentenced to serve a term not to exceed 20 years in the State reformatory.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the complainant consented to engaging in sexual intercourse with him. Defendant was convicted by the trial court for aggravated rape. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the jury could find that the complainant was in a drunken stupor until she suddenly realized her predicament, when she began to scream, and defendant held his hand over her mouth, events corroborated by a police officer. There was testimony that she became hysterical, and that defendant was running from the scene when apprehended. Under Minn. Stat. § 609.347, subd. 3, evidence of a complainant's previous sexual conduct was not admissible unless the court found that it was material to the issue of consent or fabrication and that its prejudicial nature did not outweigh its probative value. Isolated instances of cohabitation as distinguished from evidence of promiscuity did not in themselves lend credence to a claim of consent such as defendant raised. However, defense counsel was permitted to inquire in relation to contemporaneous sexual relations within a week of the event, under Minn. Stat. § 609.347, subd. 3(b). The conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated rape.

 

409 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Schaefer v. Bloomington


No. 46129


Supreme Court of Minnesota


309 Minn. 157; 244 N.W.2d 45; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1514



June 18, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought on behalf of Pamela Schaefer, a minor, by Fred Schaefer, her father and natural guardian, for personal injuries allegedly sustained by reason of negligence of defendants, city of Bloomington and County of Hennepin, and by said Fred Schaefer on his own behalf for consequential damages. The court, Dana Nicholson, Judge, granted defendant county's motion for summary judgment, and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered. Considered and decided by the court without oral argument.



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment set aside and case remanded for trial on issues of liability and damages.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a minor's father and guardian, brought an action against defendants, a city and a county, to recover damages for injuries suffered by the minor when her bicycle wheels became engaged in a sewer grate on a public road. The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) granted the county's motion for summary judgment because the father did not serve a timely notice of claim under Minn. Stat. § 466.05, subd. 1 (1971). The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father served a timely notice of claim on the city. The city manager notified the father that the road in which the grate was located was a county road and that, thus, the city had no responsibility for the road's maintenance or construction. Ten days later, the father served on the county a notice of claim, which was three weeks after the expiration of the 30-day notice limitation of Minn. Stat. § 466.05, subd. 1 (1971). The father contended that Minn. Stat. § 466.05, subd. 1 (1971) was unconstitutional and that the notice provided to the county substantially complied with its requirements. The court held that the father's prompt but untimely notice of claim constituted substantial compliance. When two governmental entities jointly used a common facility located within their borders, which facility gave rise to a tort claim, timely notice to one entity followed by a prompt, though not timely, notice to the other entity substantially complied with the requirements of Minn. Stat. § 466.05, subd. 1 (1971). Even if the city had not notified the county of the claim, the county would have available to it the city's investigation and an ample opportunity to further investigate.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the summary judgment for the county and remanded the case for a trial on the issues of liability and damages.

 

410 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Welfare of S.


Nos. 45988, 45989, 45990, 46089, 46215, 46254, 46158, 46174, 46416


Supreme Court of Minnesota


309 Minn. 78; 244 N.W.2d 30; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1504



June 4, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nine cases: Three appeals by the state from orders of the Hennepin County District Court, Lindsay G. Arthur, Judge, denying motions for reference of juveniles I.Q.S., E.T.B., and T.L.P. for criminal prosecution as adults; an appeal by juvenile J.E.C. from an order by the same judge referring said juvenile for prosecution as an adult; a petition by juvenile William Hunter for a writ of prohibition to restrain enforcement of and to rescind a similar order by the same judge; three separate appeals by juveniles Fred Christopher Romanowski, Donald Amos, and Paul Lawrence Wright from similar orders of the same judge; and one order of the Hennepin County District Court, David R. Leslie, Judge, certifying as important or doubtful the issues involved in an order by the Ramsey County District Court, Archie Gingold, Judge, referring juvenile Steven Craig Parker for criminal prosecution as an adult.



DISPOSITION: Cases of I.Q.S., E.T.B., and T.L.P. remanded for further proceedings; writ of prohibition denied in case of juvenile Hunter; orders affirmed in cases of juveniles J.E.C., Romanowski, Amos, and Parker; order challenged by certification affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This case involved nine consolidated appeals issued by the state of juvenile courts, from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) and the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which made orders in each of the cases either denying reference of the juveniles for prosecution as an adult, or granting that relief under Minn. Stat. § 260.125.


OVERVIEW: The court took the opportunity to discuss the standards to be employed by a juvenile court in its disposition of motions for certification of juveniles for prosecution as adults made pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 260.125. The court had previously determined that orders of the juvenile court which denied the state's motion to refer a juvenile for prosecution as an adult were non-appealable. A recent United State Supreme Court case led the court to change that conclusion, and instead hold that those orders were final and appealable. The court rejected the juveniles' contention that Minn. Stat. § 260.125 was unconstitutional. The statute had ascertainable standards that could be followed and therefore survived the challenge that it was impermissibly vague. The statute compared favorably with the Uniform Juvenile Court Act, § 34, which militated against a violation of equal protection. The court imposed on lower the courts the duty of making clear findings for their reference decisions, and such findings would not be disturbed on appeal absent a showing that they were "clearly erroneous" so as to constitute an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: Various relief was granted in each of the nine cases after the court set out the standards for providing such relief.

 

411 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Thoreson v. Civil Service Com.


No. 45994


Supreme Court of Minnesota


308 Minn. 357; 242 N.W.2d 603; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1770



May 14, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari in the Ramsey County District Court upon the petition of Benjamin B. Thoreson to review action of the Civil Service Commission of the City of St. Paul, its chairman, and its members upholding the discharge of petitioner from his position as a building inspector for the city. The court, Edward D. Mulally, Judge, affirmed the commission, and petitioner appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) that sustained the decision of appellee, a city civil service commission, arguing that the district court erred in concluding that he had been terminated from his position for cause.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the city as a building inspector. He purchased a building located within the city that was scheduled for demolition and applied for a permit to rehabilitate the property. While the permit represented that the house was owned by a third party and that the work would be performed by a general contract, the employee was the actual owner and intended to do the rehabilitation work himself. Further, the inspection to be done by the building department on the house would, in the normal course of business, be assigned to the employee himself. After a co-worker reported the employee's activities to a supervisor, the employee was discharged. He challenged his discharge, but his terminate was upheld by the city civil service commission and the district court. The employee sought further review. In affirming, the court concluded that there was substantial evidence in the record to support the conclusion that the employee was discharged for cause. The employee deliberately made misrepresentations on the permit application, and he showed a willingness to take advantage of his official capacity for his own personal benefit.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

 

412 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Johnson Bros. Wholesale Liquor Co. v. United Farm Workers Nat'l Union


No. 45815


Supreme Court of Minnesota


308 Minn. 87; 241 N.W.2d 292; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1725; 92 L.R.R.M. 2302



April 2, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought by Johnson Brothers Wholesale Liquor Company and Twin City Wine Company, wholesale liquor distributors, to enjoin defendant union and some of its members and agents from alleged illegal picketing at some of plaintiffs' customers' stores. After findings for plaintiffs, Harold Kalina, Judge, defendants appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed but remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a union, union members, and union agents, sought review of the amended order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which entered a judgment for plaintiff wholesale liquor distributors in an action brought under the Secondary Boycott Act, Minn. Stat. §§ 179.40-179.47, and which permanently enjoined defendants from picketing retail liquor stores except in conformance with certain restrictions.


OVERVIEW: A labor dispute existed between the union and a winery. Defendants began a campaign of picketing at retail liquor stores to whom the distributors sold wine for resale. The words "on strike" were in larger print than other words on the picket signs. Pickets occasionally blocked ingress and egress from the retail stores. The distributors sought to enjoin the picketing activities pursuant to the Secondary Boycott Act. Ultimately, the trial court permanently enjoined the pickets except in conformance with certain restrictions. The court held that Minn. Stat. § 185.10(5) of the Anti-Injunction Act did not prohibit injunctive relief against peaceful picketing when such picketing was in violation of an express state statute, such as the Secondary Boycott Act, which served a legitimate governmental interest. Further, when otherwise peaceful picketing became obstructive and coercive, a reasonable limitation on the number of pickets was permissible under the First Amendment. However, while the union was obligated to clearly identify the struck product, it was not the proper role of an equity court to tell pickets what words they had to use to express ideas or to whom they could talk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's authority to issue the injunction but remanded with directions to modify the terms of the injunction in a manner consistent with its opinion.

 

413 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Almquist v. Marshan


No. 44599


Supreme Court of Minnesota


308 Minn. 52; 245 N.W.2d 819; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1724



April 2, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Dakota County District Court wherein plaintiff property owner sought a declaratory judgment invalidating a moratorium imposed by defendant, Town of Marshan, on granting of building permits and determining that plaintiff is entitled to proceed with a proposed development of his property. After adverse findings, Robert J. Breunig, Judge, defendant appealed from the judgment entered and from an order denying its motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town challenged the judgment of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which entered judgment in favor of respondent landowner and denied its motion for a new trial in a case involving a moratorium imposed by the town on granting building permits.


OVERVIEW: A landowner sought a declaratory judgment invalidating a moratorium imposed by a town on the granting of building permits and determining that he was entitled to proceed with a proposed development of his property. The lower court ruled in his favor, and the town appealed. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that where a municipality enacted in good faith and without discrimination, a moratorium on development, which was of limited duration, was valid if, upon enactment, the study proceeded promptly and appropriate zoning ordinances were expeditiously adopted when it was completed. The court also found that the lower court had not reached the issue of the validity of the moratorium as applied to the landowner or whether its effect on him constituted "substantial prejudice." A new trial was directed as to that issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the landowner was reversed and remanded.

 

414 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnesota State Board of Health by Lawson v. Brainerd


No. 45644


Supreme Court of Minnesota


308 Minn. 24; 241 N.W.2d 624; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1722



March 26, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Dismissed, 429 U.S. 803, 97 S. Ct. 35, 50 L. ed. 2d 63 (1976).


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus in the Crow Wing County District Court upon the petition of the State Board of Health, by Dr. Warren R. Lawson, to compel the city of Brainerd, its mayor, its city council, members of the council, and its Water and Light Board, and members of the board to comply with a statute and regulation requiring fluoridation of the municipal water supply. The court, James E. Preece, Judge, ordered a peremptory writ to issue, and respondents appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a city, its mayor, its city council, and other city related parties (collectively, city), challenged an order of the Crow Wing County District Court (Minnesota), which issued a peremptory writ of mandamus in petitioner Minnesota State Board of Health's action to compel the city to comply with the Minnesota Fluoridation Law, Minn. Stat. § 144.145, requiring fluoridation of the municipal water supply.


OVERVIEW: In a prior action, a private nonprofit corporation was denied an injunction against the enforcement of § 144.145 by the city and the Board. Thereafter, the city held a special referendum, resulting in a vote against fluoridation. Subsequently, city leaders met regarding the fluoridation and the city declared § 144.145 an unconstitutional invasion of individual rights. As such, the Board filed a petition for a writ of mandamus. The court held that the city had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the Minnesota Fluoridation Law because the question of fluoridating the drinking water of the city involved a question of substantial public interest to the people of the city and because the city claimed that such fluoridation threatened to destroy its water filtration system. The court accepted as factual the legislative determination that fluoride was a safe and effective means of reducing dental caries and held that the means of achieving the State's purpose was proper and reasonable. Specifically, the court found that, although the actual consumption of water was a private and personal act, the preparation and treatment of that water was a common and accepted public function.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

415 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kremer


No. 44728


Supreme Court of Minnesota


307 Minn. 309; 239 N.W.2d 476; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1436



February 27, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Fred L. Kremer from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Stephen L. Maxwell, Judge, whereby he was convicted of coercion and felonious theft. Upon remand, the trial court denied appellant's petition for postconviction relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota) for coercion and felonious theft. Defendant contended that a county judge improperly issued a search warrant that provided for a nighttime search and an unannounced entry. Defendant argued that the search warrant was not based upon probable cause.


OVERVIEW: The wife of a supermarket owner received a telephone call that she had won free tickets to a play. While the wife was attending the play, defendant phoned the husband and instructed him to remove money from the supermarket and leave it in his car, under threat of harm upon his wife if he did not cooperate. Police received information from an informant that while visiting defendant, the informant overheard a conversation concerning a plan that bore a striking resemblance to the plot carried out against the husband and wife. The informant described the method used to conduct surveillance of the husband and wife, i.e., walkie-talkies, and stated that the money obtained was used to buy drugs in California. Police obtained a search warrant for defendant's home that allowed a nighttime search and unannounced entry. Police seized walkie-talkies, tickets to California held in defendant's name, and drugs. Defendant was convicted for coercion and felonious theft. Defendant appealed and argued that the search warrant was improperly issued. The court held that, throughout the pre-trial and trial proceedings, defendant had failed to object to the search warrant and had waived any objection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

416 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Price v. Sheppard


No. 45588


Supreme Court of Minnesota


307 Minn. 250; 239 N.W.2d 905; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1428



February 20, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Willa Mae Price, individually and as mother and natural guardian of Dwight Price, to recover actual and punitive damages allegedly sustained by reason of electroshock therapy given to said minor by defendant Dr. Charles G. Sheppard and other unknown persons. The court, E. Thomas Brennan, Judge, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother of a minor patient involuntarily committed to a state mental hospital appealed a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to defendant medical director of the hospital in the mother's action to recover actual and punitive damages allegedly sustained by reason of electroshock therapy given to the patient without the mother's consent.


OVERVIEW: The mother brought an action against the medical director for assault and battery and violation of the patient's civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The lower court granted the medical director's motion for summary judgment, and the mother appealed. The court held that: (1) where electroshock therapy involving multiple treatments over a substantial period of time was prescribed for the involuntarily committed state mental hospital patient, who had failed to respond to other forms of treatment, the administration of the electroshock treatments, absent the effective consent of the patient or the mother, was not cruel and unusual punishment as the treatments served a legitimate purpose rather than deterrence or reprimand; (2) the electroshock treatments were not a violation of the patient's right to privacy as the interest of the state was sufficiently important for it to assume the treatment decision for the patient; and (3) the medical director, acting in his official capacity, was immune from suit as he acted in good faith and could not reasonably have known that the administration of electroshock treatments violated a constitutional right. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting summary judgment to the medical director in the mother's action for assault and battery of the patient and violation of the patient's civil rights.

 

417 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Robbinsdale Education Asso. v. Robbinsdale Federation of Teachers


No. 46216


Supreme Court of Minnesota


307 Minn. 96; 239 N.W.2d 437; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1404; 92 L.R.R.M. 2417



January 23, 1976 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Judgment Vacated and Case Remanded, 429 U.S. 880, 97 S. Ct. 225, 50 L. ed. 2d 160 (1976).


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought by Robbinsdale Education Association, Marilyn Threlkeld, and Daniel Hanka challenging the validity of a statute which allowed defendant Robbinsdale Federation of Teachers Local 872, which was certified as exclusive representative of certain bargaining units of defendant Independent School District No. 281, to assess a fair share fee from employees in such bargaining units who are not members of defendant union. After findings for plaintiffs, Crane Winton, Judge, defendant union appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a teachers' union, appealed from the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which enjoined the union from deducting a fair share fee, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 179.65, subd. 2, from the paychecks of plaintiffs, two non-union member employees of the school district in question. The two employees and an association, which also was a plaintiff, challenged the validity of the statute on constitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: The union had been elected as the exclusive representative of all employees in the school district, whether union or non-union members. Under the statute in question, the union had assessed a fair share of its fees against the non-union school district employees involved in the instant action. Such assessments were contributions toward the union's representation in negotiations and grievances with the school district. Deductions were taken from the employees' paychecks to cover the assessments without a prior hearing. The district court found that the statute violated due process under the state and federal constitutions in that it did not provide for notice and hearing prior to a determination of the fair share fee for services. The court reversed the judgment, as Minn. Stat. § 179.65, subd. 2 did not violate due process. The procedural remedies encompassed by the statute complied with due process standards, as there were sufficient safeguards in the statute to protect employees from any significant loss of property. Their need for a prior hearing was outweighed by the governmental interest in securing the financial stability of the union, as their exclusive representative.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

418 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minneapolis v. Buschette


No. 45040


Supreme Court of Minnesota


307 Minn. 60; 240 N.W.2d 500; 1976 Minn. LEXIS 1401



January 23, 1976 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Debra A. Buschette from a judgment of the Hennepin County Municipal Court, C. William Sykora, Judge, whereby she was convicted of common prostitution.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Hennepin County Municipal Court (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of common prostitution in violation of Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 870.110.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a woman, contended that § 870.110 was discriminatorily enforced. In affirming, the court held that defendant failed to establish a pattern of discriminatory enforcement against women. According to the court, defendant did not show that there was a police policy to arrest only female prostitutes. The court also determined that the police's policy of having only male officers present in areas known to be solicited by female prostitutes did not amount to discriminatory enforcement. In addition, the court found that statistics comparing the number of arrests made of men and the number made of women for prostitution did not establish discriminatory enforcement. Finally, the court noted that defendant did not meet the heavy burden of proving that the State's selection for prosecution was in bad faith.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

419 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lasley


No. 45464


Supreme Court of Minnesota


306 Minn. 224; 236 N.W.2d 604; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1239



November 21, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Larry Carl Lasley from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, A. Paul Lommen, Judge, whereby he was convicted of murder in the first degree, aggravated assault, and aggravated robbery, and from an order denying his alternative motion for judgment of acquittal or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of murder in the first degree, aggravated assault, and aggravated robbery. Defendant also appealed an order denying his alternative motion for judgment of acquittal or for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first contended that the trial court's refusal to conduct a psychiatric examination of a victim who testified constituted grounds for dismissal. The victim was an alcoholic who suffered from severe mental deterioration. However confused the victim might have been on the details, it was not unreasonable to believe that, having survived the terrifying experience that nearly cost him his life, he would recall defendant's name. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the victim to testify. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress evidence removed from his home without a search warrant. Under the circumstances of the brutal murder and the prompt investigation, the police were justified in going immediately to defendant's home without waiting for a warrant. Time was of the essence. The court held that it was not unreasonable nor a violation of the Fourth Amendment for the police to enter defendant's apartment, search for defendant, and interview defendant's wife. The evidence seized was in plain sight and was admissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder in the first degree, aggravated assault, and aggravated robbery and the order denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal or for a new trial.

 

420 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Vadnais Heights v. Board of Water Comm'rs


No. 45169


Supreme Court of Minnesota


306 Minn. 234; 236 N.W.2d 777; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1240



November 21, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court wherein plaintiff village sought an adjudication that defendant, Board of Water Commissioners of the City of Saint Paul, was legally obligated to pay an assessment levied by plaintiff for sanitary sewer improvements or that plaintiff is entitled to judicial review of the determination by defendant board of the amount its property has been benefited by said improvements. The court, John W. Graff, Judge, granted plaintiff's motion for partial summary judgment, and defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Board of Water Commissioners appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), which granted plaintiff village's motion for partial summary judgment that the Board's determination of the value of benefits to its property from sanitary sewer improvements constructed by the village was judicially reviewable.


OVERVIEW: The Board, which was responsible for providing water to St. Paul, had acquired considerable real property within the village through condemnation. After the village constructed a sanitary sewer system, which was usable by a substantial portion of the Board's property, the village established a formula to be used in setting assessments for the cost of the sewer system pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 435.19, subd. 1, which gave the village the power to levy special assessments against the property of a governmental unit to the same extent as if the property were privately owned, and it assessed the Board more than $ 178,000 for the sewer improvements. Purporting to act pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 435.19, subd. 3, the Board thereupon determined that the value of the benefits from the sewer to its property, which was the maximum amount it was required to pay, was only $ 10,000. The Board challenged the jurisdiction of the trial court to review the Board's decision, and the court affirmed summary judgment that the trial court had jurisdiction. To hold otherwise would have given the Board unlimited discretion to decide what it should pay as assessments for improvements from which it benefited.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Nieting v. Blondell


No. 45361


Supreme Court of Minnesota


306 Minn. 122; 235 N.W.2d 597; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1226



October 31, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff when her automobile collided with a tractor-trailer unit driven by defendant Henry R. Blondell, Jr., owned in part by said defendant and in part by defendant Sawyer Transportation, Inc. Defendants appeal from an order, Crane Winton, Judge, dismissing their third-party complaint filed against the state.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, driver and company, sought review of an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed their third-party complaint filed against third-party defendant, the State of Minnesota, in an action brought by plaintiff driver for personal injuries allegedly sustained by her when her car collided with a tractor-trailer unit driven by the driver and owned by the driver and the company.


OVERVIEW: The tractor-trailer crossed the median of a highway and a seven-car accident ensued. Following initiation of an action against defendants for personal injuries arising from the accident, they filed a notice of claim with the State Claims Commission (Commission) against the State pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 3.66 et seq., and alleged that the State was negligent in maintaining the barriers that separated the east and west bound lanes of the highway. The Commission, at the request of defendants, did not act on the claim. Defendants then moved for leave to file a third-party complaint against the State, which was granted. The State then moved for dismissal of the third-party complaint, which was granted. The court, after examining the history of the grant of tort immunity to a state, abolished the State's tort immunity with respect to tort claims that arose on or after August 1, 1976, subject to any appropriate action taken by the legislature. Although the court abolished tort immunity, the court affirmed the dismissal of defendants' third-party complaint because it was not fair to the State to deny it a defense on which it had a right to rely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing defendants' third-party complaint.

 

422 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Norris Creameries


No. 45344


Supreme Court of Minnesota


306 Minn. 79; 235 N.W.2d 203; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1220



October 24, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari on the relation of Norris Creameries, employer, and Firemen's Fund American Insurance Companies, insurer, to review a decision of the Workmen's Compensation Commission awarding compensation to respondent employee, Erwin Miller, against relators; denying their claim for apportionment against respondent Bituminous Casualty Corporation, a former insurer for Norris; and denying their claim for reimbursement against the Special Compensation Fund.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employer and its insurer, sought a writ of certiorari to review a decision from the Minnesota Workmen's Compensation Commission that affirmed the findings and determinations of the compensation judge and denied their reimbursement claim against respondent special compensation fund.


OVERVIEW: In 1964, after working as a milkman for more than 20 years, the employee injured his back while loading his truck. He received temporary disability benefits before returning to work. In 1970, his employer registered the employee with the Workmen's Compensation Commission as an employee with a preexisting physical impairment under Minn. Stat. § 176.131 (1969). When the employee suffered a second back injury two years later, the employer and its insurer sought reimbursement from the special compensation fund. The Workmen's Compensation Commission denied the reimbursement claim, and the employer and insurer appealed. In reversing, the court concluded that the registration of an employee as suffering from a preexisting injury vested the employer with a right to reimbursement, which was not destroyed by the legislature's amendment of the definition of the term "physical impairment" prior to when the employee suffered his second injury. The right to reimbursement vested in the employer and its insurer on the date the employee was registered as suffering from a preexisting physical impairment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Workmen's Compensation was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

423 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Larson v. Independent School Dist.


No. 45685


Supreme Court of Minnesota


305 Minn. 358; 233 N.W.2d 744; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1337



September 19, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Prohibition in this court, upon the petition of defendants in actions brought by Percy Larson and Phyllis Larson, and on behalf of Steven C. Larson, their minor child, for damages arising out of an accident in which said minor allegedly sustained injuries, to restrain the Isanti County District Court, Robert B. Gillespie, Judge, from enforcing an order requiring petitioners to furnish respondents with certain information which they had obtained from witnesses with regard to the actions.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought a writ of prohibition to restrain the Isanti County District Court (Minnesota) from enforcing an order that required defendants to furnish plaintiffs with certain information they had obtained from witnesses in regard to plaintiffs' action against defendants for damages arising out of an accident in which minor plaintiff sustained injuries.


OVERVIEW: These were consolidated personal injury actions arising out of a physical education class accident involving minor plaintiff. The actions were commenced and statements were taken before the promulgation of certain amendments to the Minnesota Rules of Civil Procedure, which substantially expanded the scope of discovery. Plaintiffs filed a motion that sought the production of all taped and written statements of nonparty witnesses' in defendants' possession. The trial court granted the motion without requiring plaintiffs to make a showing of any kind. Defendants contended that the amended rule, Minn. R. Civ. P. 26.02(3), only applied to the discovery of statements taken after the effective date of the rule. The court observed the procedural rules were to be liberally construed. The court determined that the amended rule applied to all pending actions, unless a trial court determined that its application to particular case would not be feasible or would work an injustice. The application of the amended rule to allow discovery of witnesses' statements collected before the effective date of the rule impaired no vested rights of defendants.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' application for a writ of prohibition to restrain the trial court from enforcing an order that required them to furnish plaintiffs with certain information they had obtained from witnesses in regard to plaintiffs' personal injury actions against defendants.

State v. McKinley


No. 45537


Supreme Court of Minnesota


305 Minn. 297; 232 N.W.2d 906; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1328



September 5, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the state from an order of the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey County, Joseph P. Summers, Judge, dismissing a charge against L. B. McKinley of driving after cancellation of his driver's license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the Municipal Court of St. Paul, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which dismissed a charge against defendant of driving after cancellation of his driver's license. The trial court found that the seizure of defendant was in violation of the Fourth Amendment of the United States Constitution and of Minn. Const. art. 1, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving his car in an alley, under the speed limit. Police officers stopped him, placed him in a squad car, and checked for outstanding warrants. Finding none, defendant was arrested for driving after cancellation of his driver's license. The court affirmed the dismissal of the charges, finding that no reasonable suspicion of criminal activity existed that would have supported an investigative stop. At no time prior to the stop did either police officer observe any unlawful or suspicious conduct on the part of defendant, nor was either aware that defendant's driver's license had been canceled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the charges against defendant.

Anstine v. Lake Darling Ranch


No. 45584


Supreme Court of Minnesota


305 Minn. 243; 233 N.W.2d 723; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1320



August 29, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Douglas County District Court for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff while employed in the construction of a building. Lake Darling Ranch, Inc., the owner, and Lund-Martin Construction Company, the general contractor, were named as defendants and the latter filed a third-party complaint against Egan & Sons Company, plaintiff's employer, and other subcontractors, seeking indemnity. The court, Paul Hoffman, Judge, granted motions by several third-party defendants for summary judgment, and defendant construction company appealed from the judgments entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant construction company appealed judgments of the District Court, Douglas County (Minnesota), which granted motions by several third-party defendants for summary judgment in an action for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff while employed in the construction of a building.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff worker's sustained personal injuries while employed as a plumber apprentice for a subcontractor. Plaintiff brought an action against the owner of the project and defendant general contractor. Defendant joined all of the subcontractors connected with the project as third-party defendants, seeking indemnity from them pursuant to the subcontracts' indemnity clauses. The subcontractors moved for summary judgment, which the trial court granted. Defendant appealed, arguing that, based upon the indemnity clauses, all of the subcontractors formed a pool for the benefit of defendant and were therefore liable to indemnify defendant for all personal injuries arising out of the entire construction project. The court distinguished between indemnity agreements and contracts of insurance, finding that defendant sought to convert its subcontractors into unlicensed insurers. Such a presumption was not warranted. Therefore, the grant of summary judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: Judgments of the trial court were affirmed; subcontractors were dismissed as third-party defendants in action for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff worker while employed in the construction of a building because indemnity clauses in subcontracts did not make subcontractors insurers for losses with which they had no connection.

Nyhus v. Civil Service Board


No. 45277


Supreme Court of Minnesota


305 Minn. 184; 232 N.W.2d 779; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1312



August 22, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] A. B. Nyhus filed a petition with the Ramsey County District Court for review of a decision of the Civil Service Board, State of Minnesota, upholding his dismissal from the permanent civil service of the state. After adverse findings, Ronald E. Hachey, Judge, petitioner appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a former civil service employee, sought review of the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), in favor of respondent, the Civil Service Board, State of Minnesota, upholding the employee's dismissal from the permanent civil service of the State, due to his alleged failure, after repeated requests, to take up residence within reasonable commuting distance of his assignment.


OVERVIEW: The employe was notified by letter of his dismissal, and he was informed that he had five days to reply in writing or personally and had a right to demand a hearing before the Board. The employee responded in writing, denying that he had refused to comply with the residency requirement, and requesting a hearing. He was dismissed five days after the initial letter. At the hearing, the Board concluded that the discharge was for just cause, and the district court affirmed its order. On appeal, the employee contended that he was entitled to an evidentiary hearing prior to dismissal under the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, and that there was insufficient evidence to support the determination that he was dismissed for just cause. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that the employee had procedural rights in connection with his proposed discharge but that those rights were sufficiently provided by the post-discharge hearing procedures under Minn. Stat. § 43.24, subds. 1,2. The court also held that substantial evidence supported the determination of the Board and of the district court that the discharge was for just cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Gillen v. Commissioner of Taxation


No. 44747


Supreme Court of Minnesota


305 Minn. 525; 232 N.W.2d 894; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1370



August 22, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Math P. Gillen and Gladys R. Gillen to review an order of the Tax Court which modified two orders of the commissioner of taxation with regard to said relators' income tax returns for 1967, 1968, and 1969.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certiorari, relator taxpayers sought review of an order of the Tax Court (Minnesota), which modified two orders of respondent commissioner of taxation (commissioner). The Tax Court held that Minn. Stat. § 290.01, subd. 20 (1969) adopted by reference the 1961 federal definition of gross income, and increased the taxpayers' sick-pay exclusions in an amount greater than allowed by the commissioner but less than claimed in amended tax returns.


OVERVIEW: One taxpayer received wages in the form of sick pay from his employer while he was unable to work. The taxpayers sought to exclude all such sick pay from their gross income without any waiting period. On appeal, the court held that Minn. Stat. § 290.08, subd. 5(a), which had been amended and then restored to its original form, no longer applied to sick-pay wages, but rather referred specifically to accident and health insurance payments, workmen's compensation benefits, and proceeds from lawsuits and settlements. The court held that Minn. Stat. § 290.01, subd. 20 (1969) had governed the sick-pay exclusion since 1961 and incorporated by reference the then-existing federal definitions of gross income and adjusted gross income. The court found that a 1961 version of 26 U.S.C.S. § 105(d) imposed a 30-day waiting period before allowing the exclusion while a 1964 version of § 105(d) did not. The court held that the state legislature could not delegate its function to Congress, so that the 1961 federal definition incorporated by reference by Minn. Stat. § 290.01, subd. 20 (1969) remained unchanged in state law despite the 1964 federal change.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Tax Court that increased the amount of sick pay excludable from gross income on the taxpayers' returns, but not in the amount claimed by the taxpayers.

F. & H. Inv. Co. v. Sackman-Gilliland Corp.


No. 45412


Supreme Court of Minnesota


305 Minn. 155; 232 N.W.2d 769; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1309



August 15, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Anoka County District Court brought by F. & H. Investment Company, later joined by Wholesale Lighting, Inc., to set aside a mortgage foreclosure by defendant Sackman-Gilliland Corporation. Bryant-Franklin Corporation, which had redeemed after the foreclosure, was also joined as a defendant. On the basis of stipulated facts, the court, John F. Thoreen, Judge, denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, certifying certain questions as important and doubtful, and they appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a mortgagor and a materialman, appealed from a decision of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment in their action against defendants, a mortgagee and an assignee of a judgment creditor of the mortgagor, to set aside a mortgage foreclosure as unconstitutional. The trial court certified the question of constitutionality pursuant to Minn. R. Civ. App. P. 103.03(i).


OVERVIEW: The mortgagee foreclosed the mortgaged property by advertisement and purchased it at the sheriff's sale. The assignee exercised its right of redemption and became the fee owner. The mortgagor then filed an action to set aside the foreclosure on the ground that foreclosure by advertisement as authorized by Minn. Stat. § 580.01 et seq. violated the due process clause of U.S. Const. Amend. XIV. The materialman later joined in the action as a plaintiff. The trial court denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, granted the assignee's motion for dismissal of the claims against it, and certified the question of constitutionality to the court for review. The court remanded the case, holding that it was not permitted by Rule 103.03(i) to render an advisory opinion. The court held that it was not able to rule on the constitutional question because the trial court had not determined various fact issues as to whether plaintiffs received procedural due process, including plaintiffs' standing, the presence of state action, whether notice and hearing were available, and whether the parties waived their rights, and without these determinations the court's ruling would have been advisory.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court to make the factual determinations necessary for appellate review.

Peterson v. Knutson


No. 45333


Supreme Court of Minnesota


305 Minn. 53; 233 N.W.2d 716; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1301



August 8, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court wherein plaintiff sought to recover damages allegedly caused by a decision of this court in which defendants, justices or acting justices of this court, allegedly participated. The court, James M. Lynch, Judge, granted defendants' motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate sought review of a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant judges in the candidate's action to recover damages for being injured by the participation of the judges in a judgment that mandated that the candidate's name be stricken from a general election ballot for supreme court justice.


OVERVIEW: The candidate filed for election to the office of supreme court justice. The judges mandated that the candidate's name be stricken from the general election ballot on the ground that the candidate was not learned in the law pursuant to Minn. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the judges. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that the two judges who were actually candidates for re-election disqualified themselves and the replacement judges acted correctly and responsibly in participating in and deciding the case. The court ruled that the candidate was not learned in the law within the meaning of the constitutional requirement because he was disbarred. The court held that judicial immunity required affirmance in the case. The court ruled that the case was also one for summary judgment on principles of res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Minnesota Higher Education Facilities Authority v. Hawk


No. 45582


Supreme Court of Minnesota


305 Minn. 97; 232 N.W.2d 106; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1305; 95 A.L.R.3d 987



August 8, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Minnesota Higher Education Facilities Authority against its secretary, Richard C. Hawk, for a declaratory judgment determining that said authority is empowered to issue revenue bonds for the refinancing of certain education facilities and ordering said defendant to perform acts and execute agreements relating to the issuance and sale of said bonds. After findings for plaintiff, Stephen L. Maxwell, Judge, defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Secretary of the Minnesota Higher Education Facilities Authority, appealed from an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted declaratory judgment for petitioner, the Minnesota Higher Education Facilities Authority and ordered the Secretary to issue and sale bonds to refinance the educational facilities of religiously-affiliated private educational institutions pursuant to Minn. Stat. §§ 136A.25-136A.53.
