432 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Barfnecht v. Town Board of Hollywood Township


No. 44546


Supreme Court of Minnesota


304 Minn. 505; 232 N.W.2d 420; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1453



July 18, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Carver County District Court brought by Walter Barfnecht and Mathias S. Schaust to enjoin the Town Board of Hollywood Township from widening a roadway adjoining their property. The court, Arlo E. Haering, Judge, found for defendant. After this court dismissed plaintiffs' attempted appeal from a judgment, Schaust v. Town Board of Hollywood Township, 295 Minn. 571, 204 N.W. 2d 646 (1973), judgment was entered in favor of defendant, and plaintiffs appealed from said judgment.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners brought an action in the Carver County District Court (Minnesota) to enjoin defendant town board from widening a roadway adjoining their property. The trial court found for the board. After the court dismissed the landowners' attempted appeal from a judgment, judgment was entered in favor of the board, and the landowners appealed from said judgment.


OVERVIEW: The constitutional question presented was whether Minn. Stat. § 160.05, if construed to extend public dedication of a road to a width of four rods and not simply to the extent of actual use, resulted in a taking of private property without due process of law. The board contended, and the trial court agreed, that § 160.05 constitutionally provided that any road dedicated by adverse public use was dedicated to a width of four rods, regardless of the width of actual usage. The landowners asserted that § 160.05 was unconstitutional because no notice was provided when a width greater than that of actual use was taken and that, as a result, they were denied property without the due process of law. As a result of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Minn. Const. art. 1, § 2, the court held that Minn. Stat. § 160.05 did not authorize a township to widen a road acquired by adverse public use beyond that width actually acquired by such adverse use. Privately owned land could not become public road by adverse use beyond the portion so used merely by a statutory pronouncement. Section 160.05 could operate to dedicate a road by public use only to the extent of actual use over the statutory period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

433 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Beck v. St. Paul


Nos. 45442, 45465, 45466


Supreme Court of Minnesota


304 Minn. 438; 231 N.W.2d 919; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1442



July 3, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Joseph Beck and other residents of the city of St. Paul to enjoin said city and The Stuart Corporation from taking any action under a purported rezoning of an area where plaintiffs owned property. After findings for plaintiffs, Leslie L. Anderson, retired judge, defendant corporation appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and developer challenged a judgment from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which ruled that the city's rezoning amendment, to reclassify an area from residential to commercial, was invalid and enjoined any development of the area that was inconsistent with the former zoning classification. Respondent landowners had filed an action against the city and the developer seeking to declare the rezoning amendment invalid.


OVERVIEW: Commercial and industrial development began in an area adjacent to an eight-block area, which was undeveloped and zoned "B residential" to permit single-family residences. A developer proposed development in the eight-block area, and the city council later adopted an amendment to the zoning ordinance to allow commercial developments. The landowners filed an action against the city and the developer to declare the rezoning amendment void. On appeal from a judgment for the landowners, the court held that the ordinance was valid and found that: (1) the city council's action in passing a resolution to formally initiate the rezoning consideration was sufficient to accomplish the purpose of Minn. Stat. § 462.357(4), which required a formal initiation process; (2) the city council had jurisdiction to enact the zoning amendment under § 462.357(5) because the consent of the landowners in the area to be rezoned and in the area within a boundary 100 feet from the outer perimeter of the area to be rezoned, had been obtained, notwithstanding that they had not been formally filed; and (3) the ordinance bore a significant relation to the health and welfare of the city.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had ruled that the new zoning ordinance was invalid and had enjoined the city and the developer from developing the area. The court remanded to the trial court to determine the number and the validity of the prerequisite consents, in the landowners' action to declare the zoning amendment invalid.

 

434 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul v. Mulnix


No. 45165


Supreme Court of Minnesota


304 Minn. 456; 232 N.W.2d 206; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1445



July 3, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Cathleen Mulnix, also known as Catherine Mulnix, from a judgment of the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey County, Joseph E. Salland, Judge, whereby she was convicted of disorderly conduct. Considered and decided by the court without oral argument.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Municipal Court of St. Paul, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted her of disorderly conduct. Defendant sought a reversal on the ground that St. Paul, Minn., Legislative Code, § 438.02 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a bar and became belligerent. She was asked to leave and refused. When the police attempted to remover her, she kicked one of the officers and screamed obscenities. The court first found that § 438.02 was essentially an anti-noise ordinance, which was not designed to be used to prosecute a person for exercising his First Amendment rights. Section 438.02 was applicable only to criminal conduct such as "fighting words," and not to constitutionally protected activities. Second, the prohibition in § 438.02 could be applied only to conduct that actually disturbed, and therefore it avoided the problems presented by a "tendency-to-disturb" standard. Third, § 438.02 prohibited only disturbance that unreasonably interfered with the right of others to use their property peacefully. The court concluded that, although § 438.02 was out of date and in need of revision, it was not constitutionally defective on its face. Nor was it unconstitutional in its application to defendant, whose disorderly conduct consisted of shouting and screaming, of using "fighting words," and of conduct which was clearly disturbing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct.

 

435 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Willie v. Independent School Dist.


No. 44660


Supreme Court of Minnesota


304 Minn. 319; 231 N.W.2d 272; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1425



June 13, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the St. Louis County District Court brought by the parents of children attending school in defendant school district for a declaratory judgment that defendant's policy as to fees was unconstitutional. The court, Patrick D. O'Brien, Judge, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, and plaintiffs appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and matter remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents brought an action against defendant, a school district, seeking a declaratory judgment that the compulsory fees charged by the district to their children, who attended a school in the district, violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Minn. Const. art. VIII, §§ 1 and 2, and Minn. Stat. §§ 120.06 and 123.35. The St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota) granted the district's motion for summary judgment. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court's order was issued, Minn. Stat. §§ 120.72, 120.73, and 120.74 were enacted but had not yet taken effect. Minn. Stat. § 120.72 provided that public school education was free and that no pupil would be denied an education because of economic inability. Minn. Stat. § 120.73 provided what fees could be charged. Minn. Stat. § 120.74 listed those areas for which a fee could not be charged. The court held that the trial court's decision was an improper advisory opinion without a determination of what practices were actually followed under current regulations. Minn. Stat. §§ 120.72, 120.73 and 120.74 would render moot many of the issues. The parents did not establish that they financially were unable to pay the fees and, thus, a class action on behalf of all indigent persons was not appropriate. On remand, the court suggested that the Minnesota Attorney General and the Minnesota Department of Education should be joined as proper, if not necessary, parties. There was no way of determining the actual operation of the policy prescribed by Minn. Stat. § 120.73, subd. 4 allowing school board's to waive fees or if the parents had been denied access to any activities.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

436 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Beach


Nos. 45529, 45530, 45531


Supreme Court of Minnesota


304 Minn. 302; 231 N.W.2d 75; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1423



June 6, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals by the state from orders of the Ramsey County District Court, Ronald E. Hachey, Judge, suppressing certain evidence in three criminal prosecutions, one against Wesley Beach and two against Thomas Hooker Fuller, all on charges of bribery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged orders of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted the motion to suppress that defendants filed in the trial in which they were being prosecuted on charges of bribery pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 609.42, subd. 1.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the tapes that defendants sought to suppress were not statements "in writing" under Minn. Stat. § 611.033 and that it was wrong to suppress the tapes and the transcripts on the ground that their use at the trial would have violated § 611.033. The court affirmed the portion of the district court's judgment that ordered that the tapes be suppressed as direct evidence, reversed the portion of the judgment that prohibited the witness from testifying and from using the tapes to refresh his memory, and awarded attorneys fees to each defendant. The court reasoned that the weight of authority seemed to find that tapes were functionally similar to writings in all important respects and found that it was irrelevant that the investigator for the Legislative Audit Commission that made the tapes was not a law enforcement official because the language of § 611.033 did not indicate that it only applied to law enforcement agencies. The court also held that § 611.033 did not bar using the tapes to refresh the investigator's recollection, noting that the suppression was only statutorily based and did not implicate the constitutional fruit of the poisonous tree doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the suppression order that barred using the tapes and the transcripts as direct evidence against defendants, reversed the portion of the order that barred the witness from testifying and from using the tapes to refresh his memory. The court also awarded attorneys fees to each defendant.

 

437 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. Haule


No. 44989


Supreme Court of Minnesota


304 Minn. 160; 230 N.W.2d 51; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1405



May 16, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the St. Louis County District Court brought on behalf of Pauline C. Peterson, a minor, by Richard A. Peterson, her father and natural guardian, for personal injuries allegedly sustained by said minor, and by the father individually for consequential damages, all arising out of an accident on premises owned and operated by defendant Duane Haule, d.b.a. Chisholm Dairy Queen, and constructed by defendant International Dairy Queen. The case was tried before N. S. Chanak, Judge, and a jury. On the basis of a special verdict, the court ordered judgment for plaintiffs for $ 36,000 and $ 2,285.15 respectively. Defendants appealed from an order denying their alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a storeowner and the designer of the store, appealed from an order of the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota) denying their alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV) or for a new trial in the negligence action of plaintiffs, an injured patron and her father.


OVERVIEW: The patron, a 10-year old child, suffered injuries when she walked into an unmarked plate glass door at the subject store. The door had been constructed according to a design furnished by the designer. Plaintiffs filed a complaint against defendants. After trial, the jury's answers to the questions on the special verdict forms were inconsistent. The next day, the jury submitted questions for the trial court. The trial court changed an instruction on whether the patron was negligent and resubmitted the case to the jury. The jury then changed their answers to two questions. Based on the modified special verdict forms, judgment was rendered for plaintiffs and the judgment for the patron was reduced by the amount of her own negligence. Defendants filed a motion for JNOV or for a new trial, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed the order. The patron's claim was not defeated by her own negligence because defendants' negligence was considerably greater. The store was a public building within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 299G.11. Section 299G.11 was not unconstitutionally vague. It was proper to resubmit the case to the jury under the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Federal Distillers, Inc. v. State


Nos. 44831, 44837, 44844, 44832, 44833, 44834


Supreme Court of Minnesota


304 Minn. 28; 229 N.W.2d 144; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1390



May 2, 1975 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals Dismissed sub nom. Griggs, Cooper & Co. Inc. v. Novak and Heaven Hill Distilleries, Inc. v. Novak, 423 U.S. 908, 96 S. Ct. 209, 210, 46 L. ed. 2d 137 (1975).


PRIOR HISTORY: Six appeals, by Ed Phillips & Sons Company (44831), Old Peoria Company, Inc. (44832), Heaven Hill Distillers, Inc. (44833), National Distillers & Chemical Corporation (44834), Griggs, Cooper & Co., Inc. (44837), and Federal Distillers, Inc., Mr. Boston Distiller Corporation, and Johnson Brothers Wholesale Liquor Company (44844), from an order of the Ramsey County District Court, Harold W. Schultz, Judge, denying motions for a new trial in actions brought against the State of Minnesota and Joseph Novak, liquor control commissioner, which actions were tried together and resulted in findings that a statute regulating distribution and sale of liquor by licensed distillers and wholesalers, challenged by appellants as unconstitutional, was valid and enforceable.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, distillers and wholesalers, challenged a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which ruled in favor of defendants, the State and the Minnesota Liquor Control Commissioner, and held that Minn. Stat. § 340.114 was constitutional in all respects.


OVERVIEW: The distillers and wholesalers contended that Minn. Stat. § 340.114 unconstitutionally infringed upon their existing rights in the liquor distribution system, was overbroad, discriminated between types of alcohol, and improperly criminalized distribution practices. The court affirmed the trial court's decision in favor of the State and the Commissioner upholding the validity of § 340.114 because: (1) the statute was enacted pursuant to police power granted to the State by the Twenty-First Amendment; (2) there was no vested right in the liquor distribution system existing prior to the statute's enactment; (3) the statute regulated private conduct for the public benefit of promoting competition and preventing monopolies; and (4) it was not the judiciary's role to substitute its social and economic beliefs for the state legislature's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that the statute was constitutional.

 

439 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hampton v. Hampton


No. 45059


Supreme Court of Minnesota


303 Minn. 500; 229 N.W.2d 139; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1562



April 18, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff husband from an order of the Ramsey County District Court, Otis H. Godfrey, Jr., Judge, denying his motion for a rehearing after he was denied modification of a divorce decree with regard to payment of child support. Considered and decided by the court without oral argument.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father appealed from the order of the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota) denying his motion for rehearing after denying his motion to modify a divorce decree with regard to payment of child support to defendant mother. The father also appealed from the trial court's judgment holding him in contempt for failing to pay child support and alimony.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother were divorced. The divorce decree awarded custody of their minor child to the mother and ordered the father to pay alimony. The father was also ordered to pay child support until the child turned 21. One month before the child turned 18, the father stopped his payments of alimony and child support. The mother sought to hold the father in contempt, and the father filed a motion to modify the decree to reflect the child's emancipation. The trial court denied the father's motion to modify, found him to be in contempt of court, and denied his motion for rehearing. The court ruled that 1973 Minn. Laws 725, § 74, which lowered the age of majority from 21 to 18, did not apply retroactively to decrees that had previously been entered. However, the court stated that contempt was not available to enforce payments of accrued child support after the child reached the age of majority. The court also concluded that contempt should not be invoked to enforce the payment of support after the child turned 18 because that was contrary to legislative policy as expressed in the statute, although the decree was valid as between the parties and enforceable by ordinary remedies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order in part and reversed that part of the trial court's order adjudging the father to be in contempt for failing to pay child support to the mother. The court remanded the case to allow the trial court to reconsider its contempt order as it related to alimony.

Bodin v. St. Paul


No. 44926


Supreme Court of Minnesota


303 Minn. 555; 227 N.W.2d 794; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1580



March 21, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Gerald Bodin and other law enforcement officers employed by defendant city seeking a declaratory judgment and other relief on the ground that the actions of the city, its civil service commission, and its chief of police regarding job specifications were discriminatory. After findings for plaintiffs, Hyam Segell, Judge, defendants appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff detectives brought an action against defendant, the City of St. Paul, Minnesota, for equitable relief to increase their civil service ratings, contending that St. Paul, Minn., Ordinance 15277 violated St. Paul, Minn., City Charter ch. 12 and was an unconstitutional treatment of persons similarly situated. The Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) entered a judgment invalidating St. Paul, Minn., Ordinance 15277. The City appealed.


OVERVIEW: The City's police department had been organized into uniformed and plainclothes divisions, with the position of police lieutenant in the former and detective in the latter. Both were assigned the same civil service grade, though only the former acted in a supervisory capacity. The department was reorganized, creating the higher-ranked position of lieutenant and designating the positions of police lieutenant and detective for elimination. St. Paul, Minn., Ordinance 15277 was enacted to assign police lieutenants the same grade as lieutenants without a change in duties or responsibilities. The detectives' application for a grade increase was denied. The court held that St. Paul, Minn., Ordinance 15277 did not constitute a promotion without examination in violation of the merit system of St. Paul, Minn., City Charter ch. 12. There was no change in position under St. Paul, Minn., Ordinance 3520, §§ 2 and 28(c). The detectives did not overcome the presumption of constitutionality. The positions were not similarly situated, the distinctions were genuine and substantial given the police lieutenants' supervisory capacity, and the classification was germane and relevant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

Supreme Court of Minnesota


303 Minn. 256; 226 N.W.2d 910; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1526

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by James Scheer from orders of the Ramsey County District Court, John W. Graff, Judge, denying his motion to set aside service of a summons and complaint upon him in an action brought by plaintiff against him and two other defendants to recover the amount of a mortgage note which they had allegedly guaranteed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant guarantor challenged an order of the Ramsey District Court (Minnesota), which denied the motion to quash, vacate, and set aside the service of a summons and a complaint in plaintiff mortgagee's contract action that sought to enforce a guarantee on a mortgage.

Stat. § 543.19, subds. 1(b), 3. The court affirmed the denial of the guarantor's motion, concluding that exercising jurisdiction over the guarantor did not violate the traditional standards of fair play and substantial justice or the Due Process Clause. The court reasoned that the record clearly showed that the guarantor was "transacting business" within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 543.19, noting that he corresponded with persons in the state regarding the mortgaged developments and that he made trips to the state in connection with obtaining the mortgage and developing the realty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the guarantor's motion to quash, vacate, and set aside the service of a summons and a complaint in the mortgagee's contract action for the enforcement of the guarantee.

 

442 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hartle v. Glencoe


No. 44813


Supreme Court of Minnesota


303 Minn. 262; 226 N.W.2d 914; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1527



March 7, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding in the McLeod County District Court initiated by Darrel E. Hartle and others to set aside assessments levied against their property by the city of Glencoe for a sewer project. After findings for defendant city, John M. Fitzgerald, Judge, the property owners appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged the judgment of the McLeod County District Court (Minnesota), which upheld the assessments levied by respondent town against appellants property for a sewer project in appellants' action challenging the validity of the assessments.


OVERVIEW: When respondent extended sewer and water service to the new additions where appellants' property was located, it assessed their property for the improvements. Appellants challenged the validity of the assessments and sought to have them set aside on several grounds. The court affirmed the trial court's decision to uphold the assessments. Respondent was acting with the discretionary authority granted to it by Minn. Stat. § 429.031 in taking steps before the public hearing that included hiring an engineering firm, submitting a report on the adequacy of the waste treatment plant, applying for a federal grant, and entering into a contract concerning the intersection of the improvement project with a highway. A second hearing was not required because of a discrepancy between the estimated and actual assessments because the discrepancy was not related to an underestimate of the project cost. Respondent did not err in deferring the assessment of some areas until a time when they were connected. Finally, the assessment was less than the increase in the fair market value of appellants' property as a result of the improvement. Thus, the assessments were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that upheld the assessment levied by respondent for sewer and water improvements.

 

443 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. St. Paul


No. 45547


Supreme Court of Minnesota


303 Minn. 201; 227 N.W.2d 370; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1517



February 28, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court wherein plaintiff sought to temporarily enjoin defendant city from interfering with his operation of a theater without a license; to reverse the city's action in revoking his license; or to remand the matter to the city council for a new hearing on said revocation. The court, Hyam Segell, Judge, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff theatre owner sought review of an order from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant city in the theatre owner's suit seeking to temporarily enjoin the city from interfering with his business. The owner also sought review of the revocation of his license.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a city code, the theatre owner's license to operate his motion picture theatre was revoked because one of his employees was convicted of exhibiting an obscene motion picture. Such a conviction constituted grounds for revocation of the theatre owner's license under St. Paul, Minn., Legislative Code § 476.01. The theatre owner brought suit seeking to temporarily enjoin the city from interfering with his operations and to reverse the city's revocation of his license. The district court entered summary judgment in favor of the city. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the city code, under which the theatre owner's license had been revoked, was an unconstitutional prior restraint of free speech. The court held that the city code could have been upheld if it was established that the theatre owner's operation of the theater presented a clear and present danger of a substantive evil. The court held, however, that there was nothing to indicate that the operation of the theatre presented such a danger and therefore the city code was unconstitutional on its face.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order entering summary judgment in favor of the city in the theatre owner's action challenging the city's revocation of his license to operate his motion picture theatre.

 

444 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minneapolis v. Krebes


No. 44880


Supreme Court of Minnesota


303 Minn. 219; 226 N.W.2d 617; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1519



February 28, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by William Krebes from a judgment of the Hennepin County Municipal Court, Jonathan Lebedoff, Judge, whereby he was convicted of violation of an ordinance of the city of Minneapolis relating to fire prevention. Considered and decided by the court without oral argument.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant apartment owner appealed from an order of the Hennepin County Municipal Court (Minnesota) finding him guilty of violating Minneapolis, Minn. Code of Ordinances, § 643.010, by failure to comply with an order of the fire department.


OVERVIEW: The owner's three-story apartment building had two stairways; the rear stairway was enclosed and protected with fire doors. The fire department ordered the owner to enclose the front stairway and install fire doors, as required by the Fire Prevention Code, art. 643, § 1.5-f, which was incorporated by reference into the Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances, § 643.010. The owner argued that § 1.5-f should be narrowly construed, so that having one of the two stairwells enclosed and protected by fire doors was sufficient. Affirming, the court noted that an open stairway created a life-safety hazard by providing an open shaft for hot gases and smoke to rise, thus enhancing the possibility of death to those on the higher floors. The court rejected the owner's proposed narrow reading of § 1.5. The owner also argued that the provisions of the fire prevention code were unconstitutionally vague; however, the court held that the language "lack of adequate exit facilities or any other hazardous condition" was sufficiently definite. The court rejected the owner's contention that the city's fire prevention code was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Midland Glass Co. v. Shakopee


No. 44687


Supreme Court of Minnesota


303 Minn. 134; 226 N.W.2d 324; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1509



February 21, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Scott County District Court for a declaratory judgment invalidating as unconstitutional certain ordinances of defendant city, for an injunction against said city and defendant Northern States Power Company to prevent collection of a surcharge under said ordinances, and for damages. The court, John M. Fitzgerald, Judge, granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment, reserving for trial certain issues as to damages, and defendant power company appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant power company challenged a judgment of the Scott County District Court (Minnesota), which declared Shakopee, Minn. Ord. 337, § IV, which granted the power company a service franchise, void.


OVERVIEW: In a dispute over a utility surcharge, the trial court determined that the surcharge was so intertwined with the franchise granted to the power company in Ord. 337, § IV that it rendered the whole section void. On review, the court reversed the trial court's ruling in part. The court applied stature interpretation canons in presuming a statute's constitutionality. The court held that, while the surcharge was constitutionally invalid, the remainder of the statute was sufficiently removed from the unconstitutional surcharge that § IV was not invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's holding in part, and declared that only the portion of § IV that imposed a seven-percent surcharge was void. The court held that the remainder of the ordinance was constitutionally valid.

Monk & Excelsior, Inc. v. Minnesota State Board of Health

Supreme Court of Minnesota


302 Minn. 502; 225 N.W.2d 821; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1609



January 17, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Monk and Excelsior, Inc., Martin J. Hellman, and Rudy Luther against the State Board of Health, its officers, and certain employees to determine whether a statute requiring persons planning to construct a health care facility to obtain a certificate of need therefor applied to a nursing home plaintiffs planned to construct. Alternatively plaintiffs challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The court, Leslie L. Anderson, retired judge, having determined that the statute was valid and that defendants had properly applied it, plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs nursing home builders sought review of a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, which determined, in a declaratory judgment action, that they were required to obtain a certificate of need before constructing their nursing home.


OVERVIEW: The nursing home builders consisted of a corporation and two individuals. After hiring architects, drawing up plans, and negotiating with the Minnesota Department of Health for over one year, the nursing home filed an action for declaratory judgment to determine whether they were required under Minn. the Minnesota Certificate of Need Act, Minn. On appeal, the court ruled that the nursing home builders were excluded from the purview of the Certificate of Need Act because they had developed their project to a sufficient degree prior to the effective date thereof. The court went on in its opinion to chastise the Department of Health for delaying the nursing home builders' application for a license and the manner in which they dealt with the nursing home builders.

447 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Welfare of C. v. State


No. 45033


Supreme Court of Minnesota


302 Minn. 387; 225 N.W.2d 245; 1975 Minn. LEXIS 1597



January 3, 1975 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by a juvenile defendant from an order of the Hennepin County District Court, Lindsay G. Arthur, Judge, that he be referred for prosecution as an adult on a charge of aggravated robbery.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile was charged by petition in juvenile court with delinquency for aggravated robbery. The juvenile court referee granted a motion to refer the juvenile to the district court for adult prosecution, and on appeal the referral was affirmed by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota). The juvenile sought review of this decision.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was accused of the armed robbery of three persons. He was 17 years of age at the time; his criminal history dated from when he was 10. There was no program specifically designed for hard-core, sophisticated, aggressive delinquents; a psychologist testified that the existing programs were not stringent enough for the juvenile and that he was capable of killing someone. The court held that the reasons assigned by the juvenile court for reference to adult prosecution, the lack of an appropriate rehabilitative program, fell short of the statutory requirement of Minn. Stat. § 260.125, subd. 2(d). The absence of rehabilitative facilities did not necessarily mean he was not amenable to treatment as a juvenile. However, the record was not adequate to permit the court to decide whether the juvenile could insist upon treatment as a juvenile before being referred for adult prosecution. The court instructed the juvenile court to inquire whether there was a potential treatment program, whether one could be created, and if so, why there was not one.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of referral and remanded the case to the trial court for further findings regarding available rehabilitation programs.

Blue Earth County Welfare Dep't v. Cabellero


No. 44743


Supreme Court of Minnesota


302 Minn. 329; 225 N.W.2d 373; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1193



December 20, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal to the Blue Earth County District Court by the welfare department of said county from a decision of the commissioner of the State Department of Public Welfare promulgating certain regulations with respect to public assistance grants. After a hearing wherein Juana Cabellero and other recipients appeared, the court, Noah S. Rosenbloom, Judge, made findings reversing the commissioner, and the recipients and the state appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, welfare recipients and the state welfare department, challenged a judgment of the Blue Earth County District Court (Minnesota), which reversed a decision of the state commissioner of public welfare that required respondent county welfare board to comply with the Second Brooke Amendment on the grounds that his order was unreasonable within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 256.77, subd. 3 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The county welfare agency refused to comply with the state commissioner of public welfare's order to abide by the Second Brooke Amendment, which excluded from the definition of low-rent housing those units the rents of which exceeded one-fourth of the tenant-family's income. The trial court reversed the commissioner's order, holding that the Amendment violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court reversed and reinstated the commissioner's order. While there was doubt whether the county welfare agency had standing to challenge the Amendment's constitutionality, the question was sufficiently doubtful so that the court agreed to resolve the doubt in favor of a decision on the merits. Applying a liberal rational basis test, the court concluded that the Amendment did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because it did not result in any recipient receiving welfare benefits at a level in excess of established need. It was much more difficult to make a showing of invidious discrimination where there was no alleged denial of welfare benefits, but rather an alleged overpayment. The Amendment was entitled to a presumption of constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and instructed the trial court to reinstate the decision of the state commissioner of public welfare.

 

449 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Lappegaard


No. 44329


Supreme Court of Minnesota


302 Minn. 266; 224 N.W.2d 504; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1181



December 6, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Dakota County District Court to test the validity of a statute which requires plaintiff to pay an additional registration fee for his tractor-trailer. Raymond Lappegaard, commissioner of highways, and Wallace R. Hoaglund, commissioner of public safety, were named as defendants. The court, Robert J. Breunig, Judge, denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and granted defendant Lappegaard's motion for dismissal of the action. Plaintiff appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed an order from the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota),which granted defendant commissioner of highways' motion for dismissal of the owner's action for a declaratory judgment that Minn. Stat. § 168.013 (1971) violated the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution and for an injunction.


OVERVIEW: One of the owner's truck tractors weighed in excess of its registered weight while operating in the state. The owner was issued a citation pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 168.013 for the excess weight, to which the owner pleaded guilty and paid a fine. The owner also received a notice of registration violation that required him to increase the registered weight of the truck pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 168.013, subd. 3 (1971) and pay and increased registration fee. The owner paid the fee and then brought a declaratory judgment action alleging that § 168.013 was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the owner's motion for summary judgment and granted the commissioner's motion to dismiss the action. The appellate court affirmed. The court held that § 168.013 was constitutional on its face because the State was merely seeking a return for the privilege, already exercised, of using its highways at the weight on which the increased license fee was based. The court held that the tax was not an undue burden on interstate commerce. The tax did not violate due process even though the owner's truck could not operate at the increased weight because that weight violated federal law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the owner's declaratory judgment action.

Minnesota Civil Liberties Union v. State


No. 43978


Supreme Court of Minnesota


302 Minn. 216; 224 N.W.2d 344; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1177



November 26, 1974 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied, 421 U.S. 988, 95 S. Ct. 1990, 1991, 44 L. ed. 2d 477 (1975).


PRIOR HISTORY: Two actions consolidated for trial in the Ramsey County District Court, challenging the validity of L. 1971, c. 944, which permits parents to credit against their state income tax a portion of the costs of educating their children in nonpublic schools and to receive payment of the amount by which the credit exceeded their tax. One action was commenced by Minnesota Civil Liberties Union, Americans United for Separation of Church and State, and certain individuals against the state, certain state officials, and various officials of parochial and other private schools. The other action was commenced by the Minnesota Coordinating Committee for Public Education and numerous other organizations and individuals against the state, the commissioner of taxation, the commissioner of education, the state treasurer, and the state auditor. Two groups of individuals were permitted to intervene as defendants. The court, J. Jerome Plunkett, Judge, found the statute valid, and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered and from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, Minnesota Civil Liberties Union and other concerned groups and individuals, appealed the determination of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which held that 197 Minn. Laws ch. 944 was constitutional. The law permitted parents to credit against state income tax part of the costs of educating their children at nonpublic schools.


OVERVIEW: Defendant state enacted 1971 Minn. Laws ch. 944 which allowed parents to credit against their state income tax part of the costs of educating their children at nonpublic schools. Plaintiffs challenged the law as unconstitutional violation of the separation of church and state. The trial court held that the law was constitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court. The court based its decision on United State Supreme Court decisions made since the trial court ruled. The court held that the law had as its primary effect the advancement of religion. Under a three-part standard for analyzing Establishment Clause questions, a law must have a secular legislative purpose, the law's primary effect cannot advance or inhibit religion, and the law must no foster excessive governmental entanglement with religion. Because the law offered unrestricted cash payments to parents for sending their children to sectarian schools, the Establishment Clause was violated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

New Ulm Bldg. Center, Inc. v. Studtmann


No. 44417


Supreme Court of Minnesota


302 Minn. 14; 225 N.W.2d 4; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1154



November 1, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Nicollet County District Court to foreclose a mechanics lien for materials allegedly furnished by plaintiff for the construction of a house for defendants Willmar Studtmann and Lillian M. Studtmann, in which action William F. Forbrook intervened, also claiming a lien. After findings, L. J. Irvine, Judge, establishing the priority of the various liens claimed and determining that a cross-claim filed by defendants Studtmann against the intervenor should be dismissed, defendants Studtmann and Citizens State Bank of New Ulm, a mortgage holder, appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial. Plaintiff and intervenor filed a notice of review of court's order denying their motion for change in interest awarded.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent lienholders pursued an action against appellant homeowners in the Nicollet County District Court (Minnesota) to foreclose mechanics liens. The trial court established the priority of various liens on their property, dismissed the homeowners' cross-claim against an intervenor, and denied the homeowners' motion for a new trial. The homeowners sought review of the trial court's denial of their motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the homeowners' motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, holding that the charges made by the lienholders were reasonable. The court concluded that, although they did not give express authorization for them, the homeowners were aware that extras were being included as the work on their home progressed. The court found that the homeowners' failure to make a timely objection to the extras constituted a waiver. The court reversed the trial court's decision in part, holding that the trial court's award of attorneys fees was excessive under the formula set forth in Minn. Stat. § 582.01. The court further held that the trial court erred in determining the date from which interest was calculated. The court concluded that the amount of interest had to be recomputed to permit interest from the date the notice of the filing of the liens was served until the date of payment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to the extent that it determined the value of the extras for which the homeowners were liable. The court reversed the trial court's decision to the extent that it calculated the amount of attorneys fees and interest to which the lienholders were entitled.

 

452 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reps


No. 44125


Supreme Court of Minnesota


302 Minn. 38; 223 N.W.2d 780; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1158; 78 A.L.R.3d 548



November 1, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendant, charged in the Wabasha County District Court with violation of Minn. St. 514.02, moved for dismissal of the information on the grounds it did not state a public offense. The court, Glenn E. Kelley, Judge, certified questions relating to the constitutionality of the statute as important and doubtful.



DISPOSITION: Questions certified answered in the negative and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a contractor, was charged with violating Minn. Stat. § 514.02 by receiving proceeds for improvements to real estate without either using the proceeds to pay the costs of the improvements, furnishing a valid lien waiver, or furnishing a payment bond. After defendant filed a motion to dismiss the information, a number of questions regarding the statute's constitutionality were certified to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was hired by a homeowner to make improvements on her property. He was charged with not paying outstanding bills for materials used by him as contractor. The court first held that § 514.02, subd. 1, was not repugnant to Minn. Const. art. 1, § 12, prohibiting imprisonment for debt. It held that the statute imposed a trust character on the payments made to a contractor, and it was a knowing violation of the trust, rather than a failure to pay a debt, that the statute made punishable. It held that the statute did not violate equal protection in that it applied equally to all persons who were similarly situated. Finally, the court held that the statute did not create an invalid presumption in stating that unless the contractor established that the proceeds had been used to pay costs, proof that the costs were unpaid would be sufficient to sustain a finding that the proceeds were used for a purpose other than for the payment of costs. The court stated that the fact that defendant had paid over the proceeds was more easily proven by defendant than by the State, and the burden of producing such evidence was not unfair.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions, which asked whether the statute violated various constitutional provisions, in the negative. It remanded the case.

Blue v. Loxton


No. 44106


Supreme Court of Minnesota


301 Minn. 428; 223 N.W.2d 129; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1277; 4 Collier Bankr. Cas. (MB) 820



October 25, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court to recover for property damage and personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff when his automobile was struck by an automobile owned by defendant Jim G. Loxton, also known as James G. Loxton, and driven by defendant Mary Beth Loxton. Defendants moved for summary judgment on the ground that plaintiff's claim had been discharged in bankruptcy proceedings. The court, Crane Winton, Judge, denied defendants' motion, holding that plaintiff's claim had been revived in the amount of two bonds filed by defendants pursuant to the Safety Responsibility Act. Following trial, the court, Bruce C. Stone, Judge, found that the accident resulted from the negligence of defendant Mary Beth Loxton and that plaintiff had sustained total damages of $ 1,060. Accordingly, the court ordered judgment in plaintiff's favor for $ 945, the amount of the bonds. Defendants appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a husband and wife, appealed from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) entered in favor of plaintiff driver for damages resulting from an automobile accident. Defendants had discharged this debt in bankruptcy, but the driver was awarded the amount of bonds they executed pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 170.27(1) in order to reinstate their driving privileges.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to defendants' execution of the bonds, the United States Supreme Court struck down a statute similar to Minn. Stat. § 170.33 subd. 5, under which a discharge did not relieve individuals from the requirement of posting a bond in lieu of proof of financial responsibility pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 170.25 (1). The district court held that by executing the bonds, defendants revived the discharged debt to the driver. On appeal, the court reversed. The court noted that the reaffirmation of a discharged debt had to be clear, unequivocal and voluntary. The court found that defendants executed the bonds under duress, because of their need to reinstate their driver's licenses. The court also found it inequitable to enforce the bond obligation, which it found to be a violation of the Supremacy Clause. The court noted that the commissioner of highways no longer required the bonds, and defendants lacked the financial ability to challenge the constitutionality of § 170.33, subd. 5 rather than post the bonds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court judgment. .

 

454 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 44433


Supreme Court of Minnesota


301 Minn. 455; 223 N.W.2d 775; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1283



October 25, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Joseph D. Smith, convicted of driving after revocation of his driver's license in violation of a Minneapolis ordinance, from an order of the Hennepin County District Court, Irving C. Iverson, Judge, denying his petition for postconviction relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which imposed a sentence when defendant failed to make payments on his fine. The court also denied defendant's request for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving after revocation in violation of a municipal ordinance. The court imposed sentence in the alternative, which was either a fine or 30 days in jail. Defendant was ordered to serve the 30 days after defendant failed to pay his fines. Defendant argued that his imprisonment was unconstitutional because he was indigent. On appeal, the court affirmed. First, the court noted that defendant could seek postconviction relief, even though he had been convicted under a municipal ordinance, not a state statute. Second, the court held that the constitution prohibited the state from imposing a fine as a sentence and then automatically converting it into a jail term solely because defendant was indigent. There was no prohibition against incarceration where the failure to pay was due to contumacy rather than indigency. The evidence showed that defendant failed to use due diligence in attempting to find work and to pay the fines. Lastly, the court noted that defendant was allowed to participate in the programs contained in Minn. Stat. § 631.425, which provided assistance in attaining employment and for reduction in sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Morton v. Board of Comm'rs


No. 45366


Supreme Court of Minnesota


301 Minn. 415; 223 N.W.2d 764; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1276



October 22, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Leslie G. Morton and other taxpayers against the Board of Commissioners of Ramsey County and Ramsey County Hospital and Sanitarium Commission seeking an injunction to require defendant board to submit to qualified voters of the county at the next general election the questions of remodeling certain areas within St. Paul-Ramsey Hospital and of constructing and equipping an addition thereto in conjunction with the Gillette Hospital Authority, and also to restrain defendants from proceeding with the financing and construction of said improvements until approved by a majority of the electors voting thereon. The State of Minnesota and the Gillette Hospital Authority were permitted to intervene. Upon motions of the plaintiffs and of defendants for summary judgment and upon stipulated facts, the court, Stephen L. Maxwell, Judge, ordered summary judgment in favor of defendants and the intervenors but included in his order a finding that defendant board would be required to submit to the voters of Ramsey County the question of constructing said addition as to costs, including equipment, in excess of $ 5,600,000. Plaintiffs appealed [***2] from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed without approving the foregoing finding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted defendants, a board of commissioner's, a hospital's, a sanitarium commission's, the State of Minnesota's, and the hospital authority's, motion for summary judgment in the taxpayers' action seeking an injunction requiring the board to submit the issue of remodeling of the hospital to a vote in the general election.


OVERVIEW: By their action, the taxpayers sought to enjoin the construction of an addition to the hospital and to compel the board to submit the construction issue to the electorate. On appeal, the taxpayers argued that the trial court's order should be reversed because the pertinent state statutes were erroneously construed and applied unconstitutionally. Specifically, the taxpayers contended that the situation was controlled by Minn. Stat. §§ 376.009 to 376.07, which explicitly required submission of proposals for the purchase, erection, or construction of hospital buildings to a "vote of the people." However, defendants maintained that §§ 376.009 to 376.07 did not apply. Furthermore, they argued that 1974 Minn. Laws 581 provided that an election was not required with respect to the proposed construction. The court held that the trial court correctly concluded that 1974 Minn. Laws 581 justified defendants' action with respect to the bond issue and the hospital construction plans. Additionally, the court held that after a close review of the facts of this case, it found no denial of the taxpayers' due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Bethke v. County of Brown


No. 44569


Supreme Court of Minnesota


301 Minn. 380; 223 N.W.2d 757; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1271



October 18, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Upon the filing of petitions in the Brown County District Court by Marlys R. Bethke and Alton A. Bethke and by other property owners objecting to taxes for the year 1971, levied and assessed against their property in the city of New Ulm, and the severance of issues relating to the assessment procedures, the cases were consolidated for trial on such issues. Following trial, the court, L. J. Irvine, Judge, determined that for the year 1971 the assessments were discriminatory and ordered them vacated. The county and the city appealed from the judgment thereafter entered, and the petitioners filed a notice of review of the judgment and of an order denying their motion that said assessments be held void for the year 1972.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and county sought review of a judgment of the Brown County District Court (Minnesota), which held that the real estate taxes assessed against respondent taxpayers and payable in 1971 were null and void and of no effect. The taxpayers sought review of that portion of the judgment holding that the case was not applicable to the real estate taxes payable in 1972.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed an action against the city and county objecting to the taxes for the year 1971 levied and assessed against their property and the severance of issues relating to the assessment procedures. The trial court held that for the year 1971, the assessments were discriminatory and ordered them vacated. The city and county appealed and the taxpayers filed a notice of review of the judgment and order denying their motion that said assessments were to be held void for the year 1972. On appeal, the court agreed with the holding of the trial court that the revaluation of residential real estate for assessment purposes for the year 1971 constituted a systematic, arbitrary, and intentional overvaluation of the properties of the taxpayers in comparison to the other properties of the same class in the city and resulted in an unfair and discriminatory tax against the real estate of the taxpayers. Further, the court determined that the ruling as to the validity of the 1971 taxes did not extend to the 1972 taxes because the statutory proceedings under Minn. Stat. § 278.01 were the exclusive remedy of the taxpayer. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment holding that the 1971 real estate taxes were null and void was affirmed; the judgment holding that the case was not applicable to the real estate taxes payable in 1972 was affirmed.

State v. Solem

Supreme Court of Minnesota

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Thomas Arthur Solem, James Albert Russell, and Holiday Magic, Inc., from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Douglas K. Amdahl, Judge, whereby they were convicted of the crime of consumer fraud.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) convicting them of consumer fraud.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were general distributors of Holiday Magic products. As a result of their business practices, defendants were convicted of consumer fraud, or specifically, operating a multi-level distributorship in violation of Minn. Stat. § 325.79, subd. 2(2)(a). Defendants challenged their conviction contending that the statute upon which it was based was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. The court noted that the statute only prohibited sales tactics that resulted in pyramid or multi-level distributorships. Therefore, it was not overbroad. In addition, the statute clearly defined what conduct was considered illegal. Therefore, it was not vague. Defendants' conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Ebenezer Soc. v. Minnesota State Bd. of Health


No. 45175


Supreme Court of Minnesota


301 Minn. 188; 223 N.W.2d 385; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1243



September 13, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus in this court upon the relation of Minnesota State Board of Health to compel the Dakota County District Court, Lawrence L. Lenertz, Judge, to transfer to Hennepin County an action begun in Dakota County against petitioner by Ebenezer Society and Fairview Community Hospitals.



DISPOSITION: Let writ issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Minnesota State Board of Health sought a writ of mandamus to compel the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota) to change the venue of its dispute with respondent hospitals to a different county pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 542.03, or in the alternative Minn. Stat. §§ 542.09, 542.11. The Supreme Court of Minnesota issued an order to show cause why venue should not be changed and stayed the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Two hospitals brought an action against the Minnesota State Board of Health in which they sought injunctive and declaratory relief pursuant to the Minnesota Certificate of Need Act, Minn. Stat. § 145.71 et seq. The board requested a writ of mandamus to compel the trial court to change the venue of this dispute pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 542.03, or in the alternative, Minn. Stat. §§ 542.09, 542.11. The court initially issued an order that stayed the proceedings, but later discharged that order and granted the requested writ of mandamus. A petition for a writ of mandamus was an accepted practice to seek review of a venue order. Further, the court found that relief under Minn. Stat. § 542.03, which created a special venue for actions against public officers for acts done through their office, was appropriate because the board, as an entity comprised of individual public officers, was itself a public officer under that statute. Similarly, the initial action relied wholly upon the board's alleged actions and therefore the matter was within the purview of § 542.03. Finally, the court found that venue was properly placed in the county where all pertinent acts had transpired.


OUTCOME: The court discharged its order that stayed proceedings and issued the requested writ of mandamus.

Burnsville v. Onischuk


Nos. 44232, 44253


Supreme Court of Minnesota


301 Minn. 137; 222 N.W.2d 523; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1238



September 13, 1974 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Dismissed for Want of a Federal Question, 420 U.S. 916, 95 S. Ct. 1109, 43 L. ed. 2d 388 (1975).


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the Dakota County District Court brought by the village of Burnsville and Glen Northrup, a resident of said county and village, for a declaratory judgment invalidating Ex. Sess. L. 1971, c. 24, and enjoining its administration by defendants, Carl Onischuk, auditor of Dakota County, Lou McKenna, auditor of Ramsey County, Thomas Greeder, auditor of Washington County, Olaf Kaasa, finance director of Hennepin County, George Hickey, auditor of Hennepin County, Charles Lefebvre, auditor of Anoka County, William J. Schneider, auditor of Carver County, Joseph Notermann, auditor of Scott County, and Val Bjornson, treasurer of the state. Metropolitan Council intervened as a defendant. After findings for plaintiffs, Robert J. Breunig, Judge, the last four named defendants and intervenor appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, auditors from three counties, a state treasurer, and a council, appealed from the judgment of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which was entered in favor of respondents, a village and a resident, in their declaratory judgment action invalidating 1971 Minn. Sess. Law Serv. 24 and enjoining its administration.


OVERVIEW: The village brought a declaratory judgment suit against auditors of certain counties, a finance director, and a state treasurer. A village official joined as party plaintiff and council intervened as a party defendant. The trial court held that 1971 Minn. Sess. Law Serv. 24 was in violation of Minn. Const. art. 9, § 1. Appellants sought review and the court held that the village had no standing to attack the validity of the statute. The court stated that although the question was a close one, the village official's status was sufficient to give him standing in the proceedings. The court found the issues to be of unusual public concern. The court held that the statutory scheme for revenue sharing embodied in 1971 Minn. Sess. Law Serv. 24 reached a constitutional accommodation between the tax burdens imposed and the benefits derived therefrom to a degree which satisfied the requirements of the uniformity provisions of Minn. Const. art. 9, § 1. The presumption of constitutionality which the statute enjoyed was not overcome by any explicit demonstration that its application resulted in a hostile and oppressive discrimination against the residents of particular units of government.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that had invalidated a certain statute.

 

461 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Elwell v. County of Hennepin


No. 44303


Supreme Court of Minnesota


301 Minn. 63; 221 N.W.2d 538; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1226



August 23, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two petitions in the Hennepin County District Court by Laurance Elwell, Jr., to have certain real property in said county classified as agricultural land with respect to taxes payable in 1971, 1972, and 1973. After adverse findings, William D. Gunn, retired judge, the county appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged a decision from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which held that respondent landowner's petitions to have land classified as agricultural for purposes of the Green Acres Statute, Minn. Stat. § 273.111, should be granted. The county challenged the constitutionality of the statute and argued that, when the landowner did not farm the land but leased it for farming to others, the use was not agricultural.


OVERVIEW: A landowner petitioned the county to have his land classified as agricultural for purposes of the Green Acres Statute, Minn. Stat. § 273.111, which gave preferential tax treatment to farm land. The tax assessor denied the petitions; but the district court granted them. On appeal, the county attacked the constitutionality of the Green Acres Statute but gave no notice to the state attorney general under Minn. R. Civ. P. 24.04. The court first held that it had jurisdiction to consider the constitutional challenge despite the lack of notice, overruling its prior decision in In re Condemnation by Oak Center Creamery Co. v. Grobe, 264 Minn. 435, 119 N.W. 2d 729 (1963). The court then held that the Green Acres Statute was constitutional, because its classifications of land according to use were reasonable. The Green Acres Statute did not offend either Minn. Const. art. IX, § 1 or the Fourteenth Amendment, which extended identical equal protection guarantees. Finally, the fact that the landowner did not farm the land himself but leased it to someone else who farmed it did not mean that the use of the land was not agricultural. The cash rental income qualified as production income.


OUTCOME: The court overruled In re Condemnation by Oak Center Creamery Co. v. Grobe and held that failure to notify the attorney general about a constitutional challenge to a statute did not deprive the appellate court of jurisdiction to consider it. The court affirmed the district court's decision to uphold the constitutionality of the Green Acres Statute and its application in this case.

Snyder's Drug Stores, Inc. v. Minnesota State Board of Pharmacy


No. 44624


Supreme Court of Minnesota


301 Minn. 28; 221 N.W.2d 162; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1219



August 9, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Snyder's Drug Stores, Inc., against the Minnesota State Board of Pharmacy challenging one of its regulations. The Minnesota State Pharmaceutical Association and its officers were permitted to intervene. Thereafter, the court, Hyam Segell, Judge, denied an application by the Minnesota Public Interest Research Group and Metropolitan Senior Citizens Federation to intervene, and they appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action brought by appellant drug retailer to challenge the validity of a regulation adopted by respondent board, the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) entered an order that denied the motions of appellant interest groups to intervene in the action. The interest groups sought review of that order.


OVERVIEW: The board issued a regulation that prohibited pharmacists from advertising retail prices of prescription drugs. The drug retailer alleged that the regulation violated due process of law, imposed an unconstitutional burden on interstate commerce, and was in excess of the board's statutory authority. The trial court permitted two organizations and its officers to intervene as defendants. The interest groups sought to intervene as parties plaintiff. The trial court denied the motions of the interest groups, and the court reversed and remanded. The court held that as groups that represented consumers, particularly elderly consumers who purchase a disproportionate share of prescription drugs, the interest groups had standing to intervene in the action. It also ruled that the trial court erred in not permitting the groups to intervene pursuant to Minn. R. Civ. P. 24.02 where they raised questions of law and fact common to those present in the primary litigation. The court also noted that, absent intervention by the interest groups, the parties on both sides of the action represented exclusively the interests of retail sellers of prescription drugs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order denying the motions of the interest groups to intervene.

Hughes v. Patrick & Associates

Supreme Court of Minnesota

Lynch, Judge, found in favor of defendant lien claimant, Krause Construction, Inc., and in favor of defendant landowners, John Milton and Mary Ann Milton, on their third-party complaint against Jack H. Boekhoff, d.b.a. Doran Development Company. Defendants Milton appealed from the judgment entered pursuant to stipulation, which judgment provided for attorneys' fees for the lien claimant.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners challenged a judgment from the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), awarding appellee lienholder attorney fees under Minn. Stat. § 514. 14. The homeowners were also awarded judgment against appellee development company, including attorney fees.

Nos. 44064, 44368


Supreme Court of Minnesota


300 Minn. 244; 219 N.W.2d 912; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1331



June 21, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals by plaintiff wife arising out of a divorce action in the Ramsey County District Court, one from an order, Sidney P. Abramson, Judge, denying her motion to have the report of the referee modified, rejected, or recommitted, and one from an order, James M. Lynch, Judge, denying a similar motion. Thereafter, Warren Spannaus, attorney general, intervened for the purposes of defending the constitutionality of a statute.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former wife appealed an order from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which refused consent for the former wife to remove the child to another state. The former wife also appealed an order that suspended the alimony and support provisions of the parties' divorce decree as long as she remained outside of the state and denied defendant former husband his visitation rights.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders against the former wife in part as to the denial of consent to remove the child to another state and the suspension of the alimony provision. The court vacated the second order in part and remanded the case with respect to the suspension of the former husband's obligation to pay child support.

Carpenter v. Mattison


No. 44283


Supreme Court of Minnesota


300 Minn. 273; 219 N.W.2d 625; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1334



June 21, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Polk County District Court for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff when he was operating his snowmobile and was struck by one driven by defendant. The case was tried before Harley G. Swenson, Judge, and a jury, which found that both parties were causally negligent, that their negligence contributed 25 percent and 75 percent respectively, that plaintiff did not assume the risk of injury, and that plaintiff's damages amounted to $ 32,500. Defendant appealed from an order denying his alternative motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, a new trial on the issue of liability only, or for a new trial on all issues.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant snowmobile driver sought review of the judgment of the Polk County District Court (Minnesota), which, after a jury trial, denied defendant's motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and for a new trial and entered judgment in favor of plaintiff snowmobile driver in an action for personal injuries arising out of a collision between the parties.


OVERVIEW: The parties were travelling in a group of snowmobilers when defendant increased his speed and hit a slope, causing him to leave the ground and collide with plaintiff. A jury awarded damages to plaintiff, finding defendant 25 percent negligent. The trial court denied defendant's post-trial motions. The court held that: (1) the jury had ample evidence to conclude that defendant was not traveling at the same rate of speed as the rest of the group; (2) the terms "unsafe" and "harassing" in Minn. Stat. § 84.87, subd. 2, were not unconstitutionally vague; (3) plaintiff was not guilty of assumption of risk as a matter of law because there was conflicting evidence as to whether he had his feet on his running board at the time of the collision; (4) lay opinion as to the speed of defendant's snowmobile was admissible; (5) defendant, by offering a pretrial statement into evidence, waived his right to object to the content of the statement when offered against him when he failed to request a limiting instruction; and (6) Minn. Dist. Ct. Rules part I., R. 11 and Minn. Stat. § 357.25 did not prohibit the trial court from allowing expert witnesses' fees in excess of $ 100 per day.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Stillwater v. Minnesota Municipal Com.


Nos. 44415, 44500


Supreme Court of Minnesota


300 Minn. 211; 219 N.W.2d 82; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1328



May 31, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] The town of Stillwater and H. Clay Newman brought an action for a declaratory judgment in the Washington County District Court seeking to invalidate an order of the Minnesota Municipal Commission which granted the petition of the city of Stillwater to annex certain lands. The village of Oak Park Heights and Ramona Canfield and other individuals were permitted to file complaints in intervention. The court, William T. Johnson, Judge, in two orders denied the commission's motions for dismissal and certified the question presented to be important and doubtful, and the commission and the city appealed from said orders.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Minnesota Municipal Commission (commission) sought review of an order of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota) that denied its motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim upon which relief could have been granted and certified the question presented. Plaintiff town had brought an action for a declaratory judgment that sought to invalidate the commission's grant of defendant town's petition to annex certain lands.


OVERVIEW: The proceedings concerned two petitions requesting annexation of certain lands in the town to the city. Before the Commission had completed hearings and issued all final orders in response the town commenced an action in the district court for declaratory judgment against the Commission. The relief sought was to invalidate the orders of annexation and to enjoin further pending proceedings. The district court denied the Commission's pretrial motion for dismissal of the declaratory judgment action and certified the question as to whether a declaratory judgment action pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 555 was available as an alternative remedy to challenge Commission annexation proceedings. The court reversed. Absent extraordinary circumstances, such as claims of fraud or conspiracy between the Commission and an annexing entity, the court held that the statutory review authorized by Minn. Stat. § 414.07, subd. 2, constituted the exclusive method of judicial review of annexation proceedings requiring Commission approval. The court stated that its dismissal of the action did not preclude the district court from remanding to the Commission to allow a rehearing under its rules.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and ordered dismissal of the action for declaratory judgment but did not preclude the district court, in the pending statutory review proceedings and upon proper request by any party, from remanding the proceedings to the Commission to allow a rehearing under its rules.
