Appeal of O'Rourke


Nos. 44565, 44575, 44622


Supreme Court of Minnesota


300 Minn. 158; 220 N.W.2d 811; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1323



May 24, 1974 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing 300 Minn. 158 at 182.


PRIOR HISTORY: There petitions to this court, one (No. 44565) by Kathleen Sharpe O'Rourke for permission to appeal from an order of the Dakota County District Court, John M. Fitzgerald, Judge, affirming an order of the probate court of that county; one (No. 44575) by Theresa M. O'Rourke for permission to appeal from the same order; and one (No. 44622) by Harvey Stolp for permission to appeal from an order of the Anoka County District Court, Robert B. Gillespie, Judge, which affirmed an order of the Anoka County County Court denying his motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial after trial of an action brought by him against Marie Scrimshaw arising out of an automobile accident had resulted in a jury verdict assessing Stolp's causal negligence as 80 percent and defendant Scrimshaw's causal negligence as 20 percent.



DISPOSITION: Petitions denied. Upon petition for reargument, leave to appeal granted in No. 44565 and No. 44575.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three appellants had filed petitions for leave to appeal from decisions of various district courts (Minnesota), which acted in an appellate capacity upon matters that were initiated and tried in county courts as provided by the County Court Act, Minn. Stat. § 487. The court raised the issue of the propriety of the court's discretionary act of granting or denying these applications for leave to appeal and the validity of the County Court Act.


OVERVIEW: The court addressed the question raised by appellants, in their unrelated petitions for review, of appellants' right to appeal and the court's obligation toward to those appeals with respect to the County Court Act. The court held that the Minnesota Constitution did not guarantee appellants a right of appeal and that the right of appeal was governed by statute. The court stated that the legislative regulation over the appellate authority of the court was designed to aid the court in its exercise of its appellate functions and had not abrogated the constitutionally independent appellate authority to review whatever the court deemed mandated in the interests of justice. The court held that the County Court Act had not violated the Minnesota Constitution. The court found that three counties that were allowed to appeal directly to the court under the County Court Act was not discriminatory and was not a denial of equal protection because the Equal Protection Clause related to equality between persons rather than areas, and no person was being denied their appellate rights by the County Court Act.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitions.

Kindt v. Yellow Cab of Winona, Inc.


No. 44362


Supreme Court of Minnesota


300 Minn. 190; 218 N.W.2d 459; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1325



May 24, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Winona County District Court to recover for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff Ethel Kindt when an automobile, driven by her and owned by plaintiff Edward Kindt, collided with one owned by defendant Yellow Cab of Winona, Inc., and driven by defendant James Hurley Kreisel. Plaintiff Edward Kindt sought recovery for property damage and consequential damages for his wife's injuries. Defendants counterclaimed for property damage. The case was tried before Glenn E. Kelley, Judge, and a jury, which found in a special verdict that both drivers were causally negligent, that their negligence contributed to the accident 60 percent and 40 percent respectively. Plaintiffs appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, owner and motorist, appealed from an order of the District Court of Winona County (Minnesota) denying their motion for a new trial in their action against defendants, taxicab owner and driver, for damages allegedly caused by the cab driver's negligence, in which defendants counterclaimed, alleging that the motorist's negligence was the sole cause of the accident.


OVERVIEW: At the close of the evidence in the trial of the action of the owner and motorist for damages allegedly caused by the cab driver's negligence, the trial judge told plaintiffs' counsel that, if counsel for either party asked to have the jury instructed on the effects of answers to the interrogatories he would allow the parties' counsel to argue the effects of the verdict, but he would advise the jury that plaintiffs would recover nothing if it apportioned more than 50 percent of the negligence to the motorist. Plaintiffs' counsel thereupon withdrew his request for the instruction. After the jury returned a verdict, finding that the motorist was 60 percent negligent, plaintiffs moved for a new trial on the ground that the trial court failed to explain to the jury the legal conclusions that would follow from their special findings. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying the motion. Having made a decision to withdraw their request for the instruction, plaintiffs' counsel could not complain on appeal that failure to give the instruction was error.


OUTCOME: The trial court was affirmed.

 

469 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnesota Board of Barber Examiners v. Laurance


No. 44357


Supreme Court of Minnesota


300 Minn. 203; 218 N.W.2d 692; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1327



May 24, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought by the Minnesota Board of Barber Examiners to enjoin Jack Laurance, individually and d.b.a. Laurance International Coiffures, from practicing barbering without a license. After findings for defendant, Eugene Minenko, Judge, plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered and from an order denying its alternative motion to amend its complaint or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Minnesota Board of Barber Examiners appealed a judgment from the Hennepin County District Court, Minnesota, that found in favor of defendant cosmetologist and denied the Board's request for an injunction to prevent the cosmetologist from practicing barbering without a license. The Board's post-trial alternative motion to amend its complaint to seek declaratory relief or for a new trial was also denied.


OVERVIEW: The cosmetologist had cut the hair of males, an activity that was limited exclusively to licensed barbers under Minn. Stat. §§ 154.02, 154.07. Under Minn. Stat. § 155.02, subd. 2, licensed cosmetologists could only cut the hair of women. There was no statutory standard or other satisfactory evidence to show that licensed cosmetologists were not qualified to cut men's hair. In regards to health and safety factors, there was no evidence to show that the cutting of men's hair by a licensed cosmetologist would create a danger to the public or that the sanitation requirements under either licensing procedure were harmful to the general health and welfare. The court found that the classification scheme was unconstitutional. U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV and Minn. Const. art. I, § 7 guaranteed the liberty of contract to render services in any lawful calling. The State's exercise of police power to regulate in this area had to be rationally related to the promotion of the public health, safety, and welfare. Minn. Stat. § 155.02, subd. 2, which limited cosmetologists to the trimming of female hair only, violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment that denied the Board's request for an injunction to prevent the cosmetologist from cutting men's hair and denied the Board's post-trial motion was affirmed.

 

470 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul v. Hurd


No. 44180


Supreme Court of Minnesota


299 Minn. 51; 216 N.W.2d 259; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1412



March 22, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the city of St. Paul from an order of the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey County, Allan R. Markert, Judge, dismissing charges against Charles Emmett Hurd for violation of an ordinance prohibiting carrying firearms.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of St. Paul sought review of an order of the Municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey County (Minnesota) that dismissed with prejudice charges against defendant for violating St. Paul Legislative Code, § 425.03, an ordinance that prohibited the carrying firearms.


OVERVIEW: In dismissing the appeal, the court found that based upon Minn. Stat. § 632.13, it did not have jurisdiction to hear the appeal. The requirements of Minn. Stat. § 632.13(2) had been satisfied in that the ruling of the municipal court was made on January 17, 1973, and the notice of appeal was filed on January 22, 1973. However, for purposes of Minn. Stat. § 632.13(6), the written order was made on April 25, 1973, filed on April 26, 1973, and the case was set for hearing on December 6, 1973, well beyond the 6-month time limitation. It was the obvious intent of the 6-month limitation to guarantee the constitutional right to a speedy trial, rather than the establishment of procedure that the court was to follow. It therefore was incumbent upon the city to inform the clerk of court of the urgency of setting matters for hearing. The procedural requirements was be satisfied in all appeals by the city, and failure to meet them precluded the court from an exercise of its jurisdiction to hear an appeal. Nevertheless, inasmuch as jeopardy had not attached, the use of the phrase "with prejudice" by the lower court was inconsequential.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the city's appeal of the order that dismissed the charges against defendant.

State v. Welke


No. 43554


Supreme Court of Minnesota


298 Minn. 402; 216 N.W.2d 641; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1490



March 1, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Joseph Welke from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Bruce C. Stone, Judge, whereby he was convicted of violation of a city ordinance prohibiting the exhibiting and sale of obscene material, and from an order denying his alternative motion for judgment of acquittal or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant retailer appealed from the decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him for violating a city ordinance prohibiting the exhibition and sale of obscene material, and which denied his alternative motion for judgment of acquittal or for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The retailer was a clerk at a discount bookstore. Two plainclothes policemen entered the store, brought some pornographic magazines to the checkout counter where he was standing, bought the magazines, then returned to arrest the retailer. The police did not have a search warrant. The retailer was convicted of violating the Minneapolis obscenity ordinance, Minneapolis Code of Ordinances, § 870.080, by exhibiting and selling pornographic magazines. The retailer made a pretrial motion for the suppression of evidence obtained by the search of the bookstore, which the court denied. The retailer appealed and the court reversed. The court held that the retailer's conviction could not stand because he did not have clear notice of the legislative proscription that fundamental fairness required, since the courts did not agree on what materials were subject to regulation under the ordinance. The court found that the ordinance did not comport with the requirement of specificity and, since fair notice was the basic rationale for the requirement of specifically defined sexual conduct, the ordinance's construction did not afford requisite notice with respect to a sale made over four years prior.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court, which convicted the retailer for violating a city ordinance prohibiting the exhibiting and sale of obscene material, and which denied his alternative motion for judgment of acquittal or for a new trial.

 

472 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Carlson v. Smogard


No. 44186


Supreme Court of Minnesota


298 Minn. 362; 215 N.W.2d 615; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1484



February 22, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court for personal injuries allegedly sustained while plaintiff was test-driving defendant's automobile, which had been repaired by plaintiff's employer. Defendant filed a third-party complaint against the employer for indemnity. The court, Rolf Fosseen, Judge, granted third-party defendant's motion for summary judgment, and defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car owner sought review of the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted respondent employer's motion for summary judgment against the owner's third party complaint against the employer. The owner was a defendant in plaintiff test driver's action for personal injuries that were allegedly sustained while the test driver was driving the owner's automobile that had been repaired by the test driver's employer.


OVERVIEW: When the driver was operating the owner's vehicle, the latch on the hood popped open and the driver suffered a heart attack. The owner sought indemnity or alternatively contribution from the driver's employer who had repaired the vehicle. The trial court granted the employer's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the issue was whether Minn. Stat. § 176.061, subd. 10, the Workmen's Compensation Act, was constitutionally sound in light of the fact that the employer was released from contribution to the owner because he was paying workers' compensation to the driver. The court held that § 176.061 was a violation of the due process clause of the constitution. Therefore, the court reversed the award of summary judgment. The court noted that preventing indemnification to a third-party tortfeasor from a negligent employer fostered no legitimate objective. No substitute remedy had been provided to the owner. Therefore, the court held that Minn. Stat. § 176.061, subd. 10, violated the due process clause of U.S. Const. amends. V, XIIII and it violated the Minn. Const. art. 1, § 8.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and held that it was error to grant summary judgment to the employer.

 

473 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Associated Food Services, Inc. v. Commissioner of Taxation


Nos. 44310, 44311, 44312, 44313, 44314


Supreme Court of Minnesota


298 Minn. 277; 216 N.W.2d 253; 1974 Minn. LEXIS 1474



February 8, 1974 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Five actions were consolidated for trial in the Ramsey County District Court. Four separate actions against the commissioner of taxation were brought by Associated Food Services, Inc., ARA Service of Minnesota, Inc., Automatic Vending Service of Duluth, Inc., and SirVend, Inc., to recover alleged overpayments of sales taxes. In an action against the state, the commissioner of taxation, and the director of the sales and use tax division, Minnesota Automatic Merchandising Council and its members sought a declaratory judgment determining that sales of food from vending machines are not subject to the state sales tax. After findings for plaintiffs, Hyam Segell, Judge, defendants appealed from the judgment entered and from an order denying their motion for a new trial in each action.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state tax officials appealed from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which ruled in favor of plaintiffs, vending machine owners, in consolidated actions to recover alleged overpayments of sales taxes and for a declaratory judgment determining that sales of food from vending machines were not subject to the state sales tax.


OVERVIEW: The vending machines had no mechanism available for taking pennies or returning them as change. The trial court concluded that Minn. Reg. Tax S & U 9(f)(4), which provided that food from vending machines was taxable, denied vending machine owners equal protection of the law because the owners were unable to pass the sales tax on to the consumer like other retailers. The court reversed, observing that Minn. Stat. § 297A.02, which imposed a sales tax on all retailers, and Minn. Stat. § 297A.03, which allowed retailers to pass the tax on to purchasers, were two independent provisions. The vending machine owners' adoption of a method of business which, for mechanical reasons, prohibited them from taking advantage of the pass-on provision did not automatically exempt them from the provision imposing the tax, nor did it constitute arbitrary discrimination against them. Even if the same products would have been tax-exempt if sold by a grocery store, such unequal tax treatment was not enough to overcome the presumption of taxability found in Minn. Stat. § 297A.09.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the vending machine owners.

Sylvestre v. State


Nos. 44224, 44225, 44226, 44227, 44228, 44230


Supreme Court of Minnesota


298 Minn. 142; 214 N.W.2d 658; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1040



December 14, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Six former district court judges brought actions in the Ramsey County District Court against the state, the state auditor, the state treasurer, and the attorney general seeking declaratory judgments that certain provisions of the statutes providing for their retirement compensation were unconstitutional and void and relief from the provisions. In each case, on the basis of stipulated facts, the court, David E. Marsden, Judge, found for plaintiff, and defendants appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to plaintiffs J. H. Sylvestre, Paul J. Jaroscak, J. K. Underhill, Levi M. Hall, and Arnold C. Forbes; modified as to plaintiff Harold E. Flynn.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the state and various state officials, sought review of the decision of the Ramsey District Court (Minnesota), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, six former district court judges, regarding the constitutionality of certain provisions of statutes providing for their retirement compensation. The trial court found that the provisions were unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Six former district court judges filed suit against defendants seeking declaratory judgment that certain statutory provisions purporting to amend the amount of retirement compensation due each judge. When each judge was elected to office, the retirement provisions, codified at Minn. Stat. § 490.102, provided that, upon retirement, the judge was to receive a benefit equal to one-half the compensation allotted to his office. The provision was later amended to read "one-half the compensation allotted to his office at the time of his retirement." Five of the six judges retired prior to the amendment, and one after the enactment. The trial court held that the provision was unconstitutional as to the five judges who had retired prior to the enactment. The court found that the original language of the statute as it was in place when the judges took office acted as a unilateral contract offering the judges certain benefits as deferred compensation in exchange for their performance as judges. As such, the court found that the state court not constitutionally alter the terms of the contract as to any of the judges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to five of the judges, and modified the trial court's judgment as to the sixth judge. The court found that the statutory provisions were unconstitutional as applied to all the judges, and modified the trial court's order to reflect that the sixth judge also be entitled to retirement compensation at the same rate as the remaining five judges.

State v. Hipp


No. 43042


Supreme Court of Minnesota


298 Minn. 81; 213 N.W.2d 610; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1034



December 7, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Linda M. Hipp and other defendants from a judgment of the Hennepin County Municipal Court, Richard J. Kantorowicz, Judge, whereby they were convicted of unlawful assembly and from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Seven defendants sought review of a decision of the Hennepin County Municipal Court (Minneapolis), which convicted them of unlawful assembly in violation of Minn. St. § 609.705(3).


OVERVIEW: The seven protesters were among those arrested for picketing at a restaurant. The defendants were convicted of unlawful assembly in violation of Minn. St. § 609.705(3). On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions except as to two of the defendants against whom the court found that the evidence was insufficient. The court found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad on its face and was applied in a fair manner. The court found that a fair and full reading compelled the conclusion that the only misbehavior intended to be prohibited was that which disturbed or threatened the public peace. The court held that the language of § 609.705(3) was not so vague that a person of common understanding could not know that it forbids three or more assembled participants to so conduct themselves as to disturb or threaten the rights of other members of the public to have peace and good order prevail. The court found that defendants had disrupted the food service operation of the restaurant, impeded all vehicular traffic in the area, and engaged in an endless stream of shouting and profanities and, therefore, the trial court did not unconstitutionally apply the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions except as to three defendants whose convictions were reversed for want of sufficient evidence.

Lakeville v. Farmington


No. 43840


Supreme Court of Minnesota


297 Minn. 524; 211 N.W.2d 897; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1143



October 12, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the village of Lakeville in the Dakota County District Court from orders of the Minnesota Municipal Commission granting the petition of certain property owners for annexation of a part of Lakeville Township with the village of Farmington and directing that a part of said township be consolidated with appellant village. The court, John M. Fitzgerald, Judge, affirmed said orders, and appellant village having filed an appeal from the order for judgment, this court granted discretionary review.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village challenged a decision of the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which affirmed the orders of the Minnesota Municipal Commission granting a petition by respondent property owners for annexation of a part of a township with another village and directing that a part of the township be consolidated with the village.


OVERVIEW: The village argued that the 16 factors enumerated in Minn. Stat. § 414.031, subd. 4, which the Commission had to consider in ordering annexation, were not simply guides, which was the language of Minn. St. § 414.021, subd. 3, governing consolidations, but were mandatory prerequisites concerning which the Commission had to make findings. The court held that Minn. Stat. § 414.031, subd. 4, simply provided that, in arriving at its decision, the Commission shall consider the factors. The village also argued that the Commission did not expressly deal with the factor of existing or potential problems of environmental pollution. The court held that, although the Commission did not expressly deal with that factor, it did allude in its findings to the adequacy of facilities for sanitation and water and for the collection of garbage and rubbish. The court held that the failure to refer explicitly to that factor was not fatal to the proceedings. The court further held that a referendum under Minn. Stat. § 414.031, subd. 5, was not necessary because the proceedings for annexation had been initiated by a petition of a majority of the property owners within the area to be annexed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

479 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Davis


No. 43832


Supreme Court of Minnesota


297 Minn. 187; 210 N.W.2d 221; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1077



August 24, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Divorce action in the Hennepin County District Court wherein Warren Spannaus, Attorney General, intervened and moved for dismissal of the complaint. The court, A. Paul Lommen, Judge, granted said motion without prejudice, and plaintiff appealed from that order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed an order from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted without prejudice intervenor Attorney General's motion to dismiss the wife's complaint for divorce from defendant husband because the wife did not meet the one-year durational-residency requirement of Minn. Stat. § 518.07.


OVERVIEW: The wife separated from her husband and moved to Minnesota with the parties' children. Within months after moving to Minnesota, the wife filed a divorce complaint. The trial court granted the Attorney General's motion to dismiss the wife's complaint for failure to comply with the one-year durational-residency requirement of Minn. Stat. § 518.07. The wife appealed, arguing that she was a resident of Minnesota and that the durational residency requirement was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the wife's complaint without prejudice. The court held that the residency requirement was not sufficient to require the strict, compelling-interest test because the ultimate right to file for divorce was not affected by the durational requirement. The court concluded that § 518.07 did not deny equal protection because it was rationally related to the legitimate governmental objective of ensuring the domicile of the divorce applicants. Section 518.07 did not violate the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment because the wife's access to the courts was not denied but only temporarily delayed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the wife's divorce action without prejudice.

 

480 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Sharood v. Hatfield


No. 44439


Supreme Court of Minnesota


296 Minn. 416; 210 N.W.2d 275; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1217



June 26, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding in this court upon the petition of R. Paul Sharood, Robert M. Frisbee, and the Minnesota State Bar Association to obtain a declaratory judgment invalidating certain provisions of L. 1973, c. 638, and restraining Rolland F. Hatfield, state auditor, Val Bjornson, state treasurer, and Richard L. Brubacher, commissioner of administration of the state, from enforcing said provisions.



DISPOSITION: Provisions declared unconstitutional; respondents enjoined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, attorneys and the Minnesota State Bar Association, sought to obtain a declaratory judgment invalidating certain provisions of Minn. Laws 1973, ch. 638, and restraining respondents, the state auditor, the state treasurer, and the state commissioner of administration, from enforcing the provisions that allowed the legislature to take attorney registration fees and put them in the state general fund.


OVERVIEW: At the 1973 session of the Minnesota legislature, Minn. Laws 1973, ch. 638 was enacted, regulating many professions including the practice of law. Later, Minn. Stat. § 481.01 was amended to allow the money collected as registration fees from attorneys to be deposited with the state treasurer under the assurance that it would be kept in a special fund and would never cancel. However, the state officers proposed to divert the money from the special fund to the general revenue fund of the state without an appropriation of a like amount to the court. The court held Minn. Laws 1973, ch. 638, invalid as a violation of the separation of powers. The court found that regulating the legal profession was its own duty and solely within its own power. Thus, the attorneys' funds could not be turned over to the state general fund. Consequently, the court enjoined enforcement of the law.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the state auditor and the state treasurer be permanently enjoined from transferring funds deposited with the treasurer to the general revenue fund of the state and that the state auditor and state treasurer continue to deposit such funds pursuant to the order of the court for the purpose for which such funds were collected.

 

481 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Jude v. Erdahl


No. 43901


Supreme Court of Minnesota


296 Minn. 200; 207 N.W.2d 715; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1179



May 11, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Order was issued by this court upon the application of Thaddeus V. Jude and Martin J. Rafferty, Jr., directed to the secretary of state and the auditor of Hennepin County, requiring them to show cause why they should not accept applicants' filings for the office of state representative.



DISPOSITION: Application of petitioner Jude granted; application of petitioner Rafferty denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidates applied for an order directing respondents, Secretary of State of Minnesota and auditor of Hennepin County, to show cause why they should not permit the candidates' filings for the office of state representative. The court granted one application and denied the other. It issued an opinion expanding those orders, construing Minn. Stat. § 202.04 and Minn. Const. art. 7, § 7.


OVERVIEW: The candidates applied for orders, directing defendants to show cause why their names should not be placed on ballots in the primary election for state representative. The court denied one petition and granted the other and issued an opinion expanding on those orders. As to the petition it granted, it explained that the candidate had been denied a place on the ballot because he could not attest that he would be 21 years old on the day of the election in November 1973, as § 202.04, subd. 1(e) required. His 21st birthday was some five weeks after the election, for the term that began on January 2, 1973. The court declared § 202.04 unconstitutional because it effectively increased the age requirement for eligibility for office to 21 years and 2 months, without constitutional support. In the matter of the second candidate, the court explained that it had denied his application because he would not have attained the age of 21 until April 21, 1973. The court held that the amendment of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 25, reducing the voting age to 19, had no bearing on the Minn. Const. art. 7, § 7 eligibility for office requirement of 21 years of age on the date that a term of office began.


OUTCOME: The court granted the application of one candidate and denied that of the other candidate in proceedings to require defendants to accept their filings and add their names to ballots in the primary election for state representative.

 

482 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Frink


No. 43300


Supreme Court of Minnesota


296 Minn. 57; 206 N.W.2d 664; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1156



April 13, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Prohibition in this court upon the relation of Brian J. Frink and Robert C. Mix to stay proceedings in the St. Louis County District Court, Donald E. Anderson, Judge, relating to charges of unlawful possession of narcotic drugs.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged and matter remanded for proceedings consistent with opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants and the county attorney filed a petition for a writ of prohibition that raised the issue of whether evidence obtained by intercepting messages transmitted over the telephone of one defendant would be admissible at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with possession of various drugs. The police were able to obtain evidence against defendants from intercepting messages transmitted over one defendant's telephone. An assistant county attorney filed the application for a warrant authorizing the interception. Defendants argued that such interception violated the Privacy of Communications Act, Minn. Stat. § 626A.05. The court granted the parties' petition for a writ of prohibition and held that the evidence was not admissible. The court found that § 626A.05 required that applications for interception be initiated either by the attorney general or by a county attorney. By way of comparison, the court noted that the federal statute, 18 U.S.C.S. § 2516(2), required that the "principal prosecuting attorney" make the application. Moreover, 18 U.S.C.S. § 2516(1) provided that the attorney general could specially designate an assistant attorney general to submit an application. The court found no corresponding statute for assistant county attorneys. Accordingly, the court held that the application for interception filed by the assistant county attorney and subsequent interception were not authorized.


OUTCOME: The court discharged the writ of prohibition and remanded the matter, holding that the evidence obtained from the interception was not admissible.

Schaust v. Town Board of Hollywood Township


No. 43016


Supreme Court of Minnesota


295 Minn. 571; 204 N.W.2d 646; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1350



February 23, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Carver County District Court brought by Mathias S. Schaust and Walter Barfnecht to enjoin the Town Board of Hollywood Township from widening a roadway adjoining their property or for damages. After adverse findings, Arlo E. Haering, Judge, plaintiffs appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial on the issue of injunctive relief and from the judgment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to denial of motion for a new trial; dismissed as to appeal from judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners, whose roadside property was taken by the Town Board to widen the adjoining roadway, complained of a judgment of the Carver County District Court (Minnesota), which denied their claim for damages, and from an order denying their motion for a new trial on the issue of injunctive relief. The property owners contended that the uncompensated taking of roadside property pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 160.05 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Because the motion for a new trial was based solely on newly discovered evidence and did not question the constitutionality of the taking, the constitutional issue was not within the scope of appellate review of the order denying that motion. Because the property owners stated no ground for a new trial as to injunctive relief, no question of law was raised. The court therefore affirmed the trial court's order denying a new trial as to injunctive relief. The notice of appeal also stated that the appeal was from the judgment, however, the judgment had not been entered and, under Minn. R. Civ. P. 58.01, the appeal was premature and was dismissed. Even if the court were to have accepted the property owners' oral revision of the written terms of the notice of appeal, stating that the appeal was from the order for judgment, the appeal from the order for judgment was not timely under Minn. R. Civ. App. P. 104.01, which required that an appeal from an order be within 30 days after service of written notice of filing thereof by the adverse party. The notice of appeal was dated more than two months after the Town Board served the written notice of the order for judgment and was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order as to denial of motion for a new trial, and dismissed the appeal from the judgment.

Schwartz v. Talmo


No. 43146


Supreme Court of Minnesota


295 Minn. 356; 205 N.W.2d 318; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1310



February 23, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Marlene M. Schwartz, widow of Neil L. Schwartz, deceased employee, to review a decision of the Workmen's Compensation Commission denying her claim for compensation against Warren Talmo, d.b.a. Warren's Masonry, employer, and Allied Mutual Insurance Company, its insurer.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, the decedent's widow, sought review of a decision by the Minnesota Workmen's Compensation Commission, which denied her claim for benefits based on the commission's finding that the decedent's death resulted from a suicide and was, therefore, non-compensable by operation of Minn. Stat. § 176.021(1).


OVERVIEW: The decedent sustained an injury to his back during the course of his employment. As a result of the injury, he received workmen's compensation benefits. Over a period of time, the decedent became extremely depressed due to his inability to regain full health. The decedent committed suicide. The commission denied the relator's request for benefits based on the provision set forth in Minn. Stat. § 176.021(1), which excluded suicide deaths from compensability. On review, the court affirmed the decision of the commission. In reaching its decision, the court held that the language of the statute was clear and explicit. Furthermore, the court rejected the relator's argument that the statute was violative of equal protection and, thus, unconstitutional. Based on its analysis, the court concluded that the realtor was not entitled to benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the commission.

 

485 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hodgson


No. 42966


Supreme Court of Minnesota


295 Minn. 294; 204 N.W.2d 199; 1973 Minn. LEXIS 1299



February 2, 1973 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Dr. Jane Elizabeth Hodgson from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, J. Jerome Plunkett, Judge, whereby she was convicted of abortion.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted her of performing an abortion pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 617.18.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a physician, was convicted of performing an abortion pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 617.18. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 617.18. The court reversed defendant's conviction. The court held that during the first trimester the attending physician, in consultation with her patient, was free to determine, without regulation by Plaintiff State, that in her medical judgment the patient's pregnancy should be terminated. The abortion was a medical decision based on the physician's professional judgment. The physician assumed a responsibility, which was properly vested in her at a time, and under circumstances, which precluded the State from claiming any compelling interest in interfering with the operation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of performing an abortion.

487 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul v. Whidby


No. 43024


Supreme Court of Minnesota


295 Minn. 129; 203 N.W.2d 823; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1124



December 29, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Forest Whidby from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Ronald E. Hachey, Judge, whereby he was convicted of visiting a disorderly house.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), in which he was convicted of visiting a disorderly house, in violation of St. Paul, Minn., City Legislative Code, § 469.01. Defendant originally pleaded guilty and was sentenced to 30 days in the workhouse. He subsequently appealed to the trial court for a trial by jury, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 488A.27(6).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on presumption of innocence and proof beyond a reasonable doubt, in instructing the jury that it would be permitted to return a verdict upon an agreement by five-sixths of its number, and in denying defendant's motion to dismiss the case because the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court concluded that a proceeding that could result in incarceration for 90 days was criminal in nature and that defendant should receive the same procedural considerations, despite the historical practice of treating city ordinance violations as civil matters. The fact that certain acts were proscribed by ordinances enacted by a municipal corporation rather than by state criminal statutes made them no less criminal in nature. The court therefore decreed that in all proceedings for violation of a municipal ordinance that may result in the penalty of incarceration and which were commenced after the date of the court's decision the defendant was to be presumed innocent until the contrary was proved and, in case of reasonable doubt, was entitled to acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction on grounds that he should have been given the presumption of innocence and his guilt should have been proven beyond a reasonable doubt in order to obtain a conviction. The court remanded the case and instructed the trial court that the five-sixths verdict instruction not be given on the new trial. The court found no merit in defendant's other arguments on appeal.

Hutson v. Christensen


No. 43351


Supreme Court of Minnesota


295 Minn. 112; 203 N.W.2d 535; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1122



December 22, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court wherein Robert Hutson and Heidi Hutson sought to enforce a judgment obtained against defendants, Larry Christensen and Joy Christensen, in an Illinois court. After findings for plaintiffs, Donald T. Barbeau, Judge, defendants appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlords filed an action upon a cognovit judgment obtained against defendant tenants in Illinois pursuant to a confession of judgment clause in a lease. The Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) granted the landlords' motion for summary judgment on the basis that the Illinois judgment was entitled to full faith and credit. The tenants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tenants asserted that a great portion of the cognovit judgment was for alleged damage to the apartment they rented from the landlords, instead of rent. The court found that this portion of the cognovit violated Illinois law, which authorized confession of judgment clauses only for debts of a fixed amount. Accordingly, the Illinois court had no jurisdiction to enter the judgment for damages and repairs to the apartment. Therefore, the court held that the judgment was not entitled to full faith and credit. The court did not reach the issue of whether cognovit judgments, obtained in foreign states, without notice to the debtor or opportunity to appear, violated due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

489 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vadnais


No. 42927


Supreme Court of Minnesota


295 Minn. 17; 202 N.W.2d 657; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1107



November 24, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Warren L. Vadnais from a judgment of the Washington County Municipal Court, Searle Sandeen, Judge, whereby he was convicted of violating an ordinance of the town of Forest Lake prohibiting the parking of mobile homes.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Washington County Municipal Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of parking a mobile home trailer upon his land in violation of Forest Lake, Minn., Ordinance 27.


OVERVIEW: Defendant parked a mobile home trailer next to his home. He was convicted of violating a municipal ordinance which prohibited use as a dwelling or parking of any type of mobile home trailer, except in a licensed trailer court or for a six month period in connection with a construction project. Defendant contended that the ordinance was enforced against him and not against others who similarly parked residential trailers within the township. The court held that a conscious exercise of some selectivity in enforcement, based on a rational exercise of police or prosecutorial discretion did not itself establish a constitutional violation; however, an intentional decision by public officials, acting as agents of the State, not to enforce penal regulations against a class of violators expressly included within the terms of such penal regulation did constitute a denial of equal protection. The court found that the evidence, including an admission by township officials that the ordinance was not always enforced, compelled it to conclude that township officials systematically discriminated in the enforcement of the ordinance at issue and thus, defendant's conviction had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Port Authority of St. Paul v. Groppoli


No. 43507


Supreme Court of Minnesota


295 Minn. 1; 202 N.W.2d 371; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1104



November 17, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Eminent domain proceeding in the Ramsey County District Court instituted by the Port Authority of the City of St. Paul to acquire land owned by Michael P. Groppoli, Gayle I. Groppoli, Lauro DiSanto, Lucille F. DiSanto, and Capitol City Distributing Company, Inc. The court, Edward D. Mulally, Judge, found the taking to be for a public use and to be necessary and authorized by law, and this court granted respondents' petition for discretionary review.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent landowners challenged an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which, in an eminent domain proceeding, granted a request by petitioner, a city's port authority, to acquire the landowners' land for a public purpose. The court granted the landowners' request for a discretionary review of the order of the trial court. The landowners argued that the taking of their land was not for a public purpose.


OVERVIEW: The land sought by the authority was located within an industrial park which, in a prior action, was determined to be blighted or marginal. The property was improved with a building which was over 40 years old and which had been used by the landowners to warehouse and distribute beer. The warehousing use conformed to the plan of the park's development, but the building did not meet the overall plan of development because it did not meet the park's restrictive covenants. In an underlying action, a private company sought to compel the authority to lease the landowners' property to it pursuant to a prior agreement. In an attempt to settle the underlying action, the authority sought to condemn the landowners' property in order to lease the building to the private company. The court held that the taking of the landowners' parcel was an unconstitutional taking of private property for a private use. The court further found that the leasing of the property to a private party for 30 years without substantial change in the nature or character of the property was inconsistent with constitutional requirements for the proper taking of private property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and denied the landowners request for an award of attorneys' fees.

 

491 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Daly


No. 43867


Supreme Court of Minnesota


294 Minn. 351; 200 N.W.2d 913; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1411



September 8, 1972 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied, sub nom. Daly v. McCarthy,    U.S.   , 93 S. Ct. 528, 34 L. ed. 2d 491 (1972).


PRIOR HISTORY: Order to show cause issued by this court directing Arlen I. Erdahl, secretary of state, Lou McKenna, Ramsey County auditor, and George B. Hickey, Hennepin County auditor, to refrain and desist from placing on the ballots for the general election to be held November 7, 1972, the names of Jerome Daly and Gordon C. Peterson as candidates for associate justice of the supreme court and the names of William E. Drexler and Charles Thibodeau as candidates for judge of district court.



DISPOSITION: Ordered that said names be omitted from the ballots.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding under Minn. Stat. § 203.38, subd. 1, to determine the eligibility of four potential candidates to have their names appear on the ballots for a general election, as candidates for justice of the supreme court or judge of the district court, the court issued an order to show cause directing respondent governmental officials to demonstrate why they should not be commanded to refrain from placing their names on the ballots.


OVERVIEW: The potential candidates were either disbarred attorneys or had never been admitted to practice law. They filed affidavits for candidacy for state court judgeships. The governmental officials questioned whether the candidates were eligible to file for, or hold, the offices for which they sought to have their names put on the ballots in the general election. The court issued an order to show cause pursuant to § 203.38, subd. 1, why the governmental officials should not be commanded to refrain from placing the names of any of the candidates on the ballots. Finding no reason, the court ordered that the potential candidates' names were to be omitted from the ballots. The court found that the phrase "learned in the law," under Minn. Const. art. 6, § 7, provided the basis for denying admission on the ballots. As for the potential candidate who had never been admitted to practice law, the court found that he had no legal training and was not an attorney. He was a layman. He was not "learned in the law." As for the disbarred attorneys, their disbarment rendered them laymen. As such, their status deprived them of being "learned in the law."


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the potential candidates' names be omitted from the ballots by the governmental officials.

Minnesota Pollution Control Agency v. Hatfield


No. 43738


Supreme Court of Minnesota


294 Minn. 260; 200 N.W.2d 572; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1398; 4 ERC (BNA) 1453



August 11, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Rolland Hatfield, auditor of the State of Minnesota, from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, James M. Lynch, Judge, declaring an act of the legislature authorizing the issuance of water pollution control bonds to be valid.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff auditor sought review of a judgment from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which declared the act of defendant Pollution Control Agency that authorized the issuance of water pollution control bonds to have been constitutionally valid.


OVERVIEW: The legislature authorized a water pollution control fund, Ex. Sess. L. 1971, c. 20, § 1(1), to which bonds were issued by the auditor upon request of the Agency, which was to administer the fund. The Agency requested the auditor to issue the bonds, which led him to file a declaratory judgment action that sought a declaration that c. 20 was unconstitutional pursuant to Minn. Const. art. 9, § 5, which prohibited the investment by the State of public money in internal improvements, and because the legislature's delegation of authority to the Agency was improper. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the legislation and the auditor appealed. The court held that § 5 excepted investment of public money by the State where it was used for the preservation of public health and that the water pollution control fund fell under that particular category because was of chief concern to alleviate the pollution of State waters in order to make them safe for human consumption. The court held that the legislature's delegation of authority to the Agency was not unconstitutional because they were allowed to delegate legislative functions which were administrative in carrying out their laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that upheld the constitutionality of the legislation that authorized the issuance of water pollution control bonds to the Agency.

Molberg v. Marsden


No. 43342


Supreme Court of Minnesota


294 Minn. 493; 200 N.W.2d 298; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1441



July 28, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought on behalf of Susan Molberg, a minor, by Warren Molberg, her father and natural guardian, for personal injuries allegedly sustained by said minor as the result of the negligence of defendant, and by said Warren Molberg on his own behalf for consequential damages. After a settlement agreement was executed by the parties, the court, Douglas K. Amdahl, Judge, ordered payment to Hennepin County Welfare Department, which had a lien for medical services in excess of the amount of the settlement, and plaintiffs appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injury victim sought review of the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which, upon approval of an agreement settling the victim's personal injury suit against defendants, a driver and his insurer, directed that the county welfare board be reimbursed for medical expenses provided by it.


OVERVIEW: The victim, who was a minor, received substantial injuries when she was struck by the driver's vehicle. When the victim's father was unable to cover the medical costs incurred in treating the victim, the board provided financial assistance for the medical and hospital expenses. Thereafter, the victim and defendants agreed to a settlement, which was far below the value of the victim's claim, but was made necessary because her claim exceed both available insurance funds and the driver's potential to pay any judgment. The trial court ordered that the board be reimbursed for the medical expenses pursuant to the lien filed by the board under Minn. Stat. § 393.10 subd. 1. While the board's claim exceeded the settlement funds, after the allowance for attorneys' fees and costs, the trial court rejected the victim's contention that the recovery should have been apportioned. In affirming, the court held that the statutory lien clearly and expressly attached to the claim of the person to whom the services were furnished, irrespective of his legal liability to pay such claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order directing reimbursement of medical expenses to the board.

 

494 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Altendorfer v. Jandric, Inc.


No. 43349


Supreme Court of Minnesota


294 Minn. 475; 199 N.W.2d 812; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1434



July 21, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Dakota County District Court brought by Joseph E. Altendorfer and Richard A. Marsolek for property damage allegedly sustained by reason of defendant's negligence in the manner of connecting their houses to a sewer system. Defendant filed a third-party complaint against the village of Inver Grove Heights, which maintains the sewer system. The court, John B. Friedrich, Judge, granted third-party defendant's motion for summary judgment, and defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners filed a negligence action against defendant builder for property damage allegedly sustained by the connection of their houses to a sewer system. The builder filed a third-party complaint against third-party defendant municipality, which maintained the sewer system. The Dakota County District Court, (Minnesota) granted the municipality's motion for summary judgment, and the builder appealed from the judgment entered.


OVERVIEW: The third-party action, which was the subject of the appeal, arose out of the builder's claim for contribution or indemnity from the municipality. The builder alleged that the sole cause of damage was the municipality's negligence in the maintenance and operation of the sewer system. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of municipality. The sewer system was not constructed by the municipality but by a corporation, the stock of which was wholly owned by the builder. The third-party complaint did not allege a common liability for concurring negligence; a requisite for shared responsibility by contribution. Instead it attempted to offer the homeowners a different tortfeasor, which was an impermissible use of the third-party action under Minn. R. Civ. P. 14. The municipality was not notified of a tort claim against it as required by Minn. Stat. § 466.05. The builder contended that § 466.05, at least in its application to the third-party action for indemnity or contribution, unconstitutionally deprived it of due process or equal protection of the law. The court found that the constitutional issue warranted an opportunity for the attorney general to intervene in defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the municipality in the builder's third party claim for contribution or indemnity.

 

495 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rawland


No. 42444


Supreme Court of Minnesota


294 Minn. 17; 199 N.W.2d 774; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1373



June 30, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Frank S. Rawland from a judgment of the Sherburne County District Court, Robert Bakke, Judge, whereby he was convicted of murder in the third degree.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Sherburne County District Court (Minnesota), which, following a bench trial, convicted him of murder in the third degree and sentenced him to an indeterminate term of up to 25 years in prison. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court improperly found him to be sane within the test for criminal responsibility set forth in Minn. Stat. § 611.026 (1969).


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed his father to death. Prior to the stabbing, defendant had been committed for mental illness and manifested bizarre behavior. He was convicted of murder in the third degree and on appeal, the court vacated the judgment of guilty and issued directions to enter a judgment of not guilty by reason of insanity. The court held that defendant established under § 611.026 that he was laboring under such a defect of reason from mental illness that he did not know the nature of his act or that it was wrong, and that he should have been found not guilty because of insanity, particularly given his extended mental illness, his inability to control his actions at the time of the offense, and his inability to distinguish between right and wrong. In so holding, the court determined that a strict and literal construction of § 611.026 was inconsistent with its underlying objectives, basic principles of law, and constitutional requirements. Instead, evidence could be received freely so that the factfinder could take into account of the entire man and his mind as a whole. Such evidence included competent evidence that related to cognition, volition, and capacity to control behavior.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of guilty and issued directions to enter a judgment of not guilty by reason of insanity and for proceedings thereafter in the trial court for commitment.

 

496 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul v. Kekedakis


No. 43232


Supreme Court of Minnesota


293 Minn. 334; 199 N.W.2d 151; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1194



June 16, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Joseph Kekedakis from a judgment of the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey County, Roland J. Faricy, Judge, whereby he was convicted of violation of a city ordinance against possession of a firearm.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Municipal Court of St. Paul, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted him of violating St. Paul, Minn., Leg. Code § 425.03, prohibiting the possession or control of a firearm in a public place. Defendant contended that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was employed at a gasoline service station. He became concerned for his safety because of a conversation with two men. When they returned, defendant got his employer's revolver and ordered the men to leave. The incident was reported to the police and defendant was arrested. The issues raised on appeal were whether § 425.03 was so vague and indefinite that it is unenforceable and whether the ordinance denied defendant due process as to the circumstances of his case. The court held that although the language of § 425.03which prohibited a person from possessing a firearm in a public place, was broad and inclusive, it was not so vague and indefinite as to be invalid. The court declined to pass on hypothetical situations raised by defendant in which the ordinance might fall for vagueness and indefiniteness. Defendant contended that the gasoline service station where the alleged offense occurred was not a public place within the meaning of the ordinance. Noting that the station was open for business when defendant was arrested and invited patronage of the public, the court held that the service station was a public place within the meaning of § 425.03.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

497 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Housing & Redevelopment Authority v. Minneapolis


No. 42872


Supreme Court of Minnesota


293 Minn. 227; 198 N.W.2d 531; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1182



May 26, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought by the Housing and Redevelopment Authority of Minneapolis, Charles L. Horn, and Leonard W. Anderson to enjoin said city and its council from proceeding with an election on a proposed charter amendment or for a declaratory judgment holding the proposed amendment unconstitutional. Leo A. Bernat, Richard W. LeRoy, Frank S. Preston, Jr., John A. S. Webster, and Elizabeth M. Wood were granted leave to intervene on behalf of themselves and other taxpayers. After findings for plaintiffs, Irving C. Iverson, Judge, intervenors appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city housing authority filed an action in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) to enjoin defendants, the city and its council, from proceeding with an election on a proposed charter amendment that was proposed by intervening taxpayers and for a declaratory judgment that the proposed amendment unconstitutional. The trial court entered a judgment for the housing authority and enjoined the election. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought to amend the city charter to require that the development of all low-income housing projects be put to a vote of the people in a special election before the project was authorized. The housing authority argued that the proposed amendment was unconstitutional because it wrested away its legislative authority. The trial court's judgment was affirmed. The court held that it was proper for the trial court to enjoin the election rather than permit the administration and the voters of the city to experience the frustration and expense of setting up election machinery and going to the polls in a process which was ultimately destined to be futile. The court found that the proposed amendment was manifestly unconstitutional. The proposal would confer the right of referendum with respect to any action taken by the city council, not limited to the adoption of ordinances. The broad referendum right not only appeared to be without statutory authority under Minn. Stat. § 410.20 but also, would create a chaotic situation in city government.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which enjoined the city from conducting an election on the taxpayer's proposed charter amendment and which denied the taxpayer's motion for a new trial, was affirmed.

 

498 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Rochester


No. 43207


Supreme Court of Minnesota


293 Minn. 156; 197 N.W.2d 244; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1172



April 28, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Olmsted County District Court wherein plaintiff, in addition to other relief, sought to recover certain motion picture viewing machines and films allegedly seized by defendants, city of Rochester; James M. Macken, its chief of police; and Gerald H. Swanson, its attorney. The court, O. Russell Olson, Judge, ordered the property returned to plaintiff, and defendant city appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Rochester (Minnesota) challenged an order of the Olmsted District Court (Minnesota), which entered a judgment in respondent arcade owner's favor in his declaratory judgment action that sought the return of the purportedly obscene films and the coin-operated motion picture viewing machines that the city allegedly seized.


OVERVIEW: The city alleged that the search warrants under which the property was seized were valid under the First Amendment and that a pre-seizure adversary judicial hearing was not needed. The court affirmed the district court's judgment, concluding that the warrants were issued pursuant to a constitutionally infirm procedure. The court agreed with the district court that seizing the only available copy of each confiscated film was equivalent to mass seizures of every copy of a publication and that, under those circumstances, a prior adversary hearing was needed to determine whether the films' subject matter enjoyed First Amendment freedom-of-speech protection. The court also held that the owner's right to petition the municipal court for a return of the films did not provide an adequate remedy because that represented an improper effort to shift the burden of proof onto the owner and the United States Supreme Court clearly found that the censor had the burden of proving obscenity rested on the censor. The court further determined that the evidence could have been preserved by barring the owner from concealing, destroying, or tampering with the films.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in the owner's favor in the declaratory judgment action in which he sought the return of the property that the city seized.

 

499 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Klicker v. State


No. 43094


Supreme Court of Minnesota


293 Minn. 149; 197 N.W.2d 434; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1171; 4 ERC (BNA) 1015



April 21, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Ernest Klicker and other landowners, certain owners of advertising devices, and purchasers of advertising space against the state and the commissioner of highways for a declaratory judgment holding unconstitutional a statute providing for the removal of advertising devices. Several owners of advertising devices were added as plaintiffs, and Minnesota Environmental Control Citizens Association was permitted to intervene as a defendant. The court, Harold W. Schultz, Judge, granted defendants' motion for dismissal of the issue of whether the statute constitutes a taking of property without just compensation, and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff advertisers and landowners appealed a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted a motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim filed by defendants, the State and state highway commissioner. The advertisers sought declaratory and injunctive relief arguing that Minn. Stat. ch. 173 (1969), requiring removal of certain advertising signs, was an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: A statute required the removal of nonconforming signs four years later, allowing time so as to compensate sign owners by amortization instead of eminent domain. The advertisers sought relief, arguing that the amortization period was unreasonable and arbitrary and was a taking without just compensation. The trial court dismissed the constitutional challenge for failure to state a claim. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the trial court erred in dismissing without an evidentiary hearing to develop the facts necessary to decide the constitutional issue and that the advertisers were entitled to an opportunity to prove that the amortization period was unreasonable or arbitrary. The court ruled that the case was properly filed as a class action, given the large number of signs to be removed in the state, the issues common to all of the sign owners, and the importance of reaching consistent results for all those affected. The court concluded that the question of whether due process of law was otherwise available was not properly before the court and that a mandamus action to compel eminent domain proceedings could not be filed until the constitutional issue was decided.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the advertisers' complaint and remanded for an evidentiary hearing.

 

500 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Graber v. Peter Lametti Constr. Co.


No. 42738


Supreme Court of Minnesota


293 Minn. 24; 197 N.W.2d 443; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1154



March 24, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Lawrence K. Graber, employee, to review a decision of the Workmen's Compensation Commission denying his claim against Peter Lametti Construction Company and Ashbach Construction Company, a joint venture, employer, and Continental Casualty Company, its insurer.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari upon the relation of plaintiff employee to review a decision of the Workmen's Compensation Commission (Minnesota), which denied his claim for disability benefits against defendants, employer and insurer.


OVERVIEW: The employee operated a "mole" machine in the construction of an underground tunnel for his employer for a period of 14 months. Silica dust was extensively prevalent in the tunnel near the machine while it was in operation. Four years after his last exposure to the silica dust, he was diagnosed with silicosis. The employee petitioned the commission for disability benefits. The commission denied his petition for benefits because the three-year limitation in Minn. Stat. § 176.66(3) had run. The court granted certiorari upon the relation of the employee. The employee contended that the three-year limitation should not have begun to run against him until the silicosis was manifested at his examination and diagnosis as opposed to the date of his last exposure to silica dust four years earlier. The court held that § 176.66(3), clearly indicated that the legislature intended a strict denial of compensation for disability due to silicosis where the disability did not occur within three years after the employee's last exposure to the hazard. Since the employee's last exposure to silica dust was more than three years before his disablement occurred, the commission's decision was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's decision, which denied the employee's claim for disability benefits against the employer and the insurer.

 

501 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Opatz v. St. Cloud


No. 43634


Supreme Court of Minnesota


293 Minn. 379; 196 N.W.2d 298; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1206



March 20, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus in the Stearns County District Court upon the petition of Joseph Paul Opatz, by Leona Katherine Dlugosch, his guardian ad litem, to compel the city of St. Cloud and its city clerk to place petitioner's name on the ballot for the city primary election as a candidate for nomination for city councilman. The court, Charles W. Kennedy, Judge, ordered the writ discharged, and petitioner appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, proposed candidate, sought review of a decision of the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota), which discharged the proposed candidate's motion for an alternative writ of mandamus seeking to have his name placed on a ballot for city alderman.


OVERVIEW: The proposed candidate was a 19-year-old college student, who was qualified to vote due to a state constitutional amendment, passed by the people of the state, that lowered the voting age from 21 to 19 years old. The age to hold elective was maintained at 21 years of age, however. The proposed candidate sought to have his name placed on the ballot as a candidate for a ward city alderman. The city clerk refused to place the proposed candidate's name on the ballot. The proposed candidate filed suit seeking a writ of mandamus to compel the placing of his name on the ballot. The trial court denied the writ. The court affirmed, holding that the state constitutional amendment was only passed for the purpose to change the voting age to 19 from 21 years of age. The legal minimum age for a political candidate was within the purview of the legislature and the courts owed the legislature great deference as to matters properly within its purview.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the proposed candidate's motion for an alternative writ of mandamus seeking to have his name placed on a ballot for city alderman.

 

502 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. McGlynn


No. 42326


Supreme Court of Minnesota


292 Minn. 405; 195 N.W.2d 583; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1321



March 10, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Michael J. McGlynn from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Luther Sletten, Judge, whereby he was convicted of aggravated robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two accomplices robbed a fur store. Defendant appealed his aggravated robbery conviction, contending that the trial court unconstitutionally allowed his accomplices to testify at trial because they had pleaded guilty to the offense but not sentenced. He also contended that the non-accomplice testimony presented to corroborate the accomplices' testimony was insufficient. The court held that the corroboration required by Minn. Stat. § 634.04 did not have to be of sufficient weight to establish a prima facie case for conviction; rather, it was sufficient that circumstantial evidence clearly implicated defendant in the crime. The court found that the testimony of the non-accomplices amply corroborated the testimony of defendant's accomplices and, thus, the trial court properly admitted it. The court further held that there was no constitutional impediment to the State's use of defendant's accomplices who testified under the expectation of leniency with respect to their sentencing because their credibility was naturally suspect and witness credibility was a question for the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

503 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Larson


No. 42884


Supreme Court of Minnesota


292 Minn. 350; 195 N.W.2d 180; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1315



February 25, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Cedric A. Larson from an order of the Anoka County Municipal Court, Thomas G. Forsberg, Judge, denying his motion to dismiss a complaint charging him with parking and occupying a mobile home in violation of a city ordinance, and from a judgment of conviction.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order and judgment from the Anoka County Municipal Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion to dismiss a complaint charging him with parking and occupying a mobile home in violation of a city ordinance and which convicted him of violating the ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with locating a mobile home on his property without procuring a permit in violation of a city ordinance. He filed a motion for an order dismissing the action on the ground of lack of jurisdiction or in the alternative, declaring the ordinance unconstitutional. Defendant alleged that his property was within the jurisdiction of the Metropolitan Airports Commission (MAC) and not the city. The court denied his motion and convicted him of violating the ordinance. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the property was in the city and was governed by its zoning ordinances. MAC never took or purchased the property and was not vested with any authority to exercise general police power over it pursuant to Minn. Stat. §§ 360.107, subd. 17 or 360.126. The property was not located within the legally described boundaries of an airport. The ordinance was constitutional. Defendant did not meet his burden of showing by clear and convincing evidence that the relief he sought would not result in any substantial detriment to neighboring property improved in reliance on the validity of the ordinance. The ordinance was a valid exercise of the city's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and affirmed the denial of his motion to dismiss.

Fridley Recreation v. Commissioner of Taxation


No. 42826


Supreme Court of Minnesota


292 Minn. 260; 194 N.W.2d 584; 1972 Minn. LEXIS 1302



February 11, 1972 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Fridley Recreation & Service Company to review a decision of the Tax Court which affirmed an order of the commissioner of taxation relating to the sales tax liability of said relator for the year 1967.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator taxpayer, a bowling alley owner, sought certiorari to review a decision of the Tax Court (Minnesota), which affirmed an order of the commissioner of taxation relating to the sales tax liability of the taxpayer where the commission found the Minnesota sales tax was applicable to the fees paid for bowling and to receipts from the sale of bowling shoes.


OVERVIEW: The commission found that fees paid for bowling and receipts from the sale of bowling shoes were subject to the state tax. The tax court affirmed the finding. On certiorari review, the court affirmed. The court found that the fees charged bowlers for the privilege of using bowling alleys were subject to the sales tax within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 297A.01, subd. 3(d) (1969). The court found that the fee paid for bowling was an "admission" charge. The court also found that a bowling lane, approach area, and the mechanical equipment involved constituted an amusement device. The sale of bowling shoes were not included within the clothing exemption provided by Minn. Stat. § 297A.25, subd. 1(g) (1969).


OUTCOME: The tax court's decision was affirmed.
