State v. Carlson


Nos. 42278, 42279


Supreme Court of Minnesota


291 Minn. 368; 192 N.W.2d 421; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1042



November 5, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals by Robert Carlson, d.b.a. Discount Book and Magazine Store, and S. Peter Getman from judgments of the municipal court of Duluth, St. Louis County, Harry T. Lathrop, Judge, whereby they were convicted on 29 counts of possession of obscene movies with intent to sell.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed, subject to modification.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the decisions by the Municipal Court of Duluth, St. Louis County (Minnesota), which convicted defendants on 29 counts of possession of obscene movies with intent to sell.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the State did not present sufficient evidence to sustain the jury's finding of guilty on any of the 29 counts, contending that no evidence was offered to establish the elements of the offense; that the dominant theme of the materials taken as a whole appeals to a prurient interest in sex; that the material was patently offensive because it affronted contemporary community standards relating to the description or representation of sexual matters; and that the material was utterly without redeeming social value. The court thought that the instructions were quite sufficient to explain the elements of the offense under decisions of the United States Supreme Court and to enable the jury to determine whether defendants were guilty or innocent of the charges against them. It seemed to the court that the particular selection of magazines and books placed in the windows, accompanied by the signs warranting that the shopper could not be arrested in the store, were designed to represent that the material found in the store was erotically arousing, salacious, and prurient and therefore constituted pandering, denying defendants First Amendment protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of convictions, subject to modification of sentences in accordance with the opinion of the court.

 

506 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. Nelson


No. 43009


Supreme Court of Minnesota


291 Minn. 310; 191 N.W.2d 185; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1032



October 15, 1971 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Baker v. Nelson, 409 U.S. 810, 34 L. Ed. 2d 65, 93 S. Ct. 37, 1972 U.S. LEXIS 1164 (1972)
Related proceeding at McConnell v. United States, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 1313 (D. Minn., Jan. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mandamus in the Hennepin County District Court to compel the clerk of said court to issue a marriage license to petitioners, Richard John Baker and James Michael McConnell. The court, Tom Bergin, Judge, ordered the alternative writ quashed and ordered said clerk not to issue the license, and petitioners appealed from said orders.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner marriage applicants, both of whom were the same sex, appealed from an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which quashed applicants' writ of mandamus and directed respondent clerk of court not to issue a marriage license to applicants.


OVERVIEW: Two adult male persons made an application to a clerk of court for a marriage license pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 517.08. The clerk declined to issue the license because the applicants were of the same sex. The applicants filed a writ of mandamus that was quashed by the trial court. The trial court ruled the clerk was not required to issue a marriage license and specifically directed the license not be issued. The applicants appealed from that order, arguing that the absence of an express statutory prohibition against same-sex marriages evinced a legislative intent to authorize such marriages. However the reviewing court looked at the historical background of the statute and determined it did not authorize marriage between persons of the same sex. The applicants also argued the statute was unconstitutional because the right to marry was a fundamental right of all persons and that restricting marriage to only couples of the opposite sex was irrational and invidiously discriminatory. The reviewing court stated the Fourteenth Amendment was not offended by the state's classification of persons authorized to marry. The order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order quashing applicants' writ of mandamus and directing the clerk of court not to issue applicants a marriage license was affirmed because the state statute did not authorize marriage between persons of the same sex and the statute was not irrational and invidiously discriminatory.

State v. Senske


No. 42208


Supreme Court of Minnesota


291 Minn. 228; 190 N.W.2d 658; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1018



September 24, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Benjamin Arthur Senske from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Otis H. Godfrey, Jr., Judge, whereby he was convicted of aggravated robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of aggravated robbery. Defendant appealed his conviction on multiple grounds. Defendant had been identified after the robbery by a person who was present at the robbery after the person looked at some pictures at police headquarters. The person claimed that he attended school with defendant and stated that defendant was the robber on the sound of his voice and from his build and just from looking at him. Four eyewitnesses identified defendant as the robber although there were some inconsistencies in their testimony as to the robber's dress and appearance. There was other evidence that defendant had visited an apartment across from the site robbed with a gun in his possession and asked for a nylon stocking and that he returned later in the evening with $ 10 bills in his possession. The only witness for defendant had testified that he couldn't see what the robber had over his face but that his hair was blond. Since the jury accepted the testimony of the State's witnesses as the truth and defendant had not preserved objections, there was sufficient evidence in the record to support the conviction and the court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment against defendant.

Chandler v. Kroiss


No. 42730


Supreme Court of Minnesota


291 Minn. 196; 190 N.W.2d 472; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1012



September 10, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Class action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Wesley M. Chandler for himself and other affected property owners to challenge the validity of certain ordinances of defendant village of Shoreview; of a special-use permit issued by said village to defendants Raymond J. Kroiss and Margaret C. Kroiss upon application of defendant Ray Kroiss Construction, Inc., to allow construction of multiple-family dwellings on property owned by Raymond Kroiss; and of an amendment to said permit issued upon application of defendant Pemble Development, Inc. After findings, Ronald E. Hachey, Judge, that said ordinances, permit, and amendment were valid, plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner brought a class action on behalf of himself and all others similarly situated seeking judgment that a special-use permit granted to defendant developers by defendant village was invalid and that the ordinances under which the permit was granted were unconstitutional. The Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) denied relief and the landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first developer filed an application with the village council for an extension of the M-1 zoning and for a special-use permit for a planned unit development and filed a proposed plan of development for the entire property. After two hearings, the planning and zoning commission recommended approval of the application and the village council unanimously granted it. The second developer sought an amendment to the special-use permit for a portion of the acres covered; this amendment was approved. Affirming, the court rejected the landowner's contention that the developer should have applied for a variance rather than a special use permit to allow multiple dwellings in an R-1 zone. The ordinances in question, Shoreview, Minn., Mun. Code §§ 913.091 and 913.130 (1967), were specifically intended to give the village flexibility to allow substantial variances from the provisions of the Municipal Code by way of special use permits. The approval of the planned unit development amended the comprehensive plan to the extent the development did not conform to the plan. Although a resolution rather than a motion was required by § 913.130, the permit was not invalid on that basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying relief to the landowner.

In re Daly


No. 42174


Supreme Court of Minnesota


291 Minn. 488; 189 N.W.2d 176; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1058



July 16, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding for the discipline of Jerome Daly, an attorney at law of this state, upon a petition and accusation filed by the State Board of Law Examiners.



DISPOSITION: Disbarment ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The proceeding was before the court for the discipline of respondent attorney for numerous acts of unprofessional conduct.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was given every opportunity to explain or justify the alleged misconduct. Instead, he exhibited indifference to the proceedings and undertook to use the hearing before the referee as a forum for expounding his own views concerning the constitutionality of the Federal Reserve System and the validity of Federal Reserve notes, as well as the constitutionality of the civil procedure rules and the rules governing the conduct and discipline of attorneys. The court ordered disbarment. The court determined that the finding of the referee confirmed a pattern of conduct indicated by the attorney's contumacious behavior before the court which resulted in his temporary suspension from practice. The court concluded that the misconduct found by the referee, and demonstrated by the attorney's oral declarations before the court in violation of the canons of professional ethics, reflected professional irresponsibility to such a degree as to render the attorney totally unfit to continue to discharge the duties of his position.


OUTCOME: The attorney was ordered disbarred for his unprofessional conduct.

 

510 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Curtis


No. 42283


Supreme Court of Minnesota


290 Minn. 429; 190 N.W.2d 631; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1149



July 9, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by George Carpenter Curtis from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Edward D. Mulally, Judge, whereby he was convicted of possession of a narcotic drug.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) which convicted defendant of possession of marijuana in violation of Minn. Stat. § 618.02. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence of a search of defendant after a motor vehicle stop, determining that the search was reasonable as a search incident to an arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of marihuana. Defendant contended that the search, which resulted in the discovery of the marijuana following defendant's arrest for a minor traffic violation, was invalid. The police officers stopped defendant's motor vehicle after observing defective taillights and defendant turning without signaling. After the stop, defendant exited his vehicle and was pat-frisked. The police officer testified he felt an object in defendant's pocket, which did not appear to be a weapon. Upon searching the pocket, the marijuana was discovered. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress, holding that the search was reasonable as a search incident to an arrest. The court reversed defendant's conviction, holding that no search incident to an arrest was authorized for a routine arrest for a trivial traffic offense unless the police officer had reason to fear an assault or had probable cause for believing defendant had committed a more serious crime.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of marijuana and the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress.

Johnson v. Donovan


No. 42710


Supreme Court of Minnesota


290 Minn. 421; 188 N.W.2d 864; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1148



July 2, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court for a declaratory judgment to determine the validity of a tax on recreational vehicles. The court, Otis H. Godfrey, Jr., Judge, found for defendants, the secretary of state and the state, and plaintiffs, owners of such vehicles, appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, recreational vehicle owners, sought review of a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) in favor of appellees, the Secretary of State and the State of Minnesota, declaring valid a tax on recreational vehicles under 1969 Minn. Laws 824, §§ 2, 3.


OVERVIEW: The owners commenced a class action for a declaratory judgment, seeking to have the act declared invalid. The trial court held 1969 Minn. Laws 824 to be constitutionally valid. The only issue on appeal was whether the act contravened U.S. Const. amend. XIV, or Minn. Const. art. 9, § 1. The court held that the classification of recreational vehicles in 1969 Minn. Laws 824 was predicated upon a characteristic common to recreational vehicles and not to vehicles falling under other classifications. The court found no confiscation of property by failing to allow for depreciation of recreational vehicles because it was not a violation of the uniformity requirement, in that the length of time such equipment was used did not necessarily establish a decreased value of it. Age was not indicative of value. The language was not unconstitutionally vague because the terms used, such as "house trailer," "slip in camper," or "van," were terms that were in common usage and the owners had little difficulty in determining the applicability of the taxing statute to property so described. The decision of the trial court upholding the validity of 1969 Minn. Laws 824 was correct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

512 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Cleaver v. State


No. 42464


Supreme Court of Minnesota


290 Minn. 336; 187 N.W.2d 700; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1132



June 4, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Richard L. Cleaver from an order of the Hennepin County District Court, Thomas Tallakson, Judge, denying his petition for postconviction relief after a conviction of aggravated forgery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion for postconviction relief from his conviction for aggravated forgery.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of aggravated forgery and was committed to prison to serve a five-year sentence. Subsequently, the inmate was extradited to Tennessee for trial on an attempted armed robbery charge. The governors of Minnesota and Tennessee entered into an executive agreement pursuant to 1967 Tenn. Pub. Acts 270 and Minn. Stat. § 629.05 under which the inmate was to be returned to Minnesota upon demand of the executive authority of Minnesota. The inmate pleaded guilty of the Tennessee charge and began serving his sentence in Tennessee before he was returned to Minnesota to continue serving his sentence for aggravated forgery. The inmate sought postconviction relief on the ground that Minnesota lost jurisdiction over his person because of a breach of the executive agreement. The court affirmed the trial court's order denying relief. The executive agreement clearly provided that the inmate would be returned to Minnesota upon demand. By relinquishing temporary custody over the inmate to Tennessee, Minnesota did not surrender jurisdiction over him and upon his return to Minnesota it had the right to require him to complete his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

513 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Credit Service Co. v. Linnerooth


No. 42449


Supreme Court of Minnesota


290 Minn. 256; 187 N.W.2d 632; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1121



May 21, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Univac Division of Sperry Rand Corporation, garnishee, from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Eugene Minenko, Judge, allowing recovery by plaintiff, Credit Service Company, against said garnishee in an action brought by said plaintiff against Douglas Linnerooth and Mrs. Linnerooth.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Garnishee employer appealed a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which allowed plaintiff judgment creditor to recover funds that had been garnished from defendant judgment debtor's paycheck after the employer released those funds.


OVERVIEW: The creditor filed suit against the debtor and her husband. A default judgment was entered against them two years later. Prior to entry of the judgment, the creditor served a garnishment summons on the employer. The employer, however, released the funds that were subject to the garnishment when the United States Supreme Court declared that a Wisconsin statute permitting prejudgment garnishment of wages was unconstitutional and when the Minnesota Legislature amended the garnishment law, Minn. Stat. § 571.41 (1967), to prohibit garnishments before judgment except in certain cases. The trial court ordered the employer to pay the creditor the funds that had been released and the employer appealed. The court held that (1) the debtor had had an opportunity to be heard on the merits of the creditor's claim, but failed to exercise that right; (2) the creditor's right had vested under § 571.41 at the time of the garnishment proceedings because it had a right to enter judgment in the main case due to the debtor's default; and (3) the employer was under an obligation to continue to hold the debtor's funds subject to proceedings to have the funds applied on the creditor's claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Schoepke v. Alexander Smith & Sons Carpet Co.


No. 42497


Supreme Court of Minnesota


290 Minn. 518; 187 N.W.2d 133; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1168



May 14, 1971

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator employee challenged a decision of the Workmen's Compensation Commission (Minnesota), which denied the employee's petition vacate an award on stipulation against respondents, an employer and its insurer.


OVERVIEW: On December 21, 1949, the employee allegedly sustained an injury to his back arising out of and in the course of his employment. On September 8, 1950, a stipulation of settlement was reached among the parties. On October 8, 1969, the employee filed a petition to vacate the earlier award. In affirming, the court held the Minn. The court also determined that the employee's unsupported argument that questioned the Commission's sitting in judgment on a matter wherein the records had been destroyed was waived. The court found that because the employee did not give the Attorney General the requisite notice, the employee could not challenge the constitutionality of Minn. Stat. § 175.36. Finally, the court held that the Commission did not abuse its discretion in refusing to vacate the 1950 award based on stipulation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

515 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Leeper v. Hampton Hills, Inc.


No. 42355


Supreme Court of Minnesota


290 Minn. 143; 187 N.W.2d 765; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1106



April 23, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court for damages allegedly sustained by plaintiff landowners by reason of the lowering of the level of a lake and the establishment of a roadway across plaintiffs' property by defendant village of Plymouth. Hampton Hills, Inc., Kenneth G. Hampton, Sr., and Gordon J. Johnson were joined as defendants by reason of their alleged lowering of the lake level, trespass, and removal of trees from plaintiffs' property. The court, Douglas K. Amdahl, Judge, found that plaintiffs William T. Leeper and Lillian L. Leeper were entitled to recover from defendants Johnson, Hampton, and Hampton Hills only in the amount of $ 2,200, and said plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; remanded for further action in accordance with opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners challenged an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which failed to award damages in their trespass action under Minn. Stat. § 160,05, subd. 1, against defendant developers for the destruction of trees and shrubbery that were taken from their right-of-way.


OVERVIEW: The landowners brought an action to recover damages for trespass and unlawful appropriation of their land under Minn. Stat. § 160.05, subd. 1, claiming that the trail from their driveway was never established as a public road but was merely a part of their private property. The trial court disagreed, finding that the contested lane became a public road before the landowners purchased the property. On appeal, the court affirmed that finding because the trial court's application of the statute to the facts was justified by evidence that in 1946 the entire length of the lane was graveled and "crowned up," snowplow crews worked on the road, the road was graded, weeds were mowed, culverts were installed, and there was evidence of some public use of the contested portion of the road. Remand was required because the lower court made no findings of facts pertinent to wrongful removal of trees from the roadway or from the landowners' property and neither awarded nor denied recovery for the alleged wrong. Under Minn. Stat. § 160.22, the developers would be liable if they wilfully cut down trees on the property or in the roadway running through the landowners' property without permission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as to the public nature of a road and remanded the case for assessment of damages, if any, against the developers for the wrongful removal of trees from the landowners' property.

 

516 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Reutzel v. State Dep't of Highways


No. 42558


Supreme Court of Minnesota


290 Minn. 88; 186 N.W.2d 521; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1101



April 9, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition in the Stearns County District Court by Claudia Reutzel for reinstatement of her driver's license. The court, Paul Hoffman, Judge, found for petitioner, and the Department of Highways appealed from said order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Minnesota State Department of Highways appealed an order of the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota), which granted petitioner uninsured motorist's request for reinstatement of her driver's license after it was suspended under the Safety Responsibility Act, Minn. Stat. ch. 170.


OVERVIEW: The Safety Responsibility Act provided for the suspension of the license of any uninsured motorist after the commissioner received a report of an accident with damage in excess of a certain amount unless the driver deposited security in a sum determined sufficient by the commissioner. Such suspension was without a presuspension hearing. The district court held that the suspension provisions of the Act were unconstitutional and ordered the motorist's license returned. The court held that the absence of a statutory provision for a presuspension hearing did not deprive the motorist of due process. The court distinguished those cases, which found that prehearing deprivation of public assistance benefits unconstitutional. Public assistance benefits promoted more important governmental interests and provided a means by which to live. However, the court held that the commissioner's determination of the amount of security required had to be based upon competent evidence comprised, at least, of a sworn statement of the other motorist. That was not done in this case, and the motorist was entitled to the return of her license.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the district court's judgment, which found the Act unconstitutional, and affirmed that portion of the judgment that directed the return of the motorist's license.

 

517 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Travelers Ins. Co. v. Thompson


No. 42457


Supreme Court of Minnesota


289 Minn. 513; 184 N.W.2d 430; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1262



February 12, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions in the Ramsey County District Court brought by several insurance companies for a declaratory judgment that certain life insurance policies on the life of Carol S. Thompson are void. The court, J. H. Sylvestre, retired judge, granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, and defendant T. Eugene Thompson appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, beneficiary of deceased wife whom he was convicted of murdering, sought review of summary judgment from the Ramsey District Court (Minnesota), contending that such judgment debarring him from collecting the proceeds on his wife's life insurance policies violated Minn. Stat. § 631.471 which protected the property rights of convicts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, beneficiary of deceased wife whom he was convicted of killing, sought review of summary judgment contending that such judgment debarring him from collecting the proceeds on his wife's life insurance policies violated Minn. Stat. § 631.471, which protected the property rights of convicts. On appeal, summary judgment was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that the mandate ordering summary judgment did not violate § 631.471 by forfeiting property rights appellant had as owner and beneficiary of the policies for the reason that it was not his conviction of murder which barred appellant's claims against insurers, but the fact of the murder which gave rise to the conviction. The court further held that appellant's felonious acts defeated what interest he might have had in the proceeds from the insurance policies. The court also held that there was no constitutional violation of appellant's contractual rights, as there was no forfeiture within the meaning of § 631.471.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was affirmed, as the mandate ordering summary judgment did not violate appellant rights by forfeiting his property interest as owner and beneficiary of the insurance policies for the reason that it was not his conviction of murder which barred appellant's claims against insurers, but the fact of the murder which gave rise to the conviction.

 

518 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Sorenson v. Minneapolis-St. Paul Metropolitan Airports Com.


No. 42416


Supreme Court of Minnesota


289 Minn. 207; 183 N.W.2d 292; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1208



January 22, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff at airport owned and operated by defendant. The court, David E. Marsden, Judge, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action, appellant traveler challenged the judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) granting the motion of respondent Minneapolis-St. Paul Metropolitan Airports Commission (MAC) for summary judgment and dismissing the traveler's complaint for failure to provide notice of his claim within 30 days under Minn. Stat. § 466.05, subd. 1.


OVERVIEW: The traveler brought a personal injury action against the MAC. The trial court granted the MAC's motion for summary judgment, holding that the traveler had failed to give written notice of the alleged accident within 30 days as required by Minn. Stat. § 466.05, subd. 1, because the Mac was a public corporation. On review, the traveler argued that there was no clear legislative mandate that § 466.05, subd. 1 was intended to apply to the MAC, and supported his argument with a case holding that § 466.05, subd. 1 did not apply to a housing redevelopment authority. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgment, finding that a distinction existed between the traveler's cited case and the present case. The court reasoned that a personal injury claim asserted agsint a private corporation was different that one asserted against a public cooperation. There was no legislative intention that the MAC was to be treated other than as a public corporation for the notice of claim statute. The court also found that § 466.05, subd. 1did not violate Minn. Const. art. 4, § 27, which prohibited a law embracing more than one subject because its title made clear that it applied to tort liability.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

519 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schotl


No. 41420


Supreme Court of Minnesota


289 Minn. 175; 182 N.W.2d 878; 1971 Minn. LEXIS 1202



January 15, 1971 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Willard Schotl from a judgment of the Stearns County District Court, E. J. Ruegemer, Judge, whereby he was convicted of burglary, and from an order denying his alternative motion for judgment of acquittal notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Stearns County (Minnesota), convicting defendant of burglary in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.58, subd. 2(2) (1967).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction on the grounds that the search and seizure of his room was unconstitutional and that all the elements of the offense of burglary was not met. The court affirmed. First, the court held that a parent in control of premises in which a child resided could consent to a search thereof even though it might produce incriminating evidence. In the final analysis, the test of the constitutionality of a warrantless search was reasonableness and that the issue of reasonableness was one of fact and depended upon the particular circumstances in each case. The record showed that the mother had apparent authority over the entire premises and that defendant was not a tenant although defendant made a payment. There was evidence that defendant occupied the room with his siblings. Thus, the mother's consent to search was proper. Second, the court held that the premises was a dwelling under § 609.58 because access to the owner's living quarters, which was adjacent to the store premises, was easily accessible by opening a hall door.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

520 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hoene v. Jamieson


No. 41642


Supreme Court of Minnesota


289 Minn. 1; 182 N.W.2d 834; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1285



December 11, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Record Certified to United States Supreme Court April 16, 1971.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by John V. Hoene and Duininck Bros. & Gilchrist for a declaratory judgment invalidating a provision of the Tax Reform and Relief Act of 1967 and enjoining the state commissioner of highways, commissioner of taxation, and auditor from acting in accordance with it. The court, Harold W. Schultz, Judge, granted defendants' motion for summary judgment, and plaintiffs appealed from said order and from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to purchases by contractors; reversed as to purchases by the state.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractors filed a declaratory judgment action, seeking a determination that Minn. Stat. § 297A.25, subd. 4, permitting a sales tax on road-building materials purchased by contractors, was unconstitutional. The Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) upheld the statute and, on appeal, the court reversed that judgment. Defendants, various state officers, were granted a petition for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated that § 297A.25, subd. 4 was a severable provision in its entirety but not severable within itself. The contractors claimed that the sales tax on direct purchases of road-building material by the State of Minnesota was an unconstitutional diversion to the property tax relief fund of trunk highway funds protected by Minn. Const. art. XIV, that by stipulation, subd. 4 was not severable within itself, and therefore the tax was also unconstitutional as to purchases by contractors. The court ruled that: (1) because the question of severability was one of law and because the matter was of great public moment, the court was not bound by the parties' stipulation; (2) the exemptions from the sales tax on purchases of highway material both by contractors and by the State, provided in § 297A.25, subd. 4, were severable as a matter of law; (3) the purchase of materials by the contractors for use in the construction of state highways was not an unconstitutional invasion of the state trunk highway fund; and (4) the imposition of the sales tax on direct purchases by the State was an unconstitutional diversion from the trunk highway fund to the property tax relief fund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the district court's judgment that upheld the constitutionality of the statute as applied to contractors and reversed that part of the judgment that upheld the constitutionality of the statute as applied to the State.

Head v. Special School Dist.


Nos. 42734, 42747, 42766, 42852


Supreme Court of Minnesota


288 Minn. 496; 182 N.W.2d 887; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1048; 75 L.R.R.M. 2880



December 9, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought by Douglas M. Head, attorney general of the State of Minnesota, for a declaratory judgment declaring null and void certain provisions of two resolutions of defendant Special School District No. 1 and to enjoin said defendant and defendant Minneapolis Federation of Teachers, Local No. 59, from acting pursuant to said provisions. Keith W. Davidson, Katherine V. Howard, Harvey A. Ring, and Betty K. Robb were permitted to intervene as plaintiffs on behalf of themselves and other taxpayers. On the basis of a stipulation of facts, the court, Thomas Tallakson, Judge, ordered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, and defendant school board and defendant union each appealed from the order and from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, school district and teachers' union, appealed the order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which permanently enjoined defendant school district from making payment to striking Minneapolis school teachers pursuant to an agreement for increased wages and benefits negotiated between defendant board of education and defendants, Minneapolis Federation of Teachers (MFT) and City of Minneapolis Education Association (CMEA).


OVERVIEW: Defendant board obtained temporary restraining orders against defendants MFT and CMEA and restrained them from participating in a strike as defined in Minn. Stat. § 179.51. Despite the temporary restraining orders, certain teachers continued to strike. Pursuant to Resolution A, the board rehired the striking teachers and intended to pay to each of them an amount equivalent to the difference in pay between what that teacher was paid during the 1970-1971 school year and what the teacher would have been paid if the teacher had been employed at the appropriate step. Pursuant to Resolution B, the board paid each of the striking teachers for seven days during the strike period. Plaintiff, the attorney general of the State of Minnesota, brought this action to determine the legality of Resolutions A and B. The trial court issued a permanent injunction that prohibited the school board from paying the compensation provided by the resolutions. The court affirmed and found that once a person violated the provisions of § 179.51, the employment was automatically terminated by Minn. Stat. § 179.54. Thus, no compensation could be made to the striking teachers for the period of non-employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and judgment of the trial court and found that the statutes were constitutional and that no payments or compensation could be made to the striking teachers for the period of their non-employment.

Americans United Inc. As Protestants, etc. v. Ind. School Dist.


Nos. 42351, 42352


Supreme Court of Minnesota


288 Minn. 196; 179 N.W.2d 146; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1005; 41 A.L.R.3d 328



August 7, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Record Certified to United States Supreme Court September 23, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two actions in the Ramsey County District Court, one by Americans United Incorporated as Protestants and Other Americans United for Separation of Church and State, Ralston Gunvaldson, and Ronald G. Krause against Duane J. Mattheis, commissioner of education, William J. O'Brien, the state auditor, Independent School District No. 622, Ramsey County, and the members of its school board, seeking a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of L. 1969, c. 570, and injunctive relief against the expenditure of public funds for transporting school children to privately maintained sectarian schools, and the other a taxpayer's suit by Matthew Stark against the commissioner of education, the state auditor, and the members of the State Board of Education, seeking the same relief. In the first action the court, Harold W. Schultz, Judge, permitted intervention by John D. Thurston, Daniel Barrett, and Curt Rhode, minors, by their parents and natural guardians, David W. Thurston, William E. Barrett, and James R. Rhode, and by said parents individually. Following consolidation and submission of the cases on stipulated [***2] facts, the court, David E. Marsden, Judge, determined that the act was constitutional. Plaintiffs appealed from the judgment in each case.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, taxpayers and organizations, brought separate actions challenging the constitutionality of 1969 Minn. Laws 570, which authorized the use of public funds to transport children to sectarian schools. The actions were consolidated and the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) determined that the statute was constitutional. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellants claimed that the statute violated the state constitutional provisions that prohibited public taxation for a private purpose and that prohibited the appropriation of public money for the support of schools wherein the distinctive doctrines of a religious faith were promulgated or taught. Appellants also claimed that the statute violated the state and federal constitutional prohibitions of establishment of religion. The court held that although the statute went to the verge of constitutional power, it did not go beyond. The court found that the statute served a legitimate secular purpose in promoting the safety and welfare of children required to attend school under compulsory attendance laws. The court also found that although the statute somewhat encouraged attendance in sectarian schools, its purpose and primary effect was neither to benefit religion nor to support sectarian schools. The court ruled that whatever support the statute gave to sectarian schools was purely incidental and that the statute was a valid exercise of the state's police power in promoting public welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments that found that the challenged statute was constitutional in appellants' consolidated actions for a declaratory judgment that the statute was invalid.

Knapp v. O'Brien


No. 42368


Supreme Court of Minnesota


288 Minn. 103; 179 N.W.2d 88; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 996



July 24, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment brought in the Ramsey County District Court by John Knapp, John J. Todd, and Leif R. Langsjoen, individually and as members of the Tax Court to test the validity of a statute providing for their salary. The state auditor was named as defendant, and Nicholas D. Coleman, Stanley W. Holmquist, Gordon Rosenmeier, Aubrey W. Dirlam, Robert W. Johnson, and Martin O. Sabo, members of the Senate and House of Representatives, intervened as plaintiffs. On the basis of stipulated facts, the court, J. Jerome Plunkett, Judge, found the statute void, and plaintiffs and intervenors appealed from the judgment entered.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, court employees, and intervenors, senators and representatives, appealed the decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which awarded summary judgment to respondent, auditor of the State of Minnesota, and found 1969 Minn. Laws 1125 unconstitutional and void. The court found that the passage of § 1125 contravened Minn. Const. art. 4, §§ 1, 22 because it was passed after the expiration of 120 legislative days.


OVERVIEW: An employee of the Minnesota Tax Court as well as some state senators and representatives sought to have 1969 Minn. Laws 1125 enforced. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's award of summary judgment to the auditor.

Steeves v. State


No. 41739


Supreme Court of Minnesota


287 Minn. 476; 178 N.W.2d 723; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1145



June 30, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Henry Albert Steeves from an order of the Hennepin County District Court, Tom Bergin, Judge, denying his petition for postconviction relief after he was convicted of possession of narcotic drugs.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) denying his petition for post-conviction relief after he was convicted of possession of narcotic drugs and his probation for that offense was revoked upon his pleading guilty to burglary.


OVERVIEW: Police were searching the home of an acquaintance of petitioner when they observed petitioner and the acquaintance starting to enter the home. Petitioner had a gun. There was a struggle with the police; petitioner ran into the street and was shot by police. A search of petitioner produced a pink pill called Percodan-Demi. Petitioner argued that this was cocaine, and that he should have been charged under Minn. Stat. § 618.081 rather than Minn. Stat. §§ 618.01, 618.02, and 618.21. Affirming, the court held that the evidence at the hearing showed that Percodan-Demi was an entirely different and separate drug from codeine. If the legislature had intended to include Percodan-Demi (oxycodone) within Minn. Stat. § 618.081, it would have included it by name. Petitioner's sentence of 10 years' imprisonment was not cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution because the sentence was one-half of what petitioner could have received under Minn. Stat. § 618.21. The search of petitioner was reasonable and constitutionally valid as an incident to a lawful arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying post-conviction relief to petitioner.

 

525 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nomiya


No. 42531


Supreme Court of Minnesota


287 Minn. 487; 178 N.W.2d 905; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1147



June 30, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Karen Darlene Nomiya from an order of the St. Louis County District Court, Donald C. Odden, Judge, denying her petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota) denied appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was prosecuted and acquitted of second degree murder by reason of insanity. Appellant was committed to a mental hospital. Subsequently, the medical director of the hospital advised the trial court by letter that appellant had recovered and that no person or persons would be endangered by her discharge from confinement. The court agreed with appellant that the district court did not have power to refuse the release of anyone whose recovery had been certified under Minn. Stat. § 631.19. The other question was whether the letter of the hospital's medical director satisfied the requirement of § 631.19 that the patient's recovery be certified by the superintendent of the hospital where the person was confined. The court held that the term "superintendent" had to be understood to refer to the authority exercised by the official certifying the patient's recovery, rather than limiting the application of § 631.19 to certifications made by officials with the title of "superintendent." The medical director of a state hospital exercised the authority of the superintendent and his certification of the patient's recovery invoked the provisions of § 631.19.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court judgment and remanded the matter with instructions to enter an order of discharge.

 

526 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnesota Asso. of Public Schools v. Hanson


No. 42095


Supreme Court of Minnesota


287 Minn. 415; 178 N.W.2d 846; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1139



June 26, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Declaratory judgment action in the Otter Tail County District Court brought by the Minnesota Association of Public Schools and certain individual teachers contesting the validity of L. 1967, c. 833. Kenneth Hanson, auditor of Otter Tail County; the members of the county board; and Duane J. Mattheis, commissioner of education, were named as defendants. The court, Chester G. Rosengren, Judge, granted motions by defendants for dismissal of the action, and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a public school association and individual teachers, appealed the judgment of the Otter Tail County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed their complaint against defendants, a county auditor, county board members, and the education commissioner, seeking a declaration of unconstitutionality of Minn. Stat. §§ 122.41 to 122.52.


OVERVIEW: The statute at issue required that all school districts not maintaining classified elementary and secondary schools on July 1, 1970 be dissolved and attached to districts that did maintain such schools. Plaintiffs claimed that the section violated the equal protection clause by making an unreasonable classification of the schools, persons, and properties affected by the law and thereby denying the pupils in the excepted districts the benefits of better educational opportunities. The trial court dismissed plaintiffs' action, and the court affirmed. The court held that the association was asserting rights that only belonged to the pupils, and therefore no justiciable controversy existed between the association and defendants. Further, there was no impairment of the teachers' contractual rights resulting from the enactment of the statute as the teachers who would be affected by the law would be treated no differently than they would if they were in any other district. In addition, the affected teachers were not denied due process of law, and the statute was a valid exercise of the state's police powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

527 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Pakarinen


No. 41833


Supreme Court of Minnesota


287 Minn. 330; 178 N.W.2d 714; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1128



June 19, 1970 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Record Certified to United States Supreme Court September 15, 1970.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Dorothy Jeannette Hietala from an order of the St. Louis County District Court, Donald E. Anderson, Judge, dismissing her appeal from the final decree of distribution issued by the probate court of said county in the estate of Peter Pakarinen and adjudging Helmi Kilpela to be the sole heir of said decedent.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant illegitimate child challenged a judgment of the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota), which dismissed her appeal from the probate court's order decreeing the decedent's estate to respondent decedent's sister. The district court found that the decedent did not formally acknowledge the illegitimate child to be his child as required by Minn. Stat. § 525.172. The illegitimate child challenged the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The illegitimate child's birth certificate named the decedent as the father and upon his plea of guilty in a paternity proceeding, the decedent was adjudged by a district court to be the father of the illegitimate child. The child asserted that § 525.172 violated equal protection because it created a distinction in the proof necessary for an illegitimate child to inherent as opposed to a legitimate child. The court affirmed the judgment of the district court. The court held as follows: 1) Minn. Stat. § 525.172 absolutely precluded inheritance by an illegitimate child from a putative father in all cases where the father died intestate without making the attested written declaration of paternity required by the statute; 2) an adjudication of paternity designed to fix liability for support of the child did not confer any right of inheritance and was not the equivalent of the required statutory proof; and 3) the distinction drawn by the legislature was a rational classification because it bore intelligible relation to the purpose of the descent statutes, which were designed to give effect to the presumed desires of a decedent who died intestate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court dismissing the illegitimate child's appeal from the decree of the probate court giving the estate to the decedent's sister.

 

528 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Wuertz v. Garvey


Nos. 42188, 42189, 42263


Supreme Court of Minnesota


287 Minn. 353; 178 N.W.2d 630; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1131



June 19, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals arising out of two actions. One action was brought in the Meeker County District Court by James Wuertz for personal injuries allegedly sustained in an accident involving a hydraulic cylinder owned by defendant Michael Garvey and a tractor owned and operated by defendant Francis Garvey, which tractor and cylinder were manufactured by defendant Deere and Company. In that action defendants Garvey filed a cross-claim against defendant Deere and Company. The other action was brought in the Todd County District Court by Erven Zabel for personal injuries allegedly sustained in an accident involving a combine manufactured by defendant Deere and Company and sold by defendants John Deere Company of Minneapolis and Lux Hardware and Furniture Company. Defendant Deere and Company appealed from orders, Sam G. Gandrud and Chester G. Rosengren, Judges, denying its motions to dismiss the actions or to quash the service of the summons on it in each action and to dismiss the cross-claim in the first action.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff's products liability action, defendant manufacturer sought review from an order of the District Court, Meeker County (Minnesota), which denied the manufacturer's motion to dismiss or quash. In third party plaintiff's cross claim in a related action, the manufacturer sought review from a judgment of the District Court, Todd County (Minnesota), which had also denied the manufacturer's motion to dismiss or quash.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff and third party plaintiff sued the manufacturer for personal injuries cause by machinery made by the manufacturer, and served the manufacturer, a foreign corporation, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 303.13. The manufacturer moved to dismiss the actions against it, or, in the alternative to quash service in each action, arguing that § 303.13 violated due process because it required a determination of whether the manufacturer had made contracted with a state resident or committed a tort in the state before a trial on the merits. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that § 303.13 did not violate due process because it only required a prima facie showing that the manufacturer either contracted with a resident or committed a tort in the state. Plaintiff and third party plaintiff still had to prove the facts necessary to establish jurisdiction, as well as the facts necessary to prove negligence at trial by a preponderance of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the manufacturer's motion to dismiss or, alternatively, to quash service.

OVERVIEW: The case was brought to establish the validity of the action of the city, a municipal corporation, and of members of the city council of said city to effect the sale of $ 3,000,000 in revenue bonds to finance the purchase of land located near the city and the erection of a meat packing plant thereon. 530 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Olsen v. State


No. 41413


Supreme Court of Minnesota


287 Minn. 536; 177 N.W.2d 424; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1165



May 15, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Arnold P. Olsen from an order of the Ramsey County District Court, John W. Graff, Judge, denying his petition for postconviction relief after he was convicted of confining his own child to prevent his former wife from obtaining custody pursuant to an existing court order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief after he was found guilty of confining his children to prevent his ex-wife from obtaining custody in violation of Minn. Stat. Ann. § 609.26 (1965).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to one year in the county workhouse and given a fine for his conviction. The trial court denied appellant's motion for post-conviction relief and the court affirmed. It was previously determined in another decision that the evidence was sufficient to sustain the verdict convicting appellant. The court held that there was no showing that the county attorney discriminated against appellant by prosecuting him because the ex-wife's denial of appellant's visitation rights was not proscribed by Minn. Stat. Ann. § 609.26 (1965). Appellant's sentence and fine did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the Eighth Amendment and the county attorney's refusal to make appellant's children available as witnesses did not violate any of appellant's constitutional rights. The court held that the corroboration by the children was not required for a conviction under § 609.26 and that the absence of the children was immaterial as other competent evidence supported the conviction. The statute was not violative of equal protection and was not unconstitutionally vague even though amendments to the statute both broadened and narrowed its application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which denied appellant's motion for postconviction relief after he was convicted of confining his children to prevent his ex-wife from obtaining custody.

 

531 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Edwards


No. 41742


Supreme Court of Minnesota


287 Minn. 83; 177 N.W.2d 40; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1084



May 1, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Brenda Edwards from an order of the Hennepin County Municipal Court, Chester Durda, Judge, denying her motion for dismissal of a charge of operating a motorcycle without protective headgear, and from a judgment whereby she was convicted of the charge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Hennepin County Municipal Court (Minnesota), which denied her motion for dismissal of a charge of operating a motorcycle without protective headgear in violation of Minn. Stat. § 169.974, subd. 4(a), and from a judgment that convicted her of the charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant urged that § 169.974, subd. 4(a) had no relation to public welfare and safety, did not promote the general welfare, invaded fundamental rights, and denied to motorcyclists equal protection of the laws. She argued that § 169.974, subd. 4(a) exceeded the police power of the State because it protected the motorcyclist from self-harm with no concomitant benefits to the public health, safety, or welfare. The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that the question of whether § 169.974, subd. 4(a) bore a real and substantial relation to the public health, safety, and welfare and whether it was unreasonable or arbitrary were questions that were committed to the judgment of the legislative body. Unless the decisions of that body on those questions appeared to be clearly erroneous, the court would not interfere. The court determined that the legislature had plenary power over the regulation of the privilege to use the highways for the safety and best interests of the public. Because public highways had long been recognized as an appropriate subject of the police power, the court concluded that regulations could be established governing the use and the users of highways.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order and judgment.

Minneapolis Star & Tribune Co. v. Commissioner of Taxation


No. 42029


Supreme Court of Minnesota


287 Minn. 117; 177 N.W.2d 33; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1088



May 1, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Minneapolis Star and Tribune Company to review a decision of the Tax Court which sustained an order of the commissioner of taxation relating to the excise tax imposed on relator for the taxable year ending February 24, 1962.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator taxpayer sought review of a judgment from Tax Court (Minnesota), which affirmed the decision of the Commissioner of Taxation to disallow a deduction for certain net operating losses under Minn. Stat. § 290.095, subd. 4(d, h).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a corporation, organized a subsidiary corporation, which acquired and operated a newspaper in another state. The newspaper was liquidated and the subsidiary's net operating loss was deducted from the taxpayer's income tax return. The tax court affirmed the Commissioner's denial of the deduction. First, the court held that the written consent for extension of the time in which to assess taxes prepared by the commissioner and delivered to the taxpayer, thereafter timely signed by the taxpayer and redelivered to the commissioner, was a sufficient compliance with Minn. Stat. § 290.49, subd. 8. Next, the court held that Minn. Stat. § 290.095, subd. 4(d) disallowed deduction by a parent corporation of the carryover of a net operating loss sustained by a subsidiary corporation, to which the parent corporation succeeded under Minn. Stat. § 290.138, subd. 1, upon liquidation of the subsidiary, where the subsidiary's income-producing activities causing the loss were not carried on in Minnesota.

533 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Schultz v. Chicago & N. R. Co.


No. 41804


Supreme Court of Minnesota


286 Minn. 231; 175 N.W.2d 177; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1211



February 27, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Five actions in the Scott County District Court arising out of a collision between an automobile driven by defendant Edith E. Schultz and a train operated by defendant Chicago and Northwestern Railway Company. The injured plaintiffs were all minor children of defendant Schultz, and the court, Harold E. Flynn, Judge, granted her motion for summary judgment in her favor. Plaintiffs, including Arnold J. Schultz, the father of the injured plaintiffs, who sought consequential damages, appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, five injured children with their father as representative, sought review of a judgment from the Scott County District Court (Minnesota), which granted defendant mother's motion for summary judgment in plaintiffs' suit for consequential damages arising out of a collision between an automobile driven by the mother and a train operated by defendant railway company.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' causes of action accrued in 1966. The trial court held that the child-parent immunity rule in negligence cases applied to their actions. Plaintiffs contended that an exception should be made, as in another case, to the rule that child-parent tort immunity was abrogated only as to causes of action arising on or after September 27, 1968. Plaintiffs also argued that to draw a line created a favored class in violation of the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Minn. Const. art. 1, § 2, and Minn. Const. art. 4, § 33. The court affirmed the judgment, finding that plaintiffs did not actively or passively participate in the designation of another action as a case that would test the continued validity of an established doctrine. The court found that the equity in the appeal brought by plaintiffs, who were explicitly informed through the other case of the court's probable decision in their appeal, did not warrant the making of another exception. Additionally, the court determined that there were no constitutional restrictions on the part of a court in any case to decide whether the force of its decision should operate prospectively or retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

534 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


St. Paul v. Franklin


Nos. 41579, 41561


Supreme Court of Minnesota


286 Minn. 194; 175 N.W.2d 16; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1203



February 20, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two appeals were consolidated for hearing in this court, one by Lewis Franklin and Charlene G. Franklin from a judgment of the municipal court of the city of St. Paul, Allan Markert, Judge, whereby they were convicted of violating a city ordinance against operating a disorderly house; and one by Jose Flood, also known as Clarence Flood, from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, David E. Marsden, Judge, whereby he was convicted of violating the same ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, defendants sought review of judgments from the Municipal Court of the City of St. Paul (Minnesota) and from the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted them of violating St. Paul, Minn., Code 469.01, a St. Paul city ordinance against operating a disorderly house.


OVERVIEW: Defendants asserted that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and that it was in conflict with Minn. Stat. § 609.33. The court affirmed the judgments, finding that defendants' constitutional attack sought to invalidate the ordinance in toto. The court determined that as defendants framed their attack on the ordinance, it would compel the court to ignore completely the conduct of defendants that gave rise to their prosecutions. The court found that the prevailing practice was to refuse to hold a statute unconstitutionally vague unless required to do so by a consideration of facts particular to the case to which the facts applied. The court concluded that defendants' challenge provided no factual basis for determining whether the ordinance, as applied to the conduct for which they were convicted, was so vague as to require defendants to guess whether their conduct was prohibited. Consequently, the court held that defendants failed to establish that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague on its face and declined to pass upon purely hypothetical issues. Likewise, there was no factual basis to support defendants' argument that the ordinance forbade what § 609.33 permitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

535 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Jones Press, Inc. v. Motor Travel Services, Inc.


No. 42138


Supreme Court of Minnesota


286 Minn. 205; 176 N.W.2d 87; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1205



February 20, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court for an alleged conversion, in which action plaintiff instituted garnishment proceedings. The court, Edward J. Parker, Judge, denied defendant's motion for an order terminating the garnishment bond, and this court granted its petition for discretionary review of said order.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtor sought review of the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his motion for an order terminating the garnishment bond in favor of plaintiff creditor.


OVERVIEW: The court granted a discretionary appeal pursuant to Minn. R. Civ. App. P. 105 to test the constitutionality of the garnishment statutes, Minn. Stat. §§ 571.41, 571.42, and 571.60 (1967). The creditor sued the debtor alleging a wrongful conversion of lithographic negatives by the debtor. The creditor garnished the debtor's accounts receivables. Faced with more garnishments the debtor sought a restraining order to prohibit further garnishments, but was denied relief, which required the debtor to secure a bond. The trial court denied the debtor's motion for an order canceling and terminating the garnishment bond. On review, the court reversed. The economic burden that the debtor sustained stemmed directly from the garnishment proceedings. It inflicted a hardship that was different only in form and not in substance. The court held that the garnishment of accounts receivable without prior notice or an opportunity to be heard rendered the garnishment statutes unconstitutional. There was no rational distinction between a livelihood dependent on wages and one derived from the sale of services and goods.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

State v. La Rose


No. 41390


Supreme Court of Minnesota


286 Minn. 517; 174 N.W.2d 247; 1970 Minn. LEXIS 1254



January 30, 1970 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Miles LaRose from a judgment of the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey County, Clifford Janes, Judge, whereby he was convicted of tampering with a motor vehicle.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Municipal Court of St. Paul, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted him of tampering with a motor vehicle in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.605(9).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found in a shopping center sitting with a screwdriver in his hand in the automobile of another owner. It was later determined that the lock on the glove compartment had been punched out. Defendant was detained by the owner and a companion until the police arrived, after which the owner perfected a formal citizen's arrest. In the interim, defendant told the owner that he was in the car to keep warm. The owner testified at trial that defendant stated that it was people like the owner that made it hard on people like defendant, adding, "You know, my wife will kill me for this." Defendant was convicted, and on appeal, the court affirmed, holding that defendant's Miranda rights were not violated because Miranda was directed at custodial police interrogation and had no application to a citizen's arrest. The court also held that the statute under which defendant was convicted, Minn. Stat. § 609.605(9), was constitutional under the circumstances of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

O'Brien v. St. Paul


No. 41458


Supreme Court of Minnesota


285 Minn. 378; 173 N.W.2d 462; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 992



December 26, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by property owners Michael O'Brien, Harry Bratnober, William M. Dempsey, and Steven H. Hoetzel for a declaratory judgment invalidating a purported rezoning of real property in defendant city and enjoining said city, Service to Builders, Inc., and Marvin Perlman from making certain improvements pursuant to said rezoning. The court, Arthur A. Stewart, retired judge, found for plaintiffs, and defendants Service to Builders, Inc., and Perlman appealed from the judgment entered. Plaintiffs filed a notice of review as to order denying their motion for amended findings.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the builder and the property owner, sought review of the judgment by the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), holding that the requirement in Minn. Stat. § 462.357, subd. 5 and the city's code that the owner obtain written consent of two-thirds of the adjoining property neighbors prior to rezoning a property was valid. Thus, the trial court prohibited the city council's rezoning and awarded judgment to plaintiff neighbors.


OVERVIEW: The landowner filed a petition with the city clerk of the city requesting that his property be rezoned to permit the construction of apartment buildings. The land in the area had been zoned single or two-family residential for nearly 45 years. The petition did not contain the written consent of the owners of two-thirds of the neighbors located within 100 feet of the property sought to be rezoned as required by Minn. Stat. § 462.357 and the city's ordinance. The city council then passed an ordinance exempting the property owner's property from the consent requirement. The trial court held that the consent statute and ordinance were Constitutional and valid and that the rezoning was a nullity. The court held that the consent statute and ordinance did not illegal vest in the adjoining property holders the power to legislate or impose unreasonable restrictions. Rather these laws conferred only the right to waive legislatively imposed restrictions that were already in place. The court noted their concern by the council to change the appearance of a neighborhood that had for so long retained the same zoning classification without consent of the neighbors in that neighborhood.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the neighbors in the neighbors' declaratory action against the builder and property owner regarding the rezoning of the property.

Le Roy v. Special Independent School Dist.


No. 41870


Supreme Court of Minnesota


285 Minn. 236; 172 N.W.2d 764; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 971



November 28, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought by taxpayers of Special School District No. 1 of the city of Minneapolis to test the constitutionality of a statute relating to said school district and prescribing procedures for establishing its mill rate for tax purposes. The school district, its Board of Education, the auditor and treasurer of Hennepin County, the city of Minneapolis, and its Board of Estimate and Taxation were named as defendants. The court, William D. Gunn, Judge, granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment by the District Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota), which denied the taxpayers relief in their action against appellees, a school district, its board of estimate and taxation, and others, to test the constitutionality of 1967 Minn. Laws ch. 661, § 5.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought to test the constitutionality of 1967 Minn. Laws ch. 661, § 5, the statute which prescribed the procedure for establishing the school district's mill rate for tax purposes. The trial court denied the taxpayers relief. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the court rejected the taxpayers' contention that the statute violated the separation-of-powers doctrine. Moreover, the court found that the title of the statute conformed with the requirements of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 27. The court further found no merit in the taxpayers' argument that the statute permitted the board of estimate to limit the mill rate without regard to uniformity. The court rejected the taxpayer's claim that the statute vested the judicial power of vetoing the mill-rate increase proposed by the board of education in a non-judicial body, the board of estimate and taxation. The court so held based on its finding that the function imposed on the board of estimate and taxation by the statute was not judicial. The court found no merit in the taxpayers' remaining contentions and, thus, concluded that the trial court committed no error in denying the taxpayers relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Supreme Court of Minnesota


285 Minn. 51; 171 N.W.2d 695; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 950

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Norman J. Mastrian from a judgment of the St. Louis County District Court, Donald C. Odden, Judge, whereby he was convicted of murder in the first degree; and from orders denying motions for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment and orders of the St. Louis County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of murder in the first degree and denied his post-conviction motions for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from the trial court's judgment of conviction and orders denying his motions for a new trial, and argued that he was entitled to be retried based upon numerous errors. Among defendant's claimed errors was his assertion that his arrest was illegal because the arresting officers acted without authority and outside of their jurisdiction. Th officers erroneously arrested defendant in the home of a third party after breaking down the door. The officers were not in pursuit of defendant, nor was there any threat that he was about to flee the jurisdiction. The court found that although the arrest was technically invalid under Minn. Stat. Ann. § 629.34, defendant was not entitled to a new trial because no improper evidence was seized or introduced as a result of the arrest and defendant had not been prejudiced. The court also agreed with defendant that certain procedural errors had been committed by the trial court in it selection of the grand jury and other matters, however, the court determined the errors, even in accumulation, did not act to deprive defendant of a fair trial, and affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment and orders of the trial court, which convicted defendant of murder in the first degree and denied his motions for a new trial, were affirmed.

State v. Boyce


No. 41397


Supreme Court of Minnesota


284 Minn. 242; 170 N.W.2d 104; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1044



August 1, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Donald Theodore Boyce from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Edward D. Mulally, Judge, whereby he was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree and from an order denying his motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which entered a conviction for manslaughter in the first degree and denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim lived in the same neighborhood and had a history of hostility. Defendant shot the victim in what he claimed was an attempt to defend himself from an assault by the victim and another man acting in combination. Defendant was much smaller than the other two men. Defendant retreated to his front yard before shooting the victim. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence did not support the verdict. The court reversed the conviction and ordered a new trial. Although the trial court's determination was supported by the evidence, the court concluded that the evidence should have been assessed by a jury notwithstanding defendant's request for a bench trial. The court held that even though the killing was intentional, defendant should not have been found guilty of manslaughter in the first degree if the killing was justifiable or excusable according to standards established by Minn. Stat. §§ 609.06, 609.065. The court noted that the case was an extraordinary wherein the court entertained such grave doubts as to defendant's guilt that the interests of justice required a new trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed, and new trial was ordered.

 

541 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Farmington v. Minnesota Municipal Com.


Nos. 41344, 41345, 41346, 41347


Supreme Court of Minnesota


284 Minn. 125; 170 N.W.2d 197; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1029



July 11, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 284 Minn. 125 at 139.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceedings in the Dakota County District Court upon petitions for review of actions of the Minnesota Municipal Commission in failing to approve the annexation of certain land to the Village of Farmington and in ordering the merger of the Town of Lakeville with the Village of Lakeville. The court, Robert J. Breunig, Judge, affirmed the commission, and the Village of Farmington and certain of the petitioners for review appealed from the orders of the district court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, village #1 and landowners, sought review of a judgment from the Dakota County District Court (Minnesota), which affirmed the actions of respondent Minnesota Municipal Commission that granted a petition to consolidate a township with village #2 and denied a petition to annex certain land of the township to village #2.


OVERVIEW: Village #1 sought to annex some property. Village #2, the neighboring village, was seeking to consolidate the same land. The trial court affirmed an order of the Minnesota Municipal Commission granting a petition to consolidate the township with village #2 and affirmed the Commission's statutory denial of a petition to annex 195 acres of the township to village #1. Village #1 and landowners contended that neither of the rulings of the Commission were justified by the evidence. The court held that the Commission's consolidation order had to be vacated because it was ambiguous when a specific finding was required by the Minn. Stat. §414.02, subd. 3 and Minn. Stat. § 414.03, subd. 4. The court determined that a specific finding was required on whether annexation to an adjoining municipality would better serve the interests of all or any part of the area involved in the consolidation petition than consolidation would. The court noted that there was substantial evidence that annexation of the area of township, especially if modified, would best serve the interest of village #1 and the unincorporated area adjoining it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded with directions to vacate the order of the Minnesota Municipal Commission and remand the petitions for proceedings to a make a specific finding upon the question of whether annexation to an adjoining municipality would better serve the interests of all or any part of the area involved in the consolidation petition than consolidation would.
