543 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peterfeso


No. 41095


Supreme Court of Minnesota


283 Minn. 499; 169 N.W.2d 18; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1186



June 13, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by John A. Peterfeso from a judgment of the municipal court of St. Paul, Ramsey County, Clifford Janes, Judge, whereby he was convicted of an unlawful sale of radio equipment.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Municipal Court of St. Paul, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted him of an unlawful sale of radio equipment, in violation of Minn. Stat. § 626.63, subd. 2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of selling radio equipment capable of being used in a motor vehicle on a police emergency frequency without a permit in violation of Minn. Stat. § 626.63, subd. 2. On appeal, defendant argued that the statute was unconstitutional because it was overly broad and vague. Defendant argued that the terms of the statute encompassed not only criminal conduct but innocent activities as well. The court agreed and reversed the judgment. The court noted that the purpose of the statute was to prevent persons who committed crimes from determining the activities of the police dispatched to apprehend them. The court held that the statute would have been valid if it had been restricted to prohibiting the use of devices capable of receiving emergency frequencies. However, the court found that the statute was unconstitutional because it prohibited the sale of the devices when their function outside of an automobile could be entirely innocent. The court noted that a statute that spread an all-inclusive net that entangled both the innocent and the wrongdoer alike was unconstitutionally broad and vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that the statute under which defendant was convicted was unconstitutional.

 

544 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnesota Academy of Chiropractors, Inc. v. Minnesota State Board of Chiropractic Examiners


Nos. 41302, 41303, 41304, 41305, 41306


Supreme Court of Minnesota


283 Minn. 474; 169 N.W.2d 26; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1179



June 6, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 283 Minn. 474 at 481.


PRIOR HISTORY: Five appeals have been consolidated for review. One arises out of a declaratory judgment action brought by the Minnesota Academy of Chiropractors, Inc., in the Hennepin County District Court to invalidate rules promulgated by the State Board of Chiropractic Examiners. The others arise out of petitions to review license revocations by said board. After findings for plaintiffs, Dana Nicholson, Judge, defendants, said board and its members, appealed in each case from the judgment entered and from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Minnesota State Board of Chiropractic Examiners sought review of the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) for respondent, a chiropractic association, holding that a Board regulation restricting testimonial advertising pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 148.10, subd. 1(1) was invalid. The Board also sought review of the judgment setting aside its order revoking the licenses of four chiropractors for violating the regulation.


OVERVIEW: The statute, Minn. Stat. § 148.10, subd. 1(1), prohibited any advertisement wherein the terms "cure" or "guarantee to cure" or similar terms were used. The chiropractors whose licenses were revoked distributed pamphlets with testimonials of successful chiropractic treatments. On review, the court held that the Board's regulation was valid. The regulation itself limited the prohibition to testimonials which implied that the conditions described in the advertisement had been or would be cured by the practitioner. The court held that the word "testimonials" as used in the Board's regulation referred to testimonials which were expressly or by implication promises to cure or guarantee to cure. The testimonials distributed by the chiropractors violated § 148.10, subd. 1(1) because almost without exception they went beyond simply certifying improvement or relief but claimed that after chiropractic treatment a patient was "able to walk again," " a miracle had occurred," and a condition had been "cleared up" or ended. Whether true or false, to the extent that the testimonials might be construed as a promise to cure, they were, under the statute, fraudulent and misleading.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments for the association and the chiropractors.

 

545 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Keller v. Le Vander


No. 41455


Supreme Court of Minnesota


283 Minn. 461; 168 N.W.2d 491; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1176



May 29, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Kermit Hedman, sheriff of Ramsey County, from an order of the district court of said county, Edward D. Mulally, Judge, making absolute a writ of habeas corpus issued upon the petition of Franklin E. Keller, Jr., held under a rendition warrant issued by Harold LeVander, governor of the State of Minnesota.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff sought review of an order of the District Court, Ramsey County (Minnesota), which made absolute a writ of habeas corpus issued upon petitioner inmate, who was held under a rendition warrant issued by the Governor of the State of Minnesota.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was indicted in Missouri under Mo. Rev. Stat. § 559.356 (1967) and was arrested in Minnesota under a fugitive warrant. The Governor of Missouri issued a requisition warrant and the Governor of Minnesota issued a rendition warrant. The inmate then applied to the district court for a writ of habeas corpus challenging his arrest and extradition, as was his right under Minn. Stat. § 629.10. The district court made the writ absolute and the sheriff appealed. The court affirmed the decision, holding that the act of leaving Missouri was not one that could be committed entirely in another state. Thus, presence in Missouri at the time the offense was committed was the only one of the alternative requisites for a valid extradition that could be applicable, and it was conceded that the inmate was not present in Missouri during the time specified. Therefore, the Minnesota trial court properly concluded that the writ of habeas corpus should be made absolute. The court further found that the inmate had left Missouri before the effective date of Mo. Rev. Stat. § 559.356 such that it was not applicable to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

 

546 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Marciano


No. 41481


Supreme Court of Minnesota


283 Minn. 200; 167 N.W.2d 41; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1133



April 3, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Roni David Marciano from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Elmer R. Anderson, Judge, whereby he was convicted of sexual intercourse with a child.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of sexual intercourse with a child in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.295(4), and which sentenced to a term, not to exceed three years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to an information charging him with having sexual intercourse with a 16-year old girl. Defendant appealed arguing that he should have been permitted to show a lack of criminal intent because he reasonably believed that the victim was over the age of consent, and that Minn. Stat. § 609.02, subd. 9(6) was unconstitutional. Defendant asserted that the girl came to his apartment and lived with him for several weeks. He stated that the girl told him that she was pregnant and 16 years of age. Thereafter, he had sexual intercourse with her. The court upheld the trial court's judgment. First, the court held because there was no record, it was unable to determine that § 609.02, subd. 9(6) was unconstitutional as applied to defendant. The court reasoned that in some instances the criminal intent statute, § 609.02, subd. 9(6), could have been improperly applied to a party, however, absent a record, the court was unable to conclude such. Further, the court noted that defendant did not seek leave to withdraw his plea, and there was no opportunity to conduct an exhaustive hearing to determine whether defendant's prosecution would have lead to an unjust result.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

547 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Imperial Refineries of Minnesota, Inc. v. Rochester


No. 41204


Supreme Court of Minnesota


282 Minn. 481; 165 N.W.2d 699; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1248



February 28, 1969 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certified to U.S. Supreme Court April 14, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding in the Olmsted County District Court by Imperial Refineries of Minnesota, Inc., to challenge the validity of certain assessments by the city of Rochester against appellant's land for two improvement projects. After adverse findings, Donald T. Franke, Judge, said appellant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Olmstead County (Minnesota) that was rendered in favor of defendant city regarding assessments made in support of sanitary sewer and water main improvements, and for a water tank and connecting trunkline improvements.


OVERVIEW: The city initiated the sewer and water tank projects pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 429.031, subd. 1. The corporation owned property affected by the city's projects, and was given notice on the proposed assessments. A representative appeared at the hearing, protested the assessment, and made a similar appearance at a second hearing. The city, in separate actions, approved two assessments, which were appealed by the corporation over a month after the city's actions. The trial court found that the corporation's appeals were not timely under Minn. Stat. § 429.081, it nevertheless heard the appeals on their merits. Because the corporation received no notice of the date to which the city finally approved the assessments, the city made no issue regarding the timeliness of the appeals. The court affirmed and rejected the corporation's assertion that because § 429.081 did not require notice of the date the assessments were confirmed, it was unconstitutional. The court held that the statute's constitutionality had previously been decided, and that the corporation could not complain of notice when it sought and obtained a full hearing on the merits of the assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

548 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Andrews


No. 40864


Supreme Court of Minnesota


282 Minn. 386; 165 N.W.2d 528; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1233



February 7, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Julius R. Andrews from a judgment of the Wright County District Court, Leonard Keyes, Judge, whereby he was convicted of burglary.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Wright County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted defendant of burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant were caught fleeing a burglary scene, and each was charged under identical complaints, although tried separately. Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree burglary and 20-year sentence, arguing that he was denied his constitutional rights to equal protection, due process, and trial by an impartial jury, due to the State's decision to treat him more severely than his accomplice, who was convicted of third-degree burglary and sentenced to five years in prison. The court held that the differences between defendant and the accomplice included their records of prior but unrelated crimes, their participation in the burglary, and their cooperation with the State. The unequal administration of a statute by state officials was not a denial of equal protection unless an element of intentional or purposeful discrimination were present, which the record did not establish. Defendant waived his right to challenge nine jurors on grounds of bias because he failed to challenge for cause. The jury was impartial because there was no indication that jurors heard any facts in an earlier, aborted trial about the accomplice's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court, which convicted defendant.

 

549 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parker


No. 41000


Supreme Court of Minnesota


282 Minn. 343; 164 N.W.2d 633; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1228



January 31, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by John William Parker from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Tom Bergin, Judge, whereby he was convicted of aggravated robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed his conviction for aggravated robbery by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for aggravated robbery. Before and after the crime was committed, defendant held a close association with the men who stole the victim's car, and defendant fled the scene of the crime with the other men. On appeal, defendant argued he did not directly participate in the assault and robbery. Defendant contended that the trial court instructed the jury that defendant might in fact have owed a legal obligation to render aid to the victim; defendant argued that he did not have such an obligation. Moreover, defendant asserted that failure to discharge a moral obligation to aid the injured party was not enough to convict him of the crime charged. The court affirmed the conviction because evidence of defendant's subsequent acts was sufficient to prove participation in the aggravated robbery of the victim.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because defendant's acts prior to and subsequent to the crime were sufficient to prove participation in the crime charged.

 

550 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Scannell v. St. Paul


No. 40205


Supreme Court of Minnesota


282 Minn. 214; 163 N.W.2d 872; 1969 Minn. LEXIS 1209



January 3, 1969 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by Howard J. Scannell and other employees of the police and fire departments of the city of St. Paul for a declaratory judgment invalidating a statute depriving plaintiffs and others similarly situated of veterans preference; and for an injunction against defendant city and its officials with respect to said statute. The court, Arthur A. Stewart, Judge, granted defendants' motion for summary judgment, and plaintiffs appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, employees of the police and fire departments of defendant City of St. Paul, appealed a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted the City's motion for summary judgment in a declaratory judgment action brought to invalidate Minn. Stat. § 423.075, subd. 2, which purported to remove the protections of the Veterans Preference Act, Minn. Stat. §§ 197.45-137.47.


OVERVIEW: The employees were military veterans who worked for the police and fire departments of the City of St. Paul. Minn. Stat. § 423.075, subd. 1 provided that police and firemen department employees were required to retire upon reaching age 65, and that employees who had not qualified for retirement benefits were permitted to serve beyond age 65 until they became entitled to benefits. Subsequently, the legislature enacted Minn. Stat. § 423.075, subd. 2, which provided that the Veterans Preference Act did not apply to § 423.075, subd. 1. The employees argued that § 423.075, subd. 2 discriminated against them by compelling them to retire at 65 when other veterans in the same class were not required to do so. The court noted that § 423.075, subd. 1 had been found constitutional as applied to nonveterans because its purpose was to remove police officers and firemen from active duty when their age prevented them from performing the physical duties of their jobs. The court held that that rationale was equally sound when applied to veterans, and that the legislature could take away the rights it had granted to the employees under the Veterans Preference Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Johnson


Nos. 40650, 40651, 40652, 40653


Supreme Court of Minnesota


282 Minn. 153; 163 N.W.2d 750; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 939



December 13, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals by Joseph D. Johnson, Lee W. Smith, Larry Seigle, and Keith Ruona from judgments of the Hennepin County Municipal Court, Bruce C. Stone, Judge, convicting them of violations of a breach-of-the-peace ordinance of Minneapolis, and from an order denying a motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Four defendants challenged their convictions for violations of a breach-of-the-peace ordinance, Minneapolis, Minn., Code of Ordinances § 870.060, which was entered by the Hennepin County Municipal Court (Minnesota). Defendants also appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial. Defendants challenged the constitutionality of § 870.060 and the sufficiency of the evidence upon which their convictions were based.


OVERVIEW: After an afternoon street parade held in connection with a civic celebration, 15 members of the Minnesota Committee to End the War in Vietnam gathered at a busy intersection in downtown Minneapolis. They placed a stepladder on the sidewalk about five feet from a street curb. While some members of the group took turns mounting the ladder and addressing passersby with a microphone, others held signs and distributed handbills. The speeches protested against President Johnson's foreign policy as to the Vietnam War. Police officers testified that a crowd of nearly 200 people gathered, that the officers had a difficult time keeping an aisle open on the sidewalk, and that the crowd spilled into the street, blocking a lane of traffic. After 15 minutes of allowing the demonstration, the police started to break up the crowd. Defendants were arrested. The court held that the record failed to present the court with specific wrongful conduct of each individual defendant charged with breach of the peace. However, the court found that defendants were not unaware of the nature of the offense under § 870.060 and that § 870.060 was specific enough in its delineation of what constituted the offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, set aside the convictions, and remanded for a new trial.

 

552 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mitchell


No. 41024


Supreme Court of Minnesota


282 Minn. 113; 163 N.W.2d 310; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 936



December 6, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by John R. Mitchell from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Rolf Fosseen, Judge, whereby he was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree, and from an order denying his alternative motion for judgment of acquittal or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) for manslaughter in the first degree. Defendant contended that he was entitled to a new trial because the medical examiner testified that the victim died from strangulation performed from behind, defendant's statements were made without the proper Miranda warnings, and various other errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife was found dead in their burned house. He was questioned at the hospital, and the fact that he and his wife had an argument and he struck her became central in the police investigation. Defendant objected to the admission of testimony of police officers relative to the questioning, and the trial court overruled his objection. On appeal, the court held that at the time of the questioning defendant was not under arrest and was not restrained. Further, the court held that because the investigation was in its preliminary stages, the fact that police suspected arson, accelerant, and knew of the smell of gasoline on defendant's shoes did not render the questioning interrogation. The court then addressed defendant's contention that testimony of the medical examiner that defendant's wife was strangled from behind was prejudicial, rejecting the appeal and holding that because the trial judge ordered that the phrase "from behind" be stricken, there was no error in the trial court's denial of defendant's request for a mistrial. The court noted that strangulation was a subject that required expert testimony, and without it the jury could not be expected to reach a verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

553 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Armstrong


Nos. 41212, 41213


Supreme Court of Minnesota


282 Minn. 39; 162 N.W.2d 357; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 924



November 8, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals by Gayle Jean Armstrong from two judgments of the Hennepin County Municipal Court, James D. Rogers, Judge, whereby she was found guilty of violating two ordinances of the city of Minneapolis.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and new trial ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed two judgments of the Hennepin County Municipal Court (Minnesota), which convicted her of lurking and loitering in violation of Minneapolis, Minn., Ordinance § 870.050 and Minneapolis, Minn., Ordinance § 870.010, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a prostitute who was observed leaving a restaurant and entering the car of a stranger who then drove defendant around in a circuitous route. The police questioned the driver and the police testified at trial that the driver told them that defendant asked the driver whether he wanted to party when she entered the car. However, the driver did not testify at trial. The lower court convicted defendant of lurking and loitering, and the court reversed. The court held that the ordinances were not unconstitutionally vague because the loitering and lurking prohibited by the ordinances was reasonably understandable to an ordinary person. The court ruled that the prosecution was not only required to prove the acts of loitering and lurking, but it was also required to prove that those acts were done with the intent to commit an unlawful act. However, the court further ruled that because the hearsay evidence of what the driver told the police officers was improperly admitted, and it was possible that the lower court relied upon the hearsay in convicting defendant, defendant was entitled to a new trial on both charges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's convictions of defendant for lurking and loitering, and it remanded the action for a new trial on both charges.

Noltimier v. Noltimier


No. 41036


Supreme Court of Minnesota


282 Minn. 526; 162 N.W.2d 707; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 952



November 8, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied, 394 U.S. 953, 89 S. Ct. 1296, 22 L. ed. (2d) 488.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by plaintiff, Leo Noltimier, Jr., from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, William D. Gunn, Judge, in a divorce action, which judgment granted a divorce, awarded custody of one child to said plaintiff, awarded custody of two of the children to defendant, and ordered plaintiff to pay child support.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband appealed from a judgment and decree issued by the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) in a divorce action, which granted defendant wife custody of two children, awarded her support money, assigned her the equity in the homestead and its furnishings, and allowed her attorney's fees. The trial court awarded the husband custody of one child.


OVERVIEW: The husband contended that the trial court's decree denied him equal protection of the laws in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment for the following reasons: he was required to pay the wife for support of children in her custody and she was not required to pay him for the support of the child in his custody; the distribution of property acquired during coverture was not equal; he was required to pay the wife's attorney's fees as well as his own; and the trial court preserved the wife's right to future alimony. The husband cited no authority for the proposition that the statutes authorizing the payment of alimony, support money, and attorney's fees on behalf of the wife, or the unequal division of their property, were unconstitutional. The court also was aware of no such authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

North Suburban Sanitary Sewer Dist. v. Water Pollution Control Com.


No. 40,718


Supreme Court of Minnesota


281 Minn. 524; 162 N.W.2d 249; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1036; 32 A.L.R.3d 199



October 22, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal in the Anoka County District Court by the North Suburban Sanitary Sewer District, the city of Coon Rapids, and individual residents of the area involved from certain classifications and pollution standards adopted by the Water Pollution Control Commission of the State of Minnesota. After findings vacating the standards in part, Robert B. Gillespie, Judge, the commission appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Water Pollution Control Commission of the State of Minnesota, appealed from a judgment of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which vacated certain standards established by the commission sewer, in response to the challenges by respondents, North Suburban Sanitary Sewer District, city, and individual residents to the standards.


OVERVIEW: The district court considered whether the evidence supported a finding that the danger of contaminating the Minneapolis water system by locating its effluent outfall 1.1 miles downstream from the main Minneapolis water intake was sufficiently serious to justify adopting a standard which prohibited the discharge of any treated sewage effluent into the Mississippi River from two locations. The court found in part that the district court had jurisdiction under Minn. Stat. § 115.02 (1961), the District was an aggrieved party, and the issues were justiciable. On the record the district court was justified in holding that the standards were unreasonable in so far as they prohibited the discharge of all treated sewage effluent into the river between the mouth of the Rum River and the St. Anthony Falls dam, and prohibited the discharge of major quantities of treated sewage into the river between St. Anthony Falls dam and the Pig's Eye treatment plant. The court declined to hold that the standards were otherwise void. To the extent that the decision of the trial court held that the adoption of the standards was not lawful for any purpose, the conclusions of the trial court were reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's finding that the standards were unreasonable as they applied to the district but reversed as to the finding that the adoption of the standards was not lawful for any purpose.

 

556 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Naegele Outdoor Advertising Co. v. Minnetonka


No. 40,781


Supreme Court of Minnesota


281 Minn. 492; 162 N.W.2d 206; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1033



October 11, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court against the village of Minnetonka and Arthur C. Rydmark, its chief building inspector, for a declaratory judgment invalidating a zoning ordinance regulating the maintenance of signs and billboards. Defendants counterclaimed, charging plaintiff with violation of said ordinance. The court, Arnold Hatfield, Judge, found the ordinance to be valid but that enforcement against plaintiff had been discriminatory and it was enjoined.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff billboard owner challenged a judgment from Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota)holding that defendant village's zoning ordinance creating exclusively residential districts was constitutional. The trial court found that the ordinance was discriminatorily applied against plaintiff. The village counterclaimed for an order that plaintiff remove the subject billboards.


OVERVIEW: The billboard owner had oral and written leases to maintain billboards in a particular area. The village passed a zoning ordinance creating an exclusively residential neighborhood, which included the area where the billboards were located. In addition to prohibiting all future commercial uses in the zoned area, the ordinance provided that all existing nonconforming uses had to be phased out over three years. When the billboard owner was told it was time to remove its billboards it filed its action seeking a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was unconstitutional on its face. The trial court ruled against the owner, although it found that the ordinance had been discriminatorily applied against it. The billboard owner appealed. The court ruled that the ordinance was not unconstitutional on its face. It was a reasonable exercise of the village's police power as such power was currently understood. The ordinance promoted the general welfare by protecting and enhancing property values. Under the facts of the case, the billboard owner was not entitled to compensation for the "taking" of his property. The state statutes gave the village the power to enact its zoning ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

557 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morse


No. 40,557


Supreme Court of Minnesota


281 Minn. 378; 161 N.W.2d 699; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1018



September 20, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Lester J. Morse from a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, John W. Graff, Judge, whereby he was convicted of indecent assault.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court, Minnesota, which convicted him of indecent assault in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.08 (1965).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of indecent assault after taking liberties with a 15 year old girl. On appeal, defendant contended that Minn. Stat. § 609.02, subd. 9(6), which provided that defendant was not required to have knowledge that the victim was under age 16, was unconstitutional because it was vague and indefinite. The court ruled that Minn. The court noted that the United States Supreme Court had held that, though scienter was a necessary element at common law, it could be dispensed with in special situations. Defendant offered no evidence to show that he was in fact misled or mistaken as to the girl's age. Furthermore, the trial court offered to give an instruction correcting an inaccurate allusion made by the State in its closing argument concerning defendant's knowledge of the girl's age, but defendant declined to ask for the charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction.

Emery v. Hotel & Restaurant Employees Union


No. 40,440


Supreme Court of Minnesota


281 Minn. 334; 161 N.W.2d 842; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1014; 69 L.R.R.M. 2396



September 13, 1968 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certified to U.S. Supreme Court February 3, 1969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action in the Ramsey County District Court by Daniel Emery and Mileda Emery, d.b.a. The Main Diner, for damages allegedly sustained by reason of the conduct of defendant union and its representatives. The case was tried before Ronald E. Hachey, Judge, and a jury, which found that plaintiffs sustained general damages amounting to $ 3,500 and punitive damages of $ 10,000. Thereafter, the court granted defendants' motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and, should that order be reversed, granted defendants' motion for a new trial unless plaintiffs consented to a reduction of the verdict to $ 8,500. Plaintiffs appealed from said order and from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff restaurant owners appealed a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted the motion of defendant, a union and others, for a judgment notwithstanding special verdicts, and held that should the order be reversed the union was to be granted a new trial unless the owners consented to verdict reduction in the owners' damages action. The union sought review of the order conditionally granting a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The owners purchased a restaurant and union representatives began picketing, causing the owners to lose substantial amounts of business, when the owners refused to join the union. The owners brought an action for damages and the district court found that the owners had sustained general damages and punitive damages and thereafter granted the union's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and held that if that order was to be reversed, the union's motion for a new trial was to be granted unless the owners consented to a reduction of the verdict. The owners appealed and the union sought review of that part of the order which conditionally granted a new trial. The court reversed the decision, finding that, pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 179.11(7), the union's actions in attempting to compel the owners to join was unlawful. Further, the district court had authority to enjoin undesirable peaceful picketing. There was ample evidence to show that the union unlawfully interfered with the owners' property rights. The court affirmed, in part, holding that the total verdict was to be reduced, this in effect reducing the punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the judgment in favor of the owners reinstated, but reduced the total verdict.

 

559 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Schultz v. Ruiz


No. 40,910


Supreme Court of Minnesota


281 Minn. 281; 161 N.W.2d 537; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1005



August 30, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court for personal injuries brought on behalf of Gary Schultz, a minor, by his father and natural guardian, John Schultz; and for consequential damages by John Schultz on his own behalf. It was alleged that said minor was struck by defendants Jonathan and Abel Ruiz at a dance which was supervised by defendant John J. McDonough Homes. The court, Ronald E. Hachey, Judge, denied the motion of the latter defendant for summary judgment and certified the matter to this court as important and doubtful. Said defendant appealed from the court's order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon certification to the Minnesota Supreme Court, defendant recreation center sought review of an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which denied its motion for summary judgment in favor of plaintiff minor on his personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The question before the court was whether the 30-day notice-of-claim requirement and one-year limitation provision of Minn. Stat. § 465.09 (1961), applied to bar the minor's action for damages resulting from personal injuries he sustained, when he was assaulted after attending a dance conducted at a recreation center owned and controlled by the Housing and Redevelopment Authority (Authority). On appeal, the court answered the question in the negative and affirmed the denial of the recreation center's motion for summary judgment. The court noted that under Minn. Stat. § 462.455 the Authority was liable in contract or in tort in the same manner as a private corporation. The court also noted that there was a direct conflict between § 462.455 and Minn. Stat. § 465.09. The court interpreted the phrase "in the same manner" to encompass both the procedural and the substantive law applicable to tort actions. The court held, pursuant the rule of statutory construction in Minn. Stat. § 645.26, subd. 1, that Minn. Stat. § 462.455 controlled and that the general notice statute was inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the recreation center's motion for summary judgment.

 

560 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Weigold


No. 40,114


Supreme Court of Minnesota


281 Minn. 73; 160 N.W.2d 577; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 968



July 26, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Darrell Roy Weigold from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Paul J. Jaroscak, Judge, whereby he was convicted of indecent assault.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which entered judgment convicting defendant of indecent assault under Minn. Stat. § 617.08 and sentenced him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with indecent assault, Minn. St. 617.08, waived a jury trial, and appealed from a conviction for which he was sentenced. Defendant admitted having intercourse with complainant. There was ample evidence from which the trial court found defendant guilty. Defendant argued that time elapsed between the time the offense was committed and complainant told her version of the crime to her mother; thus the mother's testimony was not admissible as part of the res gestae. The testimony of the mother corroborated her daughter's, and did not include any new facts. Even if the testimony was not a part of the res gestae, it was admissible in a prosecution for indecent assault or rape. The trial court granted the prosecution's motion to clear the courtroom without an objection from the defense. This was a procedural matter; counsel has implied authority to speak on behalf of his client. Defendant was not deprived of his constitutional right to a public trial. Defendant contended that Minn. Stat. § 617.08, defining indecent assault, was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the statute clearly applied to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

561 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Housing & Redevelopment Authority v. Coleman's Service, Inc.


No. 41,210


Supreme Court of Minnesota


281 Minn. 63; 160 N.W.2d 266; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 967



July 19, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Coleman's Service, Inc., to review an order of the Ramsey County District Court, Arthur A. Stewart, retired judge, granting the petition of the Housing and Redevelopment Authority of the City of St. Paul for the taking of said relator's property in connection with an urban renewal project and appointing commissioners to ascertain the damages which will be sustained.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was on certiorari by petitioner company for review of an order of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted the petition of respondent, the Housing and Redevelopment Authority of the City of St. Paul for the taking of the company's property in connection with an urban renewal project.


OVERVIEW: The order being reviewed would authorize the taking by eminent domain of property owned by the company. The case presented the question of whether redevelopment of a non-slum area which was blighted was a public purpose which would justify condemnation of the property involved. The company argued on review that there was no evidence to support the finding of blight; that there was no evidence that government assistance was necessary to renovate the area; and that the taking was unconstitutional because it does not serve a public use. The court held that the Authority was not required to make a specific finding that existing conditions on property to be acquired were inimical to the public health, safety, morals, or welfare under Minn. Stat. § 462.421. Further, the court held that the evidence established that the taking of the blighted property was for a public purpose and that subsequent transfer of the property to private parties for use as a site for an apartment building was incidental to the public purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

562 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Houge


No. 40,812


Supreme Court of Minnesota


280 Minn. 372; 159 N.W.2d 265; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1112



May 31, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Glenn Myles Houge from a judgment of the Washington County District Court, Robert B. Gillespie, Judge, whereby he was convicted of aggravated forgery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of aggravated forgery in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.625, subd. 1(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that there was insufficient evidence to prove his guilt, that Minn. Stat. § 609.625, subd. 1(1) violated the single-subject and title requirements of Minn. Const. art. 4, § 27, and that evidence was inadmissible because notice of intent to use evidence of other crimes did not comply with the requirement that notice be given a "reasonable time" before trial. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that there was abundant evidence to support the trial court's finding that defendant's guilt was proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that the evidence, particularly when viewed in light of the principle that factfindings by the trier of facts would be upset only when manifestly contrary to the evidence, was more than adequate to sustain the finding of guilt. Additionally, the court found that if the word "utter" was not unconstitutionally vague, then "forgery," a word of widespread usage, was not unconstitutionally vague and that Minn. Stat. § 609.625, subd. 1(1) was therefore not unconstitutionally vague. Finally, the court found that the State's eleventh-hour filing of notice, even if erroneous, did not constitute prejudicial error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

563 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schmidt


No. 40,632


Supreme Court of Minnesota


280 Minn. 281; 159 N.W.2d 113; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1101



May 17, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Robert Theodore Schmidt from a judgment of the Crow Wing County District Court, John T. Galarneault, Judge, whereby he was convicted of soliciting without a permit in violation of an ordinance of the city of Brainerd.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Crow Wing County District Court (Minnesota), which convicted him of soliciting without a permit in violation of Brainerd, Minn. Ordinance No. 469.


OVERVIEW: Brainerd, Minn. Ordinance No. 469 required all non-resident peddlers, solicitors, and transient merchants to obtain a permit to engage in their activities. They were required to post a bond of $ 250. If a non-resident disagreed with the requirement as unduly burdensome, he could apply to the city council for an adjustment. Defendant was found guilty by the municipal court of violating the ordinance. He challenged the ordinance's constitutionality when he appealed the municipal court ruling, but he was convicted in the district court. On appeal, the court held that the ordinance violated defendant's right to equal protection of the law, and that it placed a burden on interstate commerce. It held that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The ordinance's defect was not cured by the opportunity for an appeal to the city council.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

564 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simmons


No. 40,499


Supreme Court of Minnesota


280 Minn. 107; 158 N.W.2d 209; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1070



April 11, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Mildred Simmons from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Tom Bergin, Judge, whereby she was convicted of obtaining public assistance by means of false statement, and from an order denying her motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of her conviction for obtaining public assistance by means of false statement from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) and from an order denying her motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received Aid to Families with Dependent Children from the county welfare program for over 13 years. Defendant was unemployed throughout that time period, except for a three-month period. When defendant filled out her six-month eligibility statement, she was again unemployed and under the section entitled "current resources" she marked none next to "earnings and wages from employment. Defendant testified that she thought the question referred to her current state of employment. Defendant was convicted of a misdemeanor under Minn. Stat. § 256.83 for obtaining assistance by means of a false statement. The court held that the questionnaire was too vague to support a conviction based on defendant's answer. The court explained that a person, particularly of limited education and experience, could interpret the questionnaire to refer to her current employment situation, rather than her situation for the past six months. The court explained that criminal statutes must be construed strictly in favor of a defendant. The court reasoned that the welfare program could easily reword the questionnaire to inquire more specifically and clearly about the past work income.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Ruffin


No. 40,977


Supreme Court of Minnesota


280 Minn. 126; 158 N.W.2d 202; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1074



April 11, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Jerome Ruffin from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Dana Nicholson, Judge, whereby he was convicted of theft.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) that convicted him of swindling under Minn. Stat. § 609.52, subd. 2(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended § 609.52 subd. 2(4) was unconstitutionally vague and uncertain and that the verdict was not supported by the evidence. Defendant also contended that the trial court failed to give adequate jury instructions concerning the elements of the offense charged. Upon review, the court found that the statute met the test of being sufficiently clear and definite to inform a person of ordinary intelligence what the statute proscribed. As to the issue over the jury instructions, the court held that since the statute was sufficiently clear and the nature of the offense was clearly stated in the indictment, definitions and explanations by the trial court were not required because defendant took no exception.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for swindling.

 

566 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. County of Itasca


No. 40,575


Supreme Court of Minnesota


280 Minn. 51; 157 N.W.2d 753; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1059



March 29, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceeding in the Itasca County District Court wherein plaintiff sought certain retirement compensation withheld pursuant to an allegedly unconstitutional statute. Upon stipulated facts, the court, James F. Murphy, Judge, granted a motion for summary judgment made by defendants, said county and Richard J. Whaling, its auditor. Plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired judge appealed a judgment of the Itasca County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, a county and its auditor, in the judge's action to recover certain retirement compensation that was withheld pursuant to an allegedly unconstitutional statute.


OVERVIEW: After the judge retired in 1962, the county and its auditor reduced the judge's retirement compensation by the amounts he was receiving as a member of the Public Employees Retirement Association (PERA) under the provisions of a 1961 amendment to Minn. Stat. 490.12. The judge brought an action challenging the constitutionality of the law. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the county and its auditor. On appeal the judge argued that the application of the 1961 amendment had caused him to suffer a severe and unexpected economic loss not experienced by colleagues who were not members of the PERA. The court agreed and reversed the judgment. The court held that the judge had been denied the equal protection of the laws under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, and Minn. Const. art. 1, § 2, and art. 4, § 33. The court held that distinctions which separated those included and those excluded from the application of a particular law were required to be genuine and substantial and to provide a reasonable and not a capricious or arbitrary basis for the imposition of special legislative regulations. The court held that the amendment was invalid as to the judge and others similarly situated.


OUTCOME: The court held that the amendment was invalid as to the judge and others similarly situated. The court reversed the judgment.

 

567 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State Civil Service Dep't


No. 40,750


Supreme Court of Minnesota


280 Minn. 61; 157 N.W.2d 747; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1062



March 29, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Charles J. Johnson from an order of the Ramsey County District Court, Robert V. Rensch, Judge, denying his petition for reinstatement to his employment with the Motor Vehicle Division of the office of the secretary of state, his dismissal from which had been sustained by the Civil Service Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which denied the employee's petition for reinstatement to his employment with the Motor Vehicle Division.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was terminated from his employment after he filed for the office of clerk of district court of Wabasha County and then refused to resign his employment. Minn. Stat. § 43.28 required an employee in the state classified service to resign from the service upon filing as a candidate for public office. Defendant contended that the statute violated the First and Fourteenth Amendments, U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV. The court rejected those claims. The employee did not have a constitutional right to government employment. While the statute restricted defendant's First Amendment rights, by prohibiting him from expressing his political views by seeking public office, such restriction was reasonable. The legislature reasonably determined that allowing government employees to obtain public office while still employed with the government could lead to abuse of the merit system. Campaigning could interfere with an employee's time and devotion to his official duties. The practice could also lead to employees seeking special treatment from superiors and for friends due to holding the public office. The court gave little consideration to defendant's Fourteenth Amendment argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

568 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Target Stores, Inc.


No. 41,130


Supreme Court of Minnesota


279 Minn. 447; 156 N.W.2d 908; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1219



March 19, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the state from an order of the Hennepin County Municipal Court, Donald S. Burris, Judge, dismissing complaints against Target Stores, Inc., and Kevin West, its employee, for violation of the provisions of the 1967 Sunday Closing Law.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Minnesota challenged an order of the Municipal Court of Hennepin County (Minnesota) that dismissed criminal complaints against respondents, a department store corporation and its employee, for making sales of restricted commodities in alleged violation of 1967 Minn. Laws ch. 165. The order dismissing the complaints was based solely on constitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, by selling restricted commodities on Sunday in alleged violation of 1967 Minn. Laws ch. 165, brought a test case to determine the constitutionality of the statute. The constitutional challenge was made on two broad grounds: that it was unconstitutional in fundamental purpose and that, regardless of purpose, it was unconstitutional in effect. The court ruled that the state had broad constitutional power to establish a common day of rest, repose, recreation, and tranquillity; and held that the exercise of that power did not offend against the First Amendment.Claims of discrimination were also raised as to the exemptions in the statute. The court held that the vagueness and uncertainty in the designation of restricted commodities which could not be sold on Sunday did not afford clear warning to a potential defendant of conduct which could have resulted in severe penal sanctions under the statute. The statute was nullified. The court ruled that the net result of its decision was simply to restore the Sunday closing situation in Minnesota to exactly what it had been before the enactment of 1967 Minn. Laws ch. 165.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that dismissed the State's complaint against respondents for violating the Sunday closing law.

 

569 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Rosvall v. Provost


No. 40,574


Supreme Court of Minnesota


279 Minn. 119; 155 N.W.2d 900; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1163



January 12, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Anoka County District Court wherein plaintiff sought damages for alleged malicious prosecution from the city of Coon Rapids and some of its officers and agents. The court, Leonard Keyes, Judge, granted defendants' motion for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dog owner filed an action against defendants, the City of Coon Rapids, the City's dog catcher, and others, seeking damages for alleged malicious prosecution. The Anoka County District Court (Minnesota) granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The dog catcher filed a complaint alleging that the owner was operating an unlicensed dog kennel, in violation of a City ordinance. The owner pled guilty and her sentence was suspended on the condition that she obtain a license. After failing to obtain a license, the owner was given 10 days to dispose of her dogs. Two months later, the dog catcher obtained and executed a search warrant for the owner's home and 17 unlicensed dogs were seized and the owner was arrested. The owner was later committed to the state hospital after she refused to eat and was acting in an "irrational manner." The owner later failed suit to recover damages for the loss of her dogs, for the enforced absence from her home, and for damages to her home that occurred during her absence. In affirming the district court's judgment, the court ruled that the dog catcher and other agents acted in good faith as directed by competent authority in executing the warrant, seizing the dogs, and arresting the owner and, thus, the issue of the ordinance's validity was immaterial. There was no valid cause of action for false imprisonment, and the owner failed to establish the malice element of her malicious prosecution claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

State v. Forichette


No. 40,035


Supreme Court of Minnesota


279 Minn. 76; 156 N.W.2d 93; 1968 Minn. LEXIS 1158; 34 A.L.R.3d 399



January 5, 1968 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by John William Forichette, also known as John Edward Forichette, from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Earl J. Lyons, Judge, whereby he was convicted of perjury.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of perjury in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.48, subd. 1(1) for falsely stating on his application for employment with the City of Minneapolis, Minnesota and at his discharge hearing that he was not a member of the Communist Party. He appealed from the judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), contending that Minneapolis, Minn., Civil Service Comm'n R. 4.06(j) and 12.02(q) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Minneapolis, Minn., Civil Service Comm'n R. 4.06(j) and 12.02(q) provided that the City could refuse to certify as eligible for employment any applicant who was, inter alia, a member of the Communist Party and that, inter alia, membership in the Communist Party was grounds for removal. Defendant was discharged for intentionally and falsely stating in his application that he was not a member of any political party or organization that advocated the overthrow of a constitutional form of government in the United States. His conviction was based on informant testimony that he was a dues-paying member of a local chapter of the Communist Party and had served as its treasurer. The court held that regardless of whether the certification requirements were unconstitutional, defendant could not justify his perjury on that ground. Though an agent of the Federal Bureau of Investigation (FBI) claimed privilege with regard to reports and records of the FBI's investigation of the chapter, the refusal to strike the agent's testimony was not error. Defendant was given an opportunity to secure statements that were contained therein by consenting to a 48-hour stay but failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of perjury.

St. Paul v. Tobler


No. 41,054


Supreme Court of Minnesota


278 Minn. 269; 153 N.W.2d 440; 1967 Minn. LEXIS 860



October 20, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Prohibition in this court to compel the St. Paul municipal court, Ramsey County, Stephen L. Maxwell, Judge, to refrain from further proceedings against defendants, Adolph T. Tobler, Richard C. Radman, Jr., and Michael J. Schneider, charged with failure to comply with directions of a peace officer.



DISPOSITION: Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants petitioned for a writ of prohibition to compel respondent municipal court to refrain from further proceedings against them on charges of failing to comply with the directions of a peace officer, arguing that the warrants under which they were arrested were invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendants petitioned for a writ of prohibition to challenge the validity of the warrants under which they were arrested that had been issued by the municipal court. Specifically, defendants contended that the warrants were invalid because they did not bear the signature of the chief judge of the municipal court as required by Minn. Stat. § 488A.27, subd. 7. In discharging the writ, the court concluded that, where the warrants were in fact executed by a judge of the municipal court, the absence of the signature of the chief judge was at most a negligible irregularity and was insufficient to render invalid warrants that were supported by probable cause. The signature of the chief judge was not the hallmark of validity because each municipal judge held separate office with legal competence to perform all relevant judicial acts.


OUTCOME: The writ was discharged.

OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to a charge of sodomy after he had voluntarily gone to the police and entered a confession. He was sentenced to five years imprisonment. Lenz v. Coon Creek Watershed Dist.


No. 40,441


Supreme Court of Minnesota


278 Minn. 1; 153 N.W.2d 209; 1967 Minn. LEXIS 828



September 1, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by John O. Lenz and others from a judgment of the Anoka County District Court, Leonard Keyes, Judge, restricting the issues to be reviewed by said court to the benefits and damages to two individuals and otherwise dismissing certain appeals from an order of the managers of the Coon Creek Watershed District and from an order of the Minnesota Water Resources Board, which orders approved a proposed project to improve and enlarge Coon Creek.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged a judgment of the Anoka County District Court (Minnesota), which affirmed the decision of respondent watershed district to make improvements to a creek under the Minnesota Watershed Act, Minn. Stat. 112.34 et seq., and limited individual appeals to two landowners.


OVERVIEW: The county board petitioned the watershed district to improve a drainage channel. After conducting public hearings, the watershed district approved the project. The landowners contested this decision. The district court affirmed the validity of the decision and dismissed the appeal with the exception of the individual assessments for two landowners. The court affirmed the judgment of the district court. Because the landowners were entitled to only a certiorari review under Minn. Stat. § 112.792 (1961) and because there had been extensive hearings, the court found that the landowners were properly denied a trial de novo and the opportunity to submitted additional evidence. Although Minn. Stat. § 112.48, subd. 1 (1961) was ambiguous, the court interpreted the provision to permit the county board to petition the watershed district without the signatures of any landowners. The court concluded that the managers of the watershed district were not disqualified from participating in the decision based on their land ownership because the law required a portion of the managers to be landowners in the district and no statute required their disqualification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment affirming the validity of the decision of the watershed district to approve a drainage improvement project and limiting the appeal of individual assessments to two landowners.

 

574 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Hartmann v. Lund


No. 40,673


Supreme Court of Minnesota


277 Minn. 398; 152 N.W.2d 514; 1967 Minn. LEXIS 956



August 11, 1967 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certified to U.S. Supreme Court November 28, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Dr. J. Benjamin Lund, medical director of the State Security Hospital, from an order of the Nicollet County District Court, Noah S. Rosenbloom, Judge, ordering him to release John J. Hartmann upon his petition for a writ of habeas corpus unless otherwise authorized within 30 days.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator patient filed a habeas corpus proceeding against respondent hospital seeking his release. The Nicollet County District Court (Minnesota) entered an order directing the hospital to release the patient within 30 days unless the hospital received a new warrant authorizing the patient's commitment. The hospital appealed, contending that the trial court erred in determining that the patient was denied due process in the commitment proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The patient's wife filed a petition for the patient's involuntary commitment. That day, the probate court issued an authorization to hold the patient for examination pending the outcome and issued a notice for examination and hearing that was personally served on the patient, who was in jail. A hearing was held the next day, and a board of examiners reported to the probate court that the patient was of unsound mind. The probate court issued a warrant committing the patient to the hospital's custody. The court held that the patient wholly failed to establish that the commitment was invalid. A court commissioner was authorized to preside over the proceedings by Minn. Stat. § 535.763. The patient was present and represented by counsel at both the examination and the hearing. The probate court judge's subsequent entry of the judgment was a routine matter, and the patient's absence was not a violation of due process. There was no defect upon the face of the record, and the patient was provided with reasonable notice and an opportunity to be heard. The proper procedure for attacking the commitment was for the patient to petition for restoration under Minn. Stat. § 525.78.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded with directions in accordance with the opinion.

 

575 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


No. 40,296


Supreme Court of Minnesota


277 Minn. 351; 152 N.W.2d 728; 1967 Minn. LEXIS 949



August 4, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certification by the Jackson County District Court, L. J. Irvine, Judge, of certain questions as being important and doubtful in connection with an information charging defendant with theft by check.



DISPOSITION: Questions certified answered in the negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was charged by information in the Jackson County District Court (Minnesota) with theft by means of four $ 35 checks in violation of Minn. Stat. § 609.52, subds. 2(3)(a) and 3(4), unsuccessfully moved for an order quashing the information because it did not state a public offense, in that the statute violated various provisions of the federal and state constitutions, but the matter was certified to the court as being important.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the information was invalid because the underlying statute was vague in not informing him of the nature of the prosecution against him, deprived him of his liberty without due process, caused him to be twice jeopardized for commission of the same act, denied him the right to trial by jury, and embraced more than one subject not expressed in the title. The court disagreed, indicating first that the statute had previously been ruled as not constitutionally vague and that, with respect to the due process claim, the statute was valid in all respects. The double jeopardy claim was without merit because defendant did not show that he had been prosecuted previously for the same offense or convicted or acquitted of any offense arising out of the same conduct. Because the fraudulent issuance of checks within a six-month period could be considered as a single offense in pursuit of a certain course of conduct, defendant was not entitled a separate jury trial as to each check. Clearly, the title of the statute did not embrace more than one subject.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order overruling defendant's motion to quash the information.

 

576 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Gill v. Gill


No. 40,464


Supreme Court of Minnesota


277 Minn. 166; 152 N.W.2d 309; 1967 Minn. LEXIS 923



June 30, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by plaintiff, Mary A. Gill, from a judgment entered in a divorce action in the Hennepin County District Court, Lindsay G. Arthur, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed except in so far as judgment provides that court did not have jurisdiction over defendant, Raymond S. Gill, to award support and alimony.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife appealed from a judgment in the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted the wife's request for a divorce but reserved awarding support and alimony on the ground that it did not have personal jurisdiction over defendant husband because he had been served by publication.


OVERVIEW: The wife was unable to serve the husband despite the fact that he was living in the state. Agreeing that the husband was secreting himself within the state to avoid personal service, the trial court granted an order for publication. The husband did not appear personally or through an attorney. The trial court granted the wife an absolute divorce, but reserved awarding support and alimony until such time as the trial court had personal jurisdiction over the husband. Reversing as to the reservation of awarding support and alimony, the court held that the trial court had personal jurisdiction over the husband under Minn. R. Civ. P. 4.04, which empowered courts to exercise personal jurisdiction by service through publication over residents that conceal themselves within the state for the purpose of avoiding personal service.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed except in so far as the order provided that the trial court reserved support and alimony, which holding was reversed. The court remanded to order support and alimony pursuant to the jurisdiction acquired on service of publication and to render a personal judgment therefor.

State v. Paulick


No. 40,600


Supreme Court of Minnesota


277 Minn. 140; 151 N.W.2d 591; 1967 Minn. LEXIS 919



June 23, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to this court by James Albert Paulick for a writ of prohibition to compel the Hennepin County Municipal Court, Bruce C. Stone, Judge, to desist from further proceedings in the prosecution of relator on a charge of careless driving.



DISPOSITION: Temporary restraining order made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of prohibition to compel a Hennepin County Municipal Court judge to desist from further proceedings in the prosecution of defendant on a charge of careless driving.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with operating his automobile in a careless manner. The original complaint was signed and verified by a police officer before a deputy clerk of the municipal court, on the basis of which a warrant for defendant's arrest was issued. Defendant made a special appearance in municipal court to challenge the court's jurisdiction on the ground that the complaint and warrant were unconstitutionally executed because they should have been executed before a magistrate not the clerk of court. Defendant then filed a petition for a writ of prohibition that alleged that the municipal court did not have jurisdiction over defendant and he sought to enjoin the prosecution of the traffic violation. The lower court issued a temporary restraining order. The court made the temporary restraining order absolute. The court held that the function of determining whether the complaint and warrant met constitutional standard were functions that the judiciary could not delegate to the clerk of court.
