578 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Beatty v. Winona Housing & Redevelopment Authority


No. 40,259


Supreme Court of Minnesota


277 Minn. 76; 151 N.W.2d 584; 1967 Minn. LEXIS 908



June 9, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Winona County District Court for a declaratory judgment invalidating resolutions of the council of the city of Winona creating the Winona Housing and Redevelopment Authority and other proceedings in connection with urban renewal and redevelopment in said city. The court, Arnold Hatfield, Judge, granted a motion by defendants, who include the Authority, the city, and numerous individuals, to dismiss the action, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney and real estate owner appealed from the judgment of the Winona County District Court (Minnesota), which granted a motion to dismiss his declaratory judgment action filed by defendants, the City of Winona, the Housing and Redevelopment Authority of Winona, and numerous individuals.


OVERVIEW: The attorney practiced law in the City and was also an owner of real estate in the downtown. He brought an action that sought to challenge the constitutionality of the Municipal Housing and Redevelopment Act, Minn. Stat. § 462.411, et seq., and of the Housing Act of 1949, as amended, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1441, et seq. He alleged that various acts of the city council and the Authority pertaining to urban renewal were illegal. The Authority obtained funds from the federal program and entered into two contracts, one with a firm of city planning consultants to prepare the plan and another with a firm engaged to do a marketability study of the area. When the attorney commenced his action, the plan had not been submitted to the Authority. The trial court granted the motions to dismiss, and the attorney appealed. The court affirmed the judgment. Defendants claimed that the appeal was untimely, but the court applied the rule that a plaintiff could move for a dismissal and then appeal from the judgment. The attorney failed to show that he was injured or that injury was imminent. No plan had been adopted, and no justiciable controversy existed between the parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal.

 

579 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Twin City Candy & Tobacco Co. v. A. Weisman Co.


Nos. 40,287, 40,188


Supreme Court of Minnesota


276 Minn. 225; 149 N.W.2d 698; 1967 Minn. LEXIS 1008; 1967 Trade Cas. (CCH) P72,043



March 20, 1967 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two separate actions in the Hennepin County District Court by Twin City Candy and Tobacco Company, Inc., and Minnesota Candy & Tobacco Distributors Association to enjoin defendant from selling cigarettes below the legal cost in violation of the Unfair Cigarette Sales Act. In the first action, the court, Stanley D. Kane, Judge, granted defendant's motion for summary judgment and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered; in the other, the court, William D. Gunn, Judge, granted defendant's motion to dismiss and plaintiff appealed from said order. The appeals were consolidated.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, plaintiffs, a trade association and a tobacco company, appealed the decisions of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted defendant tobacco distributor's motion for summary judgment and held the Minnesota Unfair Cigarette Sales Act to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Two actions were consolidated on appeal. The first action was brought in the trial court by plaintiff, a nonprofit trade association, which sought to enjoin defendant from violating the Minnesota Unfair Cigarette Sales Act (Cigarette Act). The second action was brought by a different plaintiff, a tobacco company, who sought to obtain an injunction and damages against defendant based on defendant's practice of selling cigarettes far below the actual invoice cost. The trial court dismissed both actions on the basis that the Cigarette Act was unconstitutional, therefore defendant could not be sued by either party for violating it. The appellate court upheld the decision of the trial court and ruled that the Cigarette Act was vague and indefinite and therefore served to deny due process of law.


OUTCOME: Plaintiffs' appeal was denied and the court affirmed the grant of defendant's motion for summary judgment.

 

580 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minneapolis Federation of Teachers v. Obermeyer


Nos. 40,477, 40,478


Supreme Court of Minnesota


275 Minn. 347; 147 N.W.2d 358; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 766; 64 L.R.R.M. 2118



December 9, 1966 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certified to U.S. Supreme Court March 13, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two actions in the Hennepin County District Court to determine the constitutionality of a legislative classification, one brought by Minneapolis Federation of Teachers, Local 59, AFL-CIO, against Peter Obermeyer, State Labor Conciliator, Board of Education of Special School District No. 1, Minneapolis, and City of Minneapolis Education Association; and one brought by said board of education against both the union and the association. The court, Eugene Minenko, Judge, ordered summary judgment declaring the statute unconstitutional, and said association appealed from the judgments entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal of two cases, appellant teachers' association sought review of a decision from Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment to respondent teachers' union and held that 1965 Minn. Law ch. 839, § 7, Minn. Stat. 179.572, which excepted teachers from the application of the rest of chapter 839, was unconstitutional and severable.


OVERVIEW: The parties were rival groups of public school teachers. In reviewing the legislation, the court held that § 7 was a constitutional classification and that the clear legislative intent was that the teachers were not to be included in the provisions of ch. 839, as other measures had been proposed and vetoed. As such, the court could not extend its scope beyond the limits of the law's provisions. The court found that ch. 839 covered the whole subject matter of public employees' labor relations and that the act repealed all of the prior laws. Even in the absence of a statute, the employees had no right to strike. Nor did the repeal of the statute, affirming the right to join labor unions, prohibit membership in a union or association organized to promote the teachers' mutual interest. While there was no implied or express power for the school board to conduct an election or to bargain with elected representatives of teacher organizations, there was nothing to prevent the board from meeting with or discussing wages with groups of employees. The court found nothing to prevent collective bargaining if it was entered into voluntarily.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision which held that new legislation to be unconstitutional. It found that the law did not apply to teachers but did not prevent them from entering in organizational groups or in reaching voluntary collective bargaining.

 

581 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Port Authority of St. Paul v. Fisher


No. 40,268


Supreme Court of Minnesota


275 Minn. 157; 145 N.W.2d 560; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 740



October 7, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court for a declaratory judgment brought by the Port Authority of the City of St. Paul, its commissioners, and the American Hoist & Derrick Company against Fred W. Fisher, as commissioner and president of the Authority, to determine the validity of a contract between said Authority and said company and of the bonds to be issued pursuant thereto. After findings for plaintiffs, Harold W. Schultz, Judge, defendant appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, president of the port authority, appealed a judgment of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) for plaintiff port authority in an action seeking judicial approval of an industrial development project. The president contended that the project's financing was invalid under Minn. Stat. ch. 458 and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The port authority sought to finance an industrial development project through revenue bonds and through leasing the building to a private corporation. The reclaimed land for the development was "marginal" land under Minn. Stat. § 458.191(4). Although the land had already been readied for industrial use, the president refused to sign the lease. The court affirmed the judgment because it found that a sale by the port authority to private interests was not economically feasible given the acquisition costs and the sales price that could be obtained. The evidence demonstrated that industrial use would benefit the public by creating jobs. In addition, if the port authority did not recoup its acquisition costs, the city's taxpayers would suffer. Consequently, the port authority had not acted arbitrarily in seeking to recoup its acquisition costs. There was no evidence that public funds were diverted. It was incidental that the private corporation also benefitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the port authority.

 

582 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minneapolis Federation of Teachers v. Obermeyer


Nos. 40,477, 40,478


Supreme Court of Minnesota


275 Minn. 46; 144 N.W.2d 789; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 727; 63 L.R.R.M. 2001; 54 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P51,537



August 22, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two actions in the Hennepin County District Court, each for a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of a statute. One action was brought by the Minneapolis Federation of Teachers, Local 59, AFL-CIO, and Peter Obermeyer, state labor conciliator; Board of Education of Special School District No. 1; and the City of Minneapolis Education Association were named as defendants. The other action was brought by the Board of Education of Special School District No. 1 against said federation and association for similar relief. The cases were heard together and after findings declaring said statute to be unconstitutional, Eugene Minenko, Judge, said association appealed from the judgments entered. Pending said appeal, the supreme court, upon motion of said association, stayed proceedings before the labor conciliator pursuant to the judgments.



DISPOSITION: Stay of proceedings extended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant education association, sought review of a decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which, in two consolidated actions, one brought by a teacher's union and the state labor conciliator against a board of education and the other brought by the board of education against the union and the education association, declared that a statute was unconstitutional and temporarily stayed proceedings before the labor conciliator.


OVERVIEW: The subject matter of the two consolidated actions was the state labor conciliator's right to conduct hearings for the purpose of establishing whether the union or the association was the appropriate bargaining unit to represent teachers in their negotiations with the school board. After the district court ordered a temporary stay of proceedings to be held before the labor conciliator, the association appealed. The court issued an order extending the stay of proceedings. The court noted that Minn. Stat. § 179.572, which the district court had held to be unconstitutional, provided that Minn. Stat. § 179.52 did not apply to public school teachers. The court noted that if the conciliator was permitted to proceed with his investigation and election, members of the union and the association could be needlessly and futilely distracted from their professional responsibilities in an expensive and time-consuming competition. The court stated that it had advanced the case on the calendar in order to render a prompt decision and that the potential harm which could result from revoking the stay far outweighed that which was likely if the stay was extended until a decision on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court extended the stay of proceedings until a decision on the merits of the two consolidated cases could be rendered.

 

583 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Northern States Power Co. v. Esperson


No. 39,942


Supreme Court of Minnesota


274 Minn. 451; 144 N.W.2d 372; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 931



July 22, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Condemnation proceeding in the Washington County District Court for an easement across certain property for power lines wherein Northern States Power Company appealed from the commissioners' award. The case was tried before Robert B. Gillespie, Judge, and a jury, which awarded damages of $ 3,600 to Margaret Sliney Minser, Mary A. Sliney, Geraldine Sliney, and Rose T. Sliney. They appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and new trial granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of an order from the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which denied their motion for a new trial filed after a jury awarded them damages of $ 3,600 in a condemnation action brought by respondent, a public utility, to acquire easements and rights of way across the owners' property.


OVERVIEW: The commissioners had awarded the owners $ 12,000, and the utility had appealed to the district court. On appeal, the owners claimed that the trial court had erred in ruling that the commissioner could not testify as their witness as to the amount of the commissioners' award and that he had acted as a commissioner. The utility claimed that the trial court correctly determined that Minn. Stat. § 117.20, subd. 8(c), which provided that, in a condemnation case, the commissioner could be called by any party as a witness to testify as to the amount of the award of the commissioners, applied only to actions brought by the state or a political subdivision, and did not apply to actions brought by public utilities. The court agreed with the owners, reversed the trial court's judgment, and granted a new trial. There was no basis in public policy for separating cases in which the state or a political subdivision was the condemnor from those proceedings in which others were condemnors. To construe § 117.20, subd. 8(c) as applying only to proceedings in which the state or a political subdivision was the condemnor denied other condemnors equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and a new trial was granted.

 

584 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Geiselhart v. Tahash


No. 40,139


Supreme Court of Minnesota


274 Minn. 464; 144 N.W.2d 354; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 933



July 22, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Gerald Geiselhart from an order of the Washington County District Court, Leonard Keyes, Judge, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order of the Washington County District Court, Minnesota, which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate was convicted willfully, wrongfully, unlawfully, and feloniously deserting and failing to care for and support his children under Minn. Stat. § 617.55 (1961).


OVERVIEW: Because he had two prior felony convictions, the inmate was sentenced to a term of imprisonment not exceeding 10 years. The sentence was suspended but subsequently the inmate's parole was revoked. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate contended that the desertion statute was unconstitutional because intent was presumed after a desertion of three months, he was denied due process because he was not afforded counsel prior to waiving a preliminary hearing, and he was not accorded a right of allocution. The court ruled that although the presumption was invalid, it did not render the statute unconstitutional. The court noted that the inmate pled guilty and the information expressly alleged intent. The court also ruled that, in view of his guilty plea, the inmate's waiver of a preliminary hearing did not prejudice him. The court also noted that the inmate was provided an opportunity to speak before his sentence was imposed and that the trial court had suspended his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied the inmate's petition for the writ.

Merz v. Oftedal


No. 40,165


Supreme Court of Minnesota


274 Minn. 401; 144 N.W.2d 58; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 924



July 8, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court by Betty L. Merz, special administratrix of the estate of Ralph L. Bloom, deceased, to recover from Maxwell L. Oftedal and Oftedal, Locke & Broadston, a Minnesota corporation, amounts allegedly due said decedent for services, in which action defendants counterclaimed. After findings determining the amount due plaintiff, William D. Gunn, Judge, plaintiff appealed from orders for judgment.



DISPOSITION: Upon motion of respondents, appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, administratrix of the decedent's estate, appealed from a decision of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which determined that certain amounts were owed to the administratrix in the administratrix's action against defendants, a corporation and a partner, allegedly due the decedent for services rendered.


OVERVIEW: The administratrix brought the action on behalf of the decedent's estate against the corporation for $ 25,000 and an accounting of a partnership. Judgment was entered for the administratrix in May 1965. The findings were amended in November. Later that month, the administratrix served on the corporation two notices of appeal from the orders in May and November 1965. The administratrix claimed that the court could review the case under Minn. Stat. § 605.09(d), (h). The court held that the orders were not appealable. Orders in trust matters, receiverships, and other special proceedings were final and appealable. The administratrix's action was an ordinary common-law action for a partnership accounting in which the administratrix also sought a money judgment. The fact that one of the defendants at one time petitioned the court for the appointment of a receiver in a wholly separate proceeding did not change things. The court concluded that it was not disposed to overrule a long line of cases holding nonappealable orders denying motions for amended findings.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

586 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Halverson v. Rolvaag


No. 40,396


Supreme Court of Minnesota


274 Minn. 273; 143 N.W.2d 239; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 902



June 3, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court on behalf of Rachelle Bauer Halverson, a minor, by her mother and natural guardian, Genevra Bauer Halverson, and by the mother on her own behalf against Karl Rolvaag, governor of Minnesota, and Chester Moeglein, adjutant general, for benefits allegedly due by reason of the death of Lieutenant Gene C. Bauer. The court, Robert V. Rensch, Judge, granted summary judgment on the claim of the minor plaintiff, and defendants appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Governor of Minnesota and the adjutant general, appealed from a decision of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted summary judgment for plaintiff minor in the minor's claim for benefits after her father, a member of the Minnesota National Guard, died.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's wife filed an action for herself and on behalf of the minor to recover compensation under Minn. Stat. §§ 192.38 and 192.39 (1961), for the death of their husband and father who died as the result of an accident which occurred while he was engaged in active duty as a member of the Minnesota National Guard. Defendants pleaded the statute of limitations and alleged that the claims were subject to reduction under 1963 Minn. Laws ch. 854. The court rejected the trial court's conclusion and held that 1963 Minn. Laws ch. 854 could be applied to claims based upon deaths occurring before its enactment even though no formal claim had been filed until after enactment. There was no showing that the decedent was induced by the existence of benefits under Minn. Stat. §§ 192.38 and 192.39 to enter membership in the National Guard. Principles of justice and equity were not violated because the only effect of the application of 1963 Minn. Laws ch. 854 was to prevent double recovery. The distinction that 1963 Minn. Laws ch. 854 made between pending claims and claims not pending was not unreasonable, arbitrary, or discriminatory and therefore did not violate equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

 

587 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Olson


No. 40,301


Supreme Court of Minnesota


274 Minn. 225; 143 N.W.2d 69; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 897



May 31, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Prohibition in this court upon the relation of Anton Olson, charged with murder in the first degree, to compel the Ramsey County District Court, David E. Marsden, Judge; Gerard Snell, Solicitor General; and Dr. Philip Artz, court-appointed psychiatrist, to refrain from further proceedings requiring relator to submit to a psychiatric examination.



DISPOSITION: Writ made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator accused sought a writ of prohibition to restrain respondents, the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota) and a court-appointed psychiatrist, from compelling the accused to submit to a court-ordered psychiatric examination to determine if the accused was legally sane at the time two murders were committed.


OVERVIEW: The accused was charged with two counts of first degree murder under Minn. Stat. § 609.185, and he indicated that his defense would be temporary insanity when the crimes were committed. The trial court granted the State's motion for an order compelling the accused to submit to an examination by a court-appointed psychiatrist to determine if he were insane at that time. The accused filed a petition for a writ of prohibition. The court granted the writ and held that although Minn. Stat. §§ 610 and 631.18 prohibited the trial of the accused if he were found to be insane and provided for his commitment if he were insane, no Minnesota statute authorized the trial court to compel him to submit to a psychiatric examination to determine if the accused was insane when the crime was committed. If the State had access to the accused's interviews with the psychiatrist, the interviews would violate the accused's privilege against self-incrimination in U.S. Const. amend. V and Minn. Const. art. I, § 7. Therefore, the trial court lacked authority to order the psychiatric examination.


OUTCOME: The court issued the writ of prohibition and made it absolute.

 

588 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hanlon v. Towey


Nos. 40,084, 40,203


Supreme Court of Minnesota


274 Minn. 187; 142 N.W.2d 741; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 890



May 20, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment brought in the Olmsted County District Court by David G. Hanlon, Rex H. Gregor, and William H. Coats, residents, freeholders, and taxpayers of said county and of the city of Rochester, attacking a proposed redistricting by the county board of said county. The individual county commissioners, its auditor, and the county itself were named as defendants. After findings for plaintiffs, O. Russell Olson, Judge, defendants Lawrence W. Schulz, Erwin Brennan, and Clyde Hoffman appealed from an order denying their motion for a new trial and from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent county residents filed an action in the Olmstead County District Court (Minnesota) attacking a proposed redistricting by the county board of the county and seeking a declaration that the redistricting violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and Minn. Const. art. I, § 2. The trial court found in favor of the residents. Appellants, county commissioners, a county auditor, and a county, sought review.


OVERVIEW: Minn. Stat. § 375.02 required that each county in Minnesota have been divided into districts of an equal population, and that no city of a particular size could have been in more than two commissioner districts. The county proposed to redistrict the county such that a city, in which the residents lived, would have been limited to only two commissioners, as required by § 375.02. The residents filed an action protesting the redistricting, asserting that its population was 62 percent of the total population of the county. By allowing the three other districts, which collectively only constituted 38 percent of the county population, to have equal voting power, the residents' votes were significantly diluted. The trial court agreed, holding that § 375.02 violated the state and federal constitutions because it did not respect the requirement of "one man, one vote" found in the Equal Protection Clause. On appeal, appellants contended that the Fourteenth Amendment did not apply to the apportionment of county commissioner districts. The court held that it did apply. The equal-population principle of the Equal Protection Clause applied to the legislative apportionment of county government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment entered in favor of the county residents.

 

589 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Campbell v. Glenwood Hills Hospitals, Inc.


No. 39,949


Supreme Court of Minnesota


273 Minn. 525; 142 N.W.2d 255; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 858



April 15, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court against Glenwood Hills Hospitals, Incorporated, and Raymond T. Rascop, superintendent of said hospital, for damages allegedly sustained by plaintiff as a result of his involuntary hospitalization. The court, Donald T. Barbeau, Judge, granted defendants' motion for dismissal, and plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff involuntary patient appealed a judgment from the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which granted the motion of defendants, a hospital and its superintendent, to dismiss the patient's suit for false imprisonment, assault and battery, and violations of his federal constitutional due process rights as a result of his commitment under Minn. Stat. § 525.751.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Minn. Stat. § 525.751, a probate court authorized a patient's involuntary commitment to a hospital without a hearing. The probate court appointed counsel for the patient and held a hearing a week later. Defendant's commitment was extended for six months during which period two more hearings were held. Defendant filed a tort action against the hospital and its superintendent in state court and also filed a civil rights action against them in federal court. After the federal court dismissed the federal suit, the state court granted defendants' motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court affirmed and held as follows: The dismissal of the federal claims in federal court was res judicata for the federal claims in state court. Because the probate court, not defendants, had the duty to provide the patient with an attorney and hearings, they could not deprive the patient of his due process rights. Because defendants complied with the probate court's order, they were immune from the patient's tort suit. Because the patient did not serve notice of the appeal on the Minnesota Attorney General, the court had no jurisdiction to review the claim that § 525.751 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

590 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mathiasen


No. 39,800


Supreme Court of Minnesota


273 Minn. 372; 141 N.W.2d 805; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 837



March 25, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by James A. Mathiasen from a judgment of the Stearns County District Court, Charles W. Kennedy, Judge, whereby he was convicted of theft.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of conviction of the Stearns County District Court (Minnesota), which was based on defendant's plea of guilty to an information charging him with the violation of Minn. St. § 609.52, subd. 2(3)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant urged that the statute under which he was convicted, Minn. Stat. § 609.15, subd. 3, was unconstitutional and that he was inadequately represented by counsel in the district court proceedings. The court held that § 609.52, subd. 3 and the proceedings thereunder were valid. By its enactment of this statute the legislature had declared that a person cashing a series of checks, aggregating in excess of $ 100 within a 6-month period, without sufficient funds on deposit to cover them respectively, was guilty of a felony. In so doing it exercised its unquestioned authority to declare which acts or what course of conduct should be deemed inimical to the public welfare. The court held that it was within the province of the legislature to declare that certain acts could constitute or be parts of different offenses, and to determine that the same acts might be offenses under different statutes. If it could be determined with reasonable certainty what conduct was subject to legislative disapproval, the statute defining the prohibited conduct would not be held unconstitutional on the ground of indefiniteness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

591 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Minnetonka Electric Co. v. Golden Valley


No. 39,837


Supreme Court of Minnesota


273 Minn. 301; 141 N.W.2d 138; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 830



March 11, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court to enjoin defendant village from requiring plaintiff to have an electrical contractor's license. After findings for defendant, Dana Nicholson, Judge, plaintiff appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor appealed an order of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which entered a judgment in favor of defendant village in the contractor's action to enjoin the village from requiring the contractor to have an electrical contractor's license from the village.


OVERVIEW: The contractor operated its business under a master electrician's license issued by the state to its president. In 1962, the village refused to issue electrical construction permits to the contractor because the contractor had not obtained a village license. The village, through its agents and employees, physically expelled the contractor's employees from an electrical job which it had undertaken in the village. The contractor then secured the license and initiated the instant action. The trial court held that the village had the power to license electrical contractors; that the State had not preempted the field; and that there was no valid constitutional objection to such licensing. The contractor appealed, and the court reversed and held the contractor was entitled to a granting of its motion for amendment of findings and conclusions of law in the trial court. The court held that the village municipality had no power to license electricians under Minn. Stat. § 412.221, subds. 17, 28, and 32, or Minn. Stat. § 326.31, subd. 4, or Minn. Stat. § 326.32 because the village's power to license was not an integral or necessary part of the village's power to regulate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the village.

 

592 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Ahern v. Young


No. 40,105


Supreme Court of Minnesota


273 Minn. 240; 141 N.W.2d 15; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 818



February 25, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Michael Patrick Ahern from an order of the Sherburne County District Court, Robert B. Gillespie, Judge, discharging a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner sought review of an order from the Sherburne County District Court (Minnesota), which discharged a writ of habeas corpus filed in response to the State revoking his probation and ordering him to jail to serve out his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Following his plea of guilty to forgery, petitioner was sentenced for a term not to exceed 3 years. On that date the court entered an order staying the execution of the sentence and placing petitioner on probation on certain conditions. Petitioner continued on probation for almost one and one-half years, when, pursuant to Minn. Stat. §609.14, the stay and probation were revoked after hearing and petitioner ordered committed to serve the sentence previously imposed. At issue was whether petitioner was entitled to credit toward the expiration of his sentence for time spent on probation. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal, holding that the court was able to vacate the stay and reinstate the sentence at any time. The court held further that the legislature had determined what sentence to impose and that they treated persons on parole and those on probation differently, which did not discriminate against them in such a way as to violate equal protection. The court held that the trial court had to be able to uphold the threat of imposing the sentence to encourage people not to violate probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of petitioner's writ of habeas corpus.

 

593 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schmit


No. 39,079


Supreme Court of Minnesota


273 Minn. 78; 139 N.W.2d 800; 1966 Minn. LEXIS 795



January 21, 1966 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Defendant was convicted of indecent assault in the Ramsey County District Court, and he appealed from an order, Robert V. Rensch, Judge, denying his alternative motion for judgment of acquittal notwithstanding the verdict or for a new trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and new trial granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Ramsey County (Minnesota), which convicted him of indecent assault. Defendant was charged by information with the crime of sodomy in violation of Minn. Stat. § 617.14, but indecent assault was submitted to the jury as a lesser included offense over defendant's objection. Defendant appealed from an order denying his motion for judgment of acquittal or in the alternative a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court denied him the fundamental right to a public trial by excluding spectators because of the nature of the crime and the anticipated testimony. The court held that the constitutional mandate for a public trial was an assurance to the accused that he would be dealt with justly and protected not only against gross abuses of judicial power but also against petty arbitrariness. The order of the trial court that excluded everyone from the trial, except members of the bar and press, solely upon the ground of the obscene nature of the crime and anticipated testimony, exceeded the power of the court to limit attendance and violated defendant's constitutional right to a public trial. The court further held that while the evidence clearly supported defendant's conviction of the crime of indecent assault, that offense was not a lesser and included offense of the crime with which defendant was charged, sodomy. To submit a lesser and included offense, the State must show that the offense charged could not have been committed without necessarily committing the lesser and included offense. It was not essential in proving sodomy to prove an assault.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and granted a new trial.

 

594 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Rasmussen v. Tahash


No. 39,847


Supreme Court of Minnesota


272 Minn. 539; 141 N.W.2d 3; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 686



December 10, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Melford Rasmussen from an order of the Washington County District Court, Leonard Keyes, Judge, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that a statement elicited was in violation of his constitutional right to counsel as defined in Escobedo and that the voluntariness of his confession was not tested and resolved by the trial court. The court held that prospective application of the Escobedo decision was the better course to follow unless the U.S. Supreme Court decided otherwise. While it was good procedure of the police to advise an arrested person immediately of his rights, the failure to give that advice would not of itself have made a subsequent confession inadmissible, but the absence of such warnings would have been a significant factor in testing whether the confession was given freely. Therefore, the court affirmed the decision because: (1) the conviction of petitioner was final before Escobedo; (2) the record failed to show any affirmative action on the part of law enforcement authorities, denying petitioner the services of retained counsel; (3) a U.S. Supreme Court case holding that there should be a separate determination of voluntariness applied prospectively as well; (4) there was no adequate objection during trial based upon the constitutional grounds asserted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

595 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Flores v. Tahash


No. 39,431


Supreme Court of Minnesota


272 Minn. 451; 138 N.W.2d 626; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 673



December 3, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by James A. Flores from an order of the Washington County District Court, William T. Johnson, Judge, discharging a writ of habeas corpus.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate sought review of an order of the Washington County District Court (Minnesota), which discharged his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate was convicted of the unlawful possession of empirin compound with codeine phosphate and contended that the classification in Minn. Stat. § 618.01 was unreasonable and violated equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: The inmate admitted that he possessed at least 85 bottles containing a variety of narcotic drugs. The inmate asserted that the classification of the codeine he possessed as unlawful was unreasonable and violated his equal protection rights. The inmate's expert witness testified that the tablets of empirin contained less codeine than a teaspoon of cough syrup. The trial court denied the inmate's petition for habeas corpus relief. The court agreed that the classification in the statute making the possession of empirin unlawful, but not cough syrup, was reasonable where the liquid cough syrup was more difficult to conceal than tablets, the cost of cough syrup would be prohibitive if available only by prescription, and the benefit and convenience to the public in securing cough syrup over the counter outweighed the potential dangers inherent in permitting its purchase without a prescription.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied the inmate's petition for habeas corpus relief.

 

596 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Duxbury v. Donovan


No. 40,051


Supreme Court of Minnesota


272 Minn. 424; 138 N.W.2d 692; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 671



November 26, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Ramsey County District Court brought by L. L. Duxbury, Jr., Robert C. Kucera, Aubrey W. Dirlam, Salisbury Adams, Richard W. Fitzsimons, Harold J. Anderson, George A. French, Walter K. Klaus, and Carl M. Iverson, residents and voters of the State of Minnesota and members of the house of representatives, to compel Joseph L. Donovan, secretary of state, and H. Y. Torrey, secretary of the senate, to put into effect a bill passed by the 1965 legislature prescribing the bounds of the senatorial and representative districts and apportioning anew the senators and representatives among the several districts. The court, John W. Graff, Judge, granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, and defendants appealed from the judgment entered.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, secretary of state and secretary of the senate, sought review of a judgment by the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which granted plaintiff residents' motion for summary judgment in their action seeking a judicial determination that Senate File 102 became complete and effective upon final passage of it by the senate and house of representatives and that the governor was without power to veto it.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was whether the Minnesota legislature, consisting of the senate and the house of representatives, had sole and exclusive power under the Minnesota Constitution to redistrict and reapportion. On appeal, the court answered the question in the negative and reversed the grant of summary judgment to the residents. The court held that the language used by the framers of the Minnesota Constitution in dealing with the problem of apportionment gave the governor the power to require a two-thirds majority of both houses in order to give to apportionment legislation the effect of law. The court reasoned that to say that the governor had the power to veto laws passed by the legislature was not to say that he had the power to compel a concurrence of two-thirds of the membership of both houses in all instances where the legislature exercised authority granted it by the Constitution. However, the court opined that deciding that the executive power to assert a qualified veto was put in the Constitution as a check upon the power of the legislature to redistrict and apportion did not imply that the use of the veto in this particular case was or was not prudent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the residents on their action to compel defendants to put the senate file into effect.

 

597 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Hosking v. Metropolitan House Movers Corp.


No. 39,848


Supreme Court of Minnesota


272 Minn. 390; 138 N.W.2d 404; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 667



November 5, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari upon the relation of Metropolitan House Movers Corporation, employer, to review a decision of the Industrial Commission awarding benefits to Dorothy Hosking, employee, against said relator.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator employer sought certiorari for review of a decision of the Industrial Commission (Minnesota), which awarded benefits to respondent employee against the employer for injuries sustained in a collapse of the secretarial chair on which she was sitting while working for the employer.


OVERVIEW: The record indicated that the steel posts in the back of the employee's chair hit the floor and, as a result, struck the employee in the back, injuring her. On the day following the accident the employee was admitted to the hospital where she remained for 2 days. The employee initiated an action to recover benefits from the employer and its insurer. The Commission awarded benefits, and the employer and insurer appealed. The court affirmed and held that the appeal presented nothing but fact questions. The court held that the Commission's findings of fact were not manifestly contrary to the evidence, nor did a consideration of all the evidence and the inferences permissible therefrom require reasonable minds to adopt a contrary conclusion. The court held that the evidence amply sustained the Commission's finding of causal relationship between the injuries and the employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award to the employee.

 

598 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Casperson v. Board of Regents


Nos. 39,420, 39,502


Supreme Court of Minnesota


272 Minn. 210; 137 N.W.2d 194; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 652



September 3, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in the Hennepin County District Court brought by Morris E. Casperson and Fifth District American Legion All-Star Corporation to enjoin the Board of Regents of the University of Minnesota and the National Collegiate Athletic Association from enforcing certain policies of said association. Plaintiffs appealed from two orders, Irving R. Brand, Judge, quashing and setting aside service of process upon defendant association.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a taxpayer and a nonprofit corporation, contested the orders by which the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota) quashed appellants' service of process upon respondents, university regents and the National Collegiate Athletic Association (NCAA).


OVERVIEW: The NCAA constitution, to which the university regents subscribed, forbade high school football all-star games that lacked official sanction from a responsible governing body. After the NCAA refused to sanction the nonprofit corporation's high school football all-star game, appellants filed suit, seeking a declaration that the subject clause was unconstitutional. After the trial court quashed appellants' service, appellants sought review and prevailed. Minn. Stat. § 540.152 provided that an out-of-state association's transaction of acts or activities within the state was deemed an appointment of the secretary of state for service of process. Section 540.152 did not require the existence of an agency relationship between the university and the NCAA, although jurisdiction could be based thereon. Instead, jurisdiction would lie if the university was an NCAA member and had some part in any transaction, act, or activity on behalf of the NCAA out of which the action arose. To that end, the court reviewed the history of respondents' combined activities within the state and concluded that the NCAA had sufficient minimum contacts with the state to subject it to suit there.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders.

 

599 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Leary


No. 39,690


Supreme Court of Minnesota


272 Minn. 34; 136 N.W.2d 552; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 631



July 23, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by Lois M. Leary, by Harlan Smith, special guardian of her estate, from a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court, Thomas Tallakson, Judge, whereby she was adjudged mentally ill and committed to the custody of the superintendent of the State Hospital at St. Peter upon appeal from a like judgment by the probate court of said county in proceedings upon the petition of Odessa Walker.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a patient, sought review of a judgment of the Hennepin County District Court (Minnesota), which adjudged her as mentally ill and committed her to the custody of the superintendent of a state hospital after her appeal from a judgment of a probate court on the petition of appellee, a petitioner. The petitioner filed a motion to dismiss the patient's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The petition sought the patient's commitment to the state hospital and was prepared based on papers contained in a probate court file that originated in earlier commitment proceedings. The petition was signed at the request of a member of the city fire department after a fire was started in the petitioner's home. After the patient was found mentally ill and needed hospital treatment, an appeal was perfected to the district court. Following a hearing, the district court wrote to the director of the hospital and solicited advice as to the patient's progress since her confinement. The court held that: (1) the district court did not acquire original jurisdiction because although the appeal was tried de novo, original jurisdiction was with the probate court; (2) appointment of a guardian ad litem was not a prerequisite to the jurisdiction of the district court where the patient was adequately represented by counsel; and (3) it was not proper for the district court to have consulted with the superintendent in the absence of the patient or her counsel because she had a right to cross-examine the doctor on any information that might have influenced the district court's determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

600 of 1634 DOCUMENTS


Sparton Industries, Inc. v. Starkey


No. 39,307


Supreme Court of Minnesota


271 Minn. 496; 136 N.W.2d 595; 1965 Minn. LEXIS 752



July 9, 1965 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari in the Ramsey County District Court wherein the court, Leonard J. Keyes, Judge, reversed a decision of the commissioner of employment security determining that respondents Spartan of Bloomington, Inc., and Spartan of West St. Paul, Inc., were required to contribute to the Minnesota unemployment fund on the basis of wages paid during 1961 and further held that respondent Spartan of Lexington, Inc., was also not required to so contribute for said year. The commissioner appealed from the court's order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the commissioner of employment security (commissioner), brought an action for review of the Ramsey County District Court (Minnesota), which reversed a decision of the commissioner determining that respondent employers were required to contribute to the Minnesota unemployment fund on the basis of wages paid during 1961.


OVERVIEW: The employers were three corporations that were subsidiaries of a New York parent corporation. Each of the employers was organized in Minnesota in 1961 and employed salaried employees for less than 20 weeks in 1961. Five officers of the parent owned the stock in the employers. The commissioner determined the officers were employees who worked for more than 20 weeks during 1961 and therefore the entire entity of the parent and subsidiary employers could be considered a single employer in determining the liability of the employing units involved. The court concluded that the service of the officers could not be counted as "employment" within the meaning of Minn. Stat. § 268.04, subd. 10(1). The term "employment" as used in subd. 10(1) had to be given the meaning ascribed to it by subd. 12(2, 3). Thus, an employing unit was not within the definition of "employer" where the services performed, whether by officers of a corporation or employees, were all performed outside the state and were therefore not "localized" in the state. The services of the five officers of each subsidiary could not be considered as "employment" in Minnesota because they performed no services in Minnesota.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.
